1601 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Duncan v. Marcin


No. 78-1942


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


82 Ill. App. 3d 963; 403 N.E.2d 653; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2626; 38 Ill. Dec. 422



March 31, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 5, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. HARRY G. COMERFORD, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff liquor licensees appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting defendant city clerk's motion to strike and dismiss the licensees' complaint against the city clerk and defendant city board of election commissioners to contest the validity of a local option election in which the sale at retail of alcoholic liquor was prohibited in a precinct.


OVERVIEW: The city held a local option election under the Liquor Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 166-182 (1975). The retail sale of liquor was prohibited in a precinct. The licensees contested the election. The trial court dismissed their action. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding: (1) The statutory system did not violate the home rule provisions of the Illinois Constitution of 1970. The prohibition against sales of alcohol did not disrupt city planning as it affected only one use of the property. The right to engage in the retail sale of liquor was determined by an affirmative vote in the precinct and not according to the zoning ordinance. (2) The statutory system was not an improper delegation of legislative authority. (3) The differences in procedures for referendums based upon the population of communities did not render the statute invalid. Classification on the basis of the population of an area was proper. (4) The complaint did not set forth sufficient grounds to contest the results of the election. The licensees' allegations of voting irregularities were conclusions of fact. (5) A license to sell alcoholic beverages at retail was not subject to due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment dismissing the licensees' complaint.

 

1602 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Housby


No. 78-203


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


82 Ill. App. 3d 537; 403 N.E.2d 62; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2565; 38 Ill. Dec. 47



March 28, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of La Salle County; the Hon. LEONARD HOFFMAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of La Salle County (Illinois), which convicted him of theft of property having a value greater than $ 150 pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16-1(a)(1) (1977) and burglary and sentenced him to a term of imprisonment of seven years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of theft and burglary, and he appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and remanded the case to the trial court for a clarification of its intent in sentencing defendant. The court held that a jury instruction did not violate defendant's right to due process of law because the challenged instruction described a permissive presumption. The instruction informed the jury that if it found that defendant had exclusive possession of recently stolen property, and there was no reasonable explanation of his possession, it was permitted to infer that he obtained possession of the property by burglary. The court also found that jury was given instructions, which set out the elements of burglary and, which stated that the State had the burden of proving each element beyond a reasonable doubt. The permissive presumption did not shift the burden of persuasion. The court ruled that there was a rational connection between the proved facts and the presumed fact that defendant obtained the property by burglary. The court held that the trial court did not err by not informing defendant of the specific sentences that would be imposed under the sentencing laws.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for theft and burglary. The court remanded the case for the purpose of permitting the trial court to clarify its intention in sentencing defendant.

 

1603 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Baker


No. 79-435


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


82 Ill. App. 3d 590; 403 N.E.2d 46; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2574; 38 Ill. Dec. 31



March 26, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Montgomery County; the Hon. JOSEPH FRIBLEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to the unlawful possession of phenmetrazine, a Schedule III controlled substance, and the State agreed to dismiss a forgery charge. The Circuit Court of Montgomery County (Illinois) entered a judgment of conviction based upon the plea and denied defendant's subsequent motion to withdraw his plea of guilty and to vacate the judgment of conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that a prior decision rendered unconstitutional the entire Controlled Substances Act possession provision, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1402(b) (1977). The court, however, found that the prior decision was limited to those possession provisions that treated the possession of a controlled substance more severely than delivery of the same substance. In the present case, the possession and delivery of phenmetrazine were treated equally, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, paras. 1401(d), 1402(b). Thus, the enforcement of the possession provision was not unconstitutional. Further, the Act provided, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1602 (1977), that the invalidation of any provision did not render invalid other provisions of the Act. Because defendant was not placed in a worse position than a comparable person, he had no injury to base an equal protection claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction and sentence.

 

1604 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Perine


No. 78-2078


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


82 Ill. App. 3d 610; 402 N.E.2d 847; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2579; 37 Ill. Dec. 845



March 21, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ROMIE PALMER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of possession of 30 grams or more of a substance containing heroin, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1402(a) (1975).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of 30 grams or more of a substance containing heroin, and the court affirmed the conviction. The court found that the record proved in its entirety that the substance obtained from defendant was the same untampered substance that was later tested and found to be heroin. The court also found that the record contained no indication of any tampering with the substance or substitution between the packet taken from defendant and the one later analyzed by the chemist. The court noted that the only support for defendant's contention that two packets existed was the reversal of the last two digits in the six-digit inventory number referred to in the stipulation. However, the court found that the same stipulation stated that the substance tested by the chemist was the same substance recovered by the officer and stated that there was an unbroken chain of custody. The court held that the difference between the numbers was more likely the result of a typographical error. The court found that the Dangerous Drug Abuse Act was rationally designed to further a legitimate state purpose, to treat drug addicts that were more likely to be rehabilitated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of possession of 30 grams or more of a substance containing heroin.

 

1605 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Maffei


No. 79-197


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


82 Ill. App. 3d 111; 402 N.E.2d 398; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2506; 37 Ill. Dec. 508



March 18, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County; the Hon. DAVID DeDONCKER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois), which entered a judgment of conviction, after a bench trial, for possession of 1.5 grams of valium capsules, a controlled substance, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1402(b) (1977). The trial court imposed a two year sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended on appeal that § 402(b) of the Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1402(b) (1977), violated the equal protection clauses of the federal and state constitutions, U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. At the time of the conviction, possession of small amounts of the controlled substance was a Class 3 felony while delivery was a Class 4 felony. The court noted that other districts had found § 402(b) of the Act to be unconstitutional and agreed that the present conviction and sentence had to be reversed on equal protection grounds. Possession under § 402(b) was a lesser-included offense of delivery of the same substance under § 401(e) of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(e) (1977). Because the possession charge carried a higher penalty than delivery, the sentencing scheme was without rational justification, and, thus, § 402(b) of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1402(b), was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment of conviction and sentence.

 

1606 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Laws


No. 79-293


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


82 Ill. App. 3d 417; 402 N.E.2d 790; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2550; 37 Ill. Dec. 788



March 18, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. MARK E. JONES, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his motion to quash a search warrant and to suppress evidence and convicted him of possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Following a stipulated bench trial, defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance and sentenced to a term of five years' probation with one year periodic imprisonment. The trial court denied defendant's motion to quash and his motion to suppress. On appeal, defendant contended that his case had to be remanded to the trial court for a hearing on his pretrial motion. The court reversed and remanded, finding that the application of the exclusionary rules to those cases where the police had no reason to know that the accused should have been afforded counsel would have failed to serve the policies implicated in all three of the criteria for determining the retroactivity of a standard. The court found further that the doctrine governing when a hearing on a pretrial motion was required should have been applied retroactively. Because the trial court denied defendant's motion based not on its substance but on the face of the affidavit rule in existence at that time, the sufficiency of defendant's allegations was not examined.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's order, which denied defendant's motion to quash the search warrant and to suppress evidence and convicted him of possession of a controlled substance.

 

1607 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Aurora Nat'l Bank v. Aurora


No. 79-197


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


82 Ill. App. 3d 72; 402 N.E.2d 365; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2499; 37 Ill. Dec. 475



March 14, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. JOHN S. PAGE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which declared an amendment to the city's zoning ordinance was invalid as applied to property owned by plaintiffs, a bank and an individual.


OVERVIEW: The central issue was whether the city substantially complied with notice and other procedural requirements in adopting the amendatory ordinance. The individual attended the public hearing accompanied by counsel and testified in opposition to the down-zoning amendment, but did not at that time object to the sufficiency of the notice. The first issue the court considered was whether the amendatory ordinance was invalid because the notice requirements of the enabling act and city ordinance were not complied with. There was no requirement in state law that the notice contain a statement of the changes contemplated by the proposed amendment, nor was such a requirement imposed by the city ordinance. Thus, the notice issued was compliant. The next issue the court considered was whether the amendatory ordinance was invalid for failure to comply with several procedural requirements imposed by the city code for initiating and processing zoning amendments. The court determined that the process of initiating the amendment was strictly an internal administrative or parliamentary procedure with none of the ramifications justifying the safeguards of formal legislative action.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the city complied with the notice and other procedural requirements of state and local law and that the trial court erred in declaring the amendatory ordinance invalid. Because the constitutional issues raised in count II of the complaint had not been addressed, the court remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1608 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Midwest Petroleum Marketers Asso. v. Chicago


No. 79-181


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


82 Ill. App. 3d 494; 402 N.E.2d 709; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2558; 37 Ill. Dec. 707



March 13, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CURRY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, petroleum marketing association and gasoline company, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion for judgment filed by defendants city, city department, and intervenor interest groups, at the close of plaintiffs' case in their action seeking to enjoin defendants from enforcing regulations and a declaratory judgment that the ordinance and regulations were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed an action against defendants seeking to enjoin the enforcement of gasoline dispensing regulations and a declaration that the regulations were unconstitutional. The trial court granted defendants' motion for judgment at the conclusion of plaintiffs' case and dismissed the case. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that: (1) a justiciable controversy existed regarding the five percent differential between the price of full service and self-service gasoline fixed by regulation, (2) the regulations that were related to the safety of self-service dispensing of gasoline were a valid exercise of the city's police power and were in the within the purview of the enabling ordinance; (3) the enabling ordinance set standards to guide the commissioner in regulating fairness in pricing; (4) the potential for economic restraint in the retail gasoline market did not outweigh the legitimate government objectives of the regulations, (5) the regulations were not unfairly discriminatory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of the defendants' motion for judgment at the close of plaintiffs' case in plaintiffs' action seeking to enjoin defendants from enforcing regulations and a declaratory judgment that the ordinance and regulations were unconstitutional.

 

1609 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


National Account Systems, Inc. v. Anderson


No. 79-868


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


82 Ill. App. 3d 233; 402 N.E.2d 656; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2525; 37 Ill. Dec. 654



March 7, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. NATHAN M. COHEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, department and director, citing the Collection Agency Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, paras. 2001-2040 (1977), appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) in favor of plaintiff collection agency in its action to enjoin the department and director from suspending or revoking its certificate of registration and to have a department rule declared violative of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2.


OVERVIEW: The director had twice rejected hearing officers' recommendations against suspension or revocation and referred the case for rehearing pursuant to the rule. The department and director contended that the collection agency did not exhausted its administrative remedies and that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, paras. 2037-2038 (1977) authorized the rule. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with directions. The court concluded that equitable relief was appropriate because of the inadequacy of available legal remedies, the futility of the collection agency pursuing administrative relief, and the likelihood of irreparable injury. The court held that the trial court erred in finding the rule unconstitutional on its face, but concluded that the director's construction of the rule exceeded her statutory authority and denied due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. The court held that the language of the rule providing for referral by the director had to be construed to provide for only a single referral for rehearing. The court held that the trial court encroached upon the director's authority by enjoining all further action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's order enjoining further re-references to hearing officers, reversed the portions declaring the rule invalid and unconstitutional on its face and enjoining the taking of action to suspend or revoke the collection agency's license, and remanded the case to the trial court with directions to enter an order directing the department and director to proceed to a final decision based on the record.

 

1610 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hamilton


Nos. 15537, 15538 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


81 Ill. App. 3d 297; 401 N.E.2d 318; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2366; 36 Ill. Dec. 637



February 29, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. DONALD W. MORTHLAND, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions and concurrent sentences imposed by the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) comprised of 30 years for rape and deviate sexual assault, extended terms of 60 years each for rape and deviate sexual assault, 15 years for attempt rape, 7 years for each of 3 convictions for burglary, and 5 years for each of 2 convictions of aggravated battery. The judgments of conviction were entered in 3 trials.


OVERVIEW: As to his conviction for burglary, rape, and deviant sexual assault committed in a day-care center, the court held that identification by the victim was clear and convincing and overcame his alibi defense. The victim's inability to describe features and hesitation to identity went to the issue of credibility for the jury's determination and did not require acquittal. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by admitting evidence of convictions for similar crimes because the convictions were recent. As to defendant's convictions for rape, deviant sexual assault, aggravated battery, and two counts of burglary, the state conceded that one of the burglary counts should have been reversed. However, he was properly convicted of aggravated battery because such conviction was not based on the same facts as the rape and deviant sexual assault convictions and it was not an included offense of those other crimes. With regard to his sentences, the court held that the trial court was not required to find that both facts listed under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2(b) (Supp. 1978) existed in order to impose extended sentences for the convictions for rape and deviant sexual assault.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction for one count of burglary arising out of an incident in a city parking garage and the corresponding sentence. The court affirmed the other convictions and sentences.

 

1611 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Perry


No. 15722


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


81 Ill. App. 3d 422; 401 N.E.2d 1263; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2384; 37 Ill. Dec. 170



February 29, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. LUTHER H. DEARBORN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury trial in the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) resulted in defendant's convictions for three counts of armed robbery, and one count each of home invasion, burglary, and felony theft. He was sentenced to 20 years for each armed robbery charge, 20 years for home invasion, 7 years for burglary, and 5 years for the theft , all to run concurrently, and appealed his convictions and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found to be in possession of property taken after a home invasion and armed robbery. In affirming his conviction, the court noted that the manner of questioning employed on direct examination indicated that defense counsel was trying to infer innocence on the present charges by the fact that defendant had pleaded guilty to previous charges. That was highly improper and the prosecutor was entitled to refute this inference by establishing a plea agreement. Because an informant was a private citizen and not a paid professional, officers were justified in relying upon his information without independent verification or examination of his reliability. Defendant's recent, exclusive, and unexplained possession of stolen items gave rise to an inference of burglary. In affirming the constitutionality of Class X legislation, the court noted that the methods of rehabilitating the criminal offender had been the subject of considerable, diverse discussion, and held that it was a question peculiarly suitable for legislative investigation, analysis, and action. Ill. Pub. Act 80-1099 had not abandoned the concept of rehabilitation set forth in Ill. Const. art. I, § 11.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for all charges and the concurrent sentences imposed, including those for Class X felonies.

 

1612 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Schisler


No. 79-523


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


81 Ill. App. 3d 280; 401 N.E.2d 301; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2362; 36 Ill. Dec. 620



February 25, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Fulton County; the Hon. FRANCIS P. MURPHY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant aunt of a decedent sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Fulton County (Illinois) in favor of appellee third wife of the decedent in the parties' cross-petitions for letters of administration.


OVERVIEW: The decedent's first marriage was annulled. The decedent was married at second time. The decedent and his second wife separated. The decedent then married his third wife. The decedent did not obtain a divorce from his second wife until three years later. The decedent and his third wife continued living together until they separated. Upon the decedent's death, the aunt filed a petition for letters of administration. The aunt's petition did not include the decedent's third wife as an heir. The third wife filed a cross-petition for letters of administration, listing herself as the decedent's sole heir. The circuit court found in favor of the third wife. The aunt appealed. The court affirmed, holding that § 212 of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 212(b) (1977), recognized the decedent's marriage to the third wife after the divorce was obtained from his second wife. The court explained that § 212(b) considered parties lawfully married who cohabited after an impediment to marriage was removed. Thus, the court concluded that the third wife was entitled to the decedent's estate because the marriage was lawful from the date of the divorce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

 

1613 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Alexander v. Harris Trust & Sav. Bank


No. 79-543


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


81 Ill. App. 3d 1047; 401 N.E.2d 1168; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2481; 37 Ill. Dec. 75



February 22, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOHN F. HECHINGER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff beneficiary appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted defendant trustee's motion to dismiss the class action for an accounting of trustees' fees and for reimbursement of trustees' fees collected in violation of § 5 of An Act to Provide for and Regulate the Administration of Trusts by Trust Companies (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 32, para. 291 (1977).


OVERVIEW: The beneficiary brought the class action claim against the trustee, alleging that the percentage fee charged for administration of the trusts violated § 5 of the Act. The circuit court dismissed the beneficiary's action, and the beneficiary appealed from the judgment. The court noted that § 5 of the Act prohibited corporate trustees from receiving compensation in excess of that allowed to natural persons for like services. The court also observed that the natural trustees of trusts created prior to October 1, 1973 were entitled to compensation expressly specified in the trust agreement, or, if not provided in the trust agreement, to reasonable compensation pursuant to § 1 of An Act Concerning Compensation of Trustees, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 148, para. 31 (1971). Because the trusts involved in the beneficiary's action were created prior to October 1, 1973, the court concluded that the trustee was entitled to the "fair and just compensation" for its services, as provided in the trust agreements. A natural trustee would have been permitted to receive the compensation provided in the agreements; therefore, the corporate trustee's fee did not violate § 5 of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the beneficiary's class action claim against the trustee for an accounting of trustee fees and reimbursement of improperly collected fees.

 

1614 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. County of Jo Daviess


No. 79-137


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


81 Ill. App. 3d 354; 401 N.E.2d 265; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2375; 36 Ill. Dec. 584



February 15, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Jo Daviess County; the Hon. HAROLD D. NAGEL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a group of trade union representatives, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Jo Daviess County (Illinois), which found in favor of appellee county in an action involving the setting of the prevailing wage rates for a county.


OVERVIEW: A county board, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 39s-4 (1977), authorized a committee to ascertain the prevailing wage rate for the county. A formula was used by the board in arriving at the prevailing wage rate and objections were filed. During an administrative hearing, the trade union representatives presented alternate findings regarding the prevailing wage rate, but the county rejected their theory and reaffirmed the wage rate set forth by the board. The trade union representatives maintained that the county's determination was erroneous. It argued that the county based the wages partly on wages paid on private projects, whereas the statute required that the rate should be determined by reference to wages paid for work of a similar character on public works. The trial court ruled in favor of the county, and the trade union representatives appealed. The court reversed and held that a literal interpretation of the statute did not render it unconstitutional. The standard for determining the wage rate was not "union scale" but was, instead, "public works." The court concluded that the statute's intent was clearly to determine wages for construction work on public works.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case.

 

1615 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dees


No. 15590


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


81 Ill. App. 3d 35; 400 N.E.2d 1050; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2327; 36 Ill. Dec. 470



February 11, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Coles County; the Hon. TOM E. GRACE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Coles County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss the pending misdemeanor charges of resisting a police officer and escape on the ground that defendant's confinement for a 14-day period, pending his arraignment, violated Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 107-14, 109-1 (1977).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was on parole when he was arrested. After his arrest, the Illinois Department of Corrections issued a warrant based on the charges. Defendant was confined for 14 days before his arraignment. Defendant asserted that his that his rights under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 107-14, 109-1 (1977) were violated by the delay between his arrest and his presentation to a magistrate. The trial court found that the provisions of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 109-1 were mandatory and that the State's failure to comply constituted a denial of defendant's rights to the due process of law under the Fifth Amendment, the Fourteenth Amendment, and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. The trial court dismissed the charges for the State's failure to explain the delay. On appeal, the court held that although a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 109-1 was not a per se due process violation, the unexcused delay was a violation of defendant's rights. The delay itself demonstrated sufficient prejudice to sustain the trial court's finding. The court affirmed the trial court's authority to dismiss the warrant as the remedy, particularly in view of the fact that no other remedy was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the misdemeanor charges against defendant.

 

1616 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Schlenz v. Castle


No. 78-586


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


80 Ill. App. 3d 1131; 400 N.E.2d 753; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2318; 36 Ill. Dec. 333



February 7, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. CHARLES W. SCOTT, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers brought an interlocutory appeal from an order of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) denying their motion for a class determination and motion for partial summary judgment on the issue of the validity of property tax assessment. The also contended that a curative statute did not operate retroactively and that the trial court should have stayed the proceedings pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers, who were property owners, sought class action status in a suit against taxing authorities, claiming that certain reassessments were void. In affirming a ruling that there was no valid class, the court determined that the finding that the prerequisites were not met did not constitute an abuse of discretion. It was possible, however, that the taxpayers might have been able to show that a subclass existed (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 57.3(b) (1977)) and on remand the trial court was directed, within its discretion, to determine whether or not such a subclass could be shown. The court held that the statutory notice prescribed was mandatory, so that the reassessments were rendered void. The court also concluded that a curative Act violated the principle of separation of powers insofar as it attempted to validate real estate assessments made without proper notice for all nonquadrennial years prior to its enactment, and because it sought to nullify a prior decision of the Illinois Supreme Court which clearly interpreted the law as it existed. The staying of proceedings was within the discretion of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that the proposed class did not meet the prerequisites, but remanded for a determination of whether a subclass existed, with the direction that if it did there had to be a substitution of attorneys or class representative. The court reversed the finding that the curative statute operated retroactively.

 

1617 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wright


No. 79-137


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


80 Ill. App. 3d 927; 400 N.E.2d 731; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2284; 36 Ill. Dec. 311



February 4, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. HORACE L. CALVO, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which entered judgment convicting defendant of unlawful possession of cannabis and a controlled substance and which imposed sentence.


OVERVIEW: After an officer observed a youth who appeared to be drinking beer, he and another investigated but discovered no beer. Nevertheless, the officers checked defendant's car for beer cans, at which time two hand-rolled cigarettes were seen in the front seat. The officer searched the rest of the car and discovered the drugs that were later used to convict defendant. At a bench trial, the trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress the confiscated items and all of the statements obtained thereafter. The court, in reversing the convictions, held that the seizure was unlawful because the illegal nature of the hand-rolled cigarettes, in the officer's plain view, was not readily apparent and could not have created in the officer's mind a reasonable suspicion thereof. The court rejected the State's argument that defendant waived his right to complain by failing to file a motion for a new trial, and noted that the waiver rule did not apply where the complaints were raised at the bench trial. Finding that the State failed to show circumstances that dissipated the taint of the illegal arrest, the court concluded that the remaining evidence was insufficient to sustain the convictions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment of conviction.

People v. Hamilton


No. 78-1205


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


80 Ill. App. 3d 794; 400 N.E.2d 599; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2262; 36 Ill. Dec. 179



January 29, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. WILLIAM COUSINS, JR., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of deviate sexual assault and attempted rape. The trial court sentenced defendant to concurrent terms.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting and sentencing defendant. The court held that defendant's transfer from juvenile court to the adult criminal court under § 2-7(3) of the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702-7(3) (1975), was not unconstitutional and that the statute did not violate due process. Moreover, the court determined that defendant's arguments were identical to those considered and rejected by the Illinois Supreme Court in caselaw upholding the statute. Next, the court held that the juvenile court was well within its discretion in transferring defendant to the criminal courts. Nevertheless, the court held that the trial court erred by not permitting defendant to display a scar on his arm to the jury. However, the court held that the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt in view of the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt and did not require reversal. Likewise, the court found no merit in defendant's claim that a black board used by the witnesses in illustrating their testimony constituted a device for "mutual coaching" among the witnesses or that use of the board otherwise prejudiced defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting and sentencing defendant for deviate sexual assault and attempted rape.

Board of Education v. Greater Peoria Sanitary & Sewage Disposal Dist.


No. 79-142


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


80 Ill. App. 3d 1101; 400 N.E.2d 654; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2311; 36 Ill. Dec. 234



January 29, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. JAMES A. HEIPLE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, Board of Education of School District No. 150 of Peoria and the Pleasure Driveway and Park District of Peoria, sought review of a judgment entered in the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois) in favor of defendant Greater Peoria Sanitary and Sewage Disposal District in plaintiffs' action challenging the validity of an ordinance imposing user charges for sewer service.


OVERVIEW: The sanitary district adopted an ordinance imposing user charges for sewer service that applied to all residential, commercial, institutional, and industrial customers, including governmental units. Plaintiffs filed a complaint for a declaratory judgment and an injunction challenging the ordinance on constitutional and statutory grounds in counts I and III and asserting a class action in count II. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the sanitary district as to counts I and III and dismissed count II. On appeal, the court affirmed and ruled (1) that the ordinance did not violate the rule that one unit of local government cannot force a second governmental unit to levy taxes to be paid to the first for its corporate purposes because it was proper for plaintiffs to use their tax revenue to pay necessary operating expenses such as sewer charges, (2) that the charge for sewer service was not a tax and thus plaintiffs could not claim exemption from the ordinance based on their tax exempt status, and (3) that sewer charges did not constitute fees and were not prohibited under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the sanitary district in plaintiffs' action challenging the validity of an ordinance imposing user charges for sewer service.

Settler v. Hopedale Medical Foundation


No. 79-360


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


80 Ill. App. 3d 1074; 400 N.E.2d 577; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2307; 36 Ill. Dec. 157



January 28, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. IVAN L. YONTZ, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff podiatrist sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment for defendants, hospital, administrator, staff podiatrists, and doctors, in the podiatrist's action for damages, punitive damages, and injunctive relief on claims of breach of contract and negligence in the denial of the podiatrist's application for staff privileges at the hospital.


OVERVIEW: The podiatrist's application for privileges to practice at the hospital, a private institution, was denied by the staff podiatrists and physicians. The podiatrist brought an action against the hospital, the administrator, the staff podiatrists, and physicians for compensatory and punitive damages and injunctive relief on claims of breach of contract and negligence. The trial court granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment on 10 counts and the podiatrist sought review. The court affirmed the judgment and held that: (1) the podiatrist had no constitutional right to staff privileges at the hospital because it was a private institution; (2) the private hospital's refusal of staff privileges was not subject to judicial review; (3) the claims against the individuals were derivative of the claim against the hospital and were also precluded; and (4) staff members called on to review the podiatrist's application were immune from suit under the Medical Practice Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91, para. 2(b) (1975).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment that dismissed 10 counts of the podiatrist's complaint against the hospital, the administrator, staff podiatrists, and physicians for the denial of staff privileges at the hospital.

Heller v. Goss


No. 79-690


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


80 Ill. App. 3d 716; 400 N.E.2d 70; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2253; 35 Ill. Dec. 933



January 18, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. LESTER D. FOREMAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tenant appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting plaintiff landlord's motions to strike the tenant's affirmative defenses and for judgment on the pleadings, in the landlord's forcible entry and detainer action.


OVERVIEW: The tenant operated an adult bookstore on the landlord's premises pursuant to a yearly lease, and after the tenant failed to yield possession when the lease expired at the end of the year, the landlord instituted a forcible entry and detainer action against the tenant. Thereafter, the landlord filed a motion to strike the tenant's affirmative defenses and a motion for judgment on the pleadings, both of which were granted. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that because the tenant was a tenant in sufferance at the expiration of his lease, the landlord was entitled to possession of the property unless the tenant pleaded a valid affirmative defense that created an issue of fact regarding possession of the property. The court found that the tenant's public policy defense under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 80, para. 71 (1977) failed because there was no evidence that the tenant's eviction was retaliatory. Further, the court determined that several of the tenant's other defenses were merely conclusions and were not supported by any facts and that the tenant failed to support his argument that the landlord and the city engaged in a civil conspiracy to evict him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order striking the tenant's affirmative defenses and granting the landlord's motion for judgment on the pleadings in the landlord's action for forcible entry and detainer.

People v. Pierce


No. 79-477


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


80 Ill. App. 3d 514; 400 N.E.2d 62; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2232; 35 Ill. Dec. 925

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of battery and sentenced defendant to one year probation on condition that he was incarcerated for the first 30 days.


OVERVIEW: In his first trial, defendant was convicted of battery and sentenced to one year probation. Within 30 days of entry of judgment, defendant filed a written motion requesting a new trial based on a claim that there had not been a jury waiver. The trial court granted defendant's motion. Following a second bench trial, defendant was convicted of battery and sentenced to one year probation on condition that he was incarcerated for the first 30 days. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but reversed that portion of the sentence requiring 30 days incarceration as a condition of probation and remanded the cause to allow the trial court to correct the length of the term of probation.

Vogel v. Robison

Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


80 Ill. App. 3d 312; 399 N.E.2d 688; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2206; 35 Ill. Dec. 622



January 15, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of La Salle County; the Hon. LEONARD HOFFMAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passenger sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of La Salle County (Illinois), which dismissed her action against defendant driver, who was her husband, in the complaint against the husband and defendant, the other driver, for damages due to the automobile accident.


OVERVIEW: The passenger was injured during an automobile accident between her husband and the driver of another car. The passenger brought a tort action against her husband and the other driver. The husband filed a motion to dismiss the action against him, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1001 (1977). The trial court granted the motion and dismissed the action against the husband. On the passenger's appeal, the court determined that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1001 provided that a married woman could bring an action without joining her husband. However, it also provided that neither the husband nor the wife could bring an action against each other for a tort committed during coverture, and that such a provision did not violate the equal protection clauses of either the U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 or the Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. Furthermore, the doctrine of stare decisis precluded an attack on the statute, which had already been found constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which dismissed the passenger's negligence action against her husband.

People v. Cornes


No. 78-348


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


80 Ill. App. 3d 166; 399 N.E.2d 1346; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2190; 35 Ill. Dec. 818



January 7, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County; the Hon. SNYDER HOWELL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois), which was entered on a jury's verdict that convicted defendant of rape, deviate sexual assault, and intimidation. Defendant was sentenced to concurrent terms of imprisonment of 60 years for rape, 60 years for deviate sexual assault, and 10 years for intimidation.


OVERVIEW: The victim alleged that defendant forced her to place his penis in her mouth and have intercourse with him twice. Defendant was convicted of rape, deviate sexual assault, and intimidation, which the court affirmed. The court held that the circuit court did not err in precluding testimony of an alleged abortion of the victim because it would only serve to arouse prejudice in the minds of the jurors. The court determined that defendant's proposed testimony as to the victim's unchaste reputation fell within the express prohibition of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115--7(a) (1978 Supp.). Further, defendant's right to due process and his right of confrontation were not violated by the Illinois rape shield law. The court held that the circuit court did not abuse its discretion by admitting the 24-year-old convictions of defendant for armed robbery into evidence. The circuit court could have determined that the convictions were not too remote in time because defendant was placed on parole only four years prior to the trial. It could also have reasonably considered the length of defendant's criminal record in deciding whether to admit the convictions for purposes of impeachment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment that convicted defendant of rape, deviate sexual assault, and intimidation, and sentenced him to concurrent prison terms.

People v. Seymour


No. 78-2033


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


80 Ill. App. 3d 221; 398 N.E.2d 1191; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3853; 35 Ill. Dec. 241



December 31, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. FRANKLIN I. KRAL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which suppressed cocaine found on defendant during a strip search. Defendant was strip searched after being arrested for a misdemeanor and was not advised of his right to be immediately released upon posting a pre set bond. Defendant was charged with possession of cocaine in violation of Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 561/2, para 1402 (1977).


OVERVIEW: Police arrested defendant after discovering defendant was carrying a concealed weapon, a misdemeanor, although defendant also had a permit for the weapon. At the police station, police searched defendant's pockets several times, eventually conducting a strip search during which they discovered a small amount of cocaine concealed in defendant's sock. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the cocaine was properly suppressed because the police failed to notify defendant of his right to be released on bond prior to the strip search. The court also found that the strip search violated defendants right to privacy under Ill. Const. art. I, § 6 because it was unreasonable to have conducted a warrantless search under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that suppressed cocaine found on defendant during a strip search after his arrest on a misdemeanor charge.

People v. Phipps


No. 15546


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


79 Ill. App. 3d 532; 398 N.E.2d 650; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3738; 34 Ill. Dec. 827



December 27, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Logan County; the Hon. WILLIAM M. ROBERTS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an interlocutory order of the Circuit Court of Logan County (Illinois), which stated that the Mental Health Code did not forbid the production of certain personal material regarding the State's potential witnesses to defendant. The circuit court held that any witnesses who invoked the privilege, or on whose behalf it was invoked, would not be permitted to testify.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with cruelty to persons, maltreatment of a mentally retarded person, and battery. All of the offenses occurred while defendant was an employee of a developmental center. He filed a pretrial motion for discovery, which requested the names and addresses of all persons to be called as witnesses by the State. The State's answer listed 20 witnesses that it intended to call. Defendant filed a motion for additional discovery, which asserted that seven witnesses were residents of the developmental center and that the State maintained personal files on the individuals. On appeal, the court held that it had no jurisdiction to hear the appeal. The court found that the circuit court's ruling was merely evidentiary and simply removed one item of evidence from consideration by the jury because the circuit court's order only affected seven of the 20 witnesses. The court concluded that the order was not appealable as "suppressing evidence" under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(a). To the extent that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 910(b) (Supp. 1978) attempted to provide for appeals from less than final judgment, the court held that it was unconstitutional and void.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

United Air Lines, Inc. v. Mahin


No. 78-320


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


79 Ill. App. 3d 1004; 398 N.E.2d 1064; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3805; 35 Ill. Dec. 114



December 27, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. EARL ARKISS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) determined that the Illinois use tax was applicable to aviation fuel purchased by plaintiff airline in Indiana and stored in Illinois, the airline moved for an order directing defendant, the director of the state's revenue department, to grant a refund, in a certain amount, from the protest fund into which the tax had been paid. The airline appealed from the trial court's denial of that motion.


OVERVIEW: The airline sought a refund in an amount equal to that which the airline had paid to the seller of the fuel in Indiana for payment of Indiana gross income taxes incurred by the seller as the result of that sale. The purchase contracts provided that any tax incurred by the seller by reason of the sale of the fuel would be paid by the airline. The airline contended the trial court erred because the airline was entitled to an exemption by the terms of the Illinois Use Tax Act. The court agreed. The Illinois Use Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 439.3 (sixth unnumbered paragraph (1975), provided that one who had purchased tangible personal property outside of Illinois and had paid a tax in that other state in respect to the sale, purchase, or use of such property was exempt from the Illinois use tax on the use of the property in Illinois to the extent of the amount of tax paid in the other state. When the seller sold the fuel to the airline, the gross receipts from that sale were subject to the Indiana gross income tax; the airline then undertook to pay the tax. Clearly this was a tax paid "in respect to" the sale or purchase of the fuel, which was all the statute required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause for entry of an order in accordance with the opinion.

People v. Clark


No. 79-309


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


80 Ill. App. 3d 46; 399 N.E.2d 261; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3839; 35 Ill. Dec. 427



December 27, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. HORACE L. CALVO, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to possession of a controlled substance, in violation of § 402(b) of the Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1402(b) (1977), and agreed to plead guilty to a misdemeanor theft charge, in return for a sentence recommendation. He was sentenced to one year's probation. He appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which denied his motion to dismiss the possession charge.


OVERVIEW: On the date he was sentenced, defendant filed a motion to withdraw his guilty plea, to vacate his sentence, and to dismiss the possession charge, citing the decision of the Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, in People v. Natoli, which held the statute under which he was charged unconstitutional. The trial court allowed defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea and vacate his sentence, but denied the motion to dismiss. Defendant moved for reconsideration. The trial court refused to dismiss the cause. The court held the trial court should have dismissed the possession charge based on the Natoli decision. It held that it had jurisdiction of the appeal because defendant filed his notice of appeal within four days after denial of the motion to reconsider and he was appealing from a final judgment for purposes of appeal. It also found that, regardless of the merits of the State's argument that defendant was estopped from attacking the negotiated guilty plea, his conviction could not stand since the statute under which he was convicted was a nullity. Defendant had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the sentencing provisions applicable to the possession charge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, denying defendant's motion to dismiss the possession charge.

Schallau v. Northlake


Nos. 78-1336, 78-1467 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


82 Ill. App. 3d 456; 403 N.E.2d 266; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3872; 38 Ill. Dec. 178



December 18, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Opinion Filed on Denial of Rehearing April 22, 1980, Reported at 82 Ill. App. 3d 456 at 468.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. REGINALD J. HOLZER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his declaratory and injunctive action against defendants, city, bank, and developer, to prevent a zoning change, annexation, and construction of an apartment complex. The defendants argued that quo warranto was the citizen's sole remedy, and the city cross-appealed a contempt order and the grant of mandamus relief to the developer.


OVERVIEW: After the developer obtained a zoning change and the city approved an annexation for the construction of an apartment complex, the citizen filed an action that sought injunctive and declaratory relief against the bank, the developer, and the city. The citizen's action was dismissed, he filed an appeal, and defendants filed a motion that quo warranto was the citizen's sole remedy. The city filed a cross-appeal as to a contempt order and the granting of mandamus relief to the developer for the issuance of a building permit. The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the citizen's action, holding that quo warranto was the only proper remedy to challenge the validity of an annexation. Because the citizen was unable to present sufficient evidence of damages in his original claim, the court found that he was not entitled to amend his complaint to conform with the Quo Warranto Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 112, para. 10 (1977) on the grounds that he had not pleaded or established facts which would entitle him to relief. The contempt order against the city, however, was invalid because the underlying order mandating the issuance of a permit to the developer had to be reversed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the citizen's action for declaratory and injunctive relief against the city, bank, and developer, to prevent a zoning change, annexation, and construction of an apartment complex. The court reversed the orders granting mandamus relief and holding the city in contempt in the city's cross-appeal against the developer.

In re Marriage of Thornqvist


No. 78-1753


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


79 Ill. App. 3d 791; 399 N.E.2d 176; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3780; 35 Ill. Dec. 342



December 14, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOHN J. CROWN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner wife appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) distributing marital property under the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 101 et seq. (1977). After she was granted a default divorce on publication, the decree was opened and thereafter an agreed order was entered allowing the dissolution to stand but vacating all other portions of the default judgment.


OVERVIEW: After a hearing concerning disposition of property, the trial court entered an order awarding respondent husband's shares in a co-owned corporation to the wife because of the contributions she made to the corporation. On appeal, the husband contended that the Act was unconstitutional and that the trial court erred in several respects. The court affirmed, holding that the Act was not unconstitutional because it encompassed more than one subject: namely, that it included both marriage and divorce and did not violate the doctrines of separation of powers and due process. The Act did not violate the husband's equal protection rights. The trial court properly denied his motion for temporary relief and the subsequent renewal thereof, requesting sufficient mileage allowance, plane fare, and temporary support so that he could appear and attend his deposition and prosecute his property rights against the wife at trial; the uncontradicted testimony of the wife was that the corporation owed him nothing, and his affidavit was lacking in anything factual to substantiate his inability to pay his own expenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Rockamann


No. 79-202


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


79 Ill. App. 3d 575; 399 N.E.2d 162; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3746; 35 Ill. Dec. 328



December 5, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. JOHN J. HOBAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of judgment from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of two counts of taking indecent liberties with a child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of taking indecent liberties with his daughter, a minor. Defendant was charged by indictment with four counts of indecent liberties with a child. Defendant was granted a competency hearing, and it was determined that defendant fit to stand trial even though he was borderline retarded and he suffered from depression. After a bench trial, defendant was found guilty of two of the four charges. Defendant appealed the conviction on the grounds that that the circuit court erred in finding him competent to stand trial, that the circuit court erred in finding that he possessed the requisite mental capacity to commit the alleged crimes, and that the circuit court erred in ruling on certain evidentiary objections. The court affirmed because the question of whether a bona fide doubt existed as to defendant's competency to stand trial was within the sound discretion of the circuit court, and there was no clear showing of abuse of discretion. The court ruled that suffering from a psychiatric disturbance did not in and of itself render defendant unfit to stand trial, for one could be fit to stand trial although his mind might otherwise be unsound or defective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1633 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. King


No. 77-533


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


78 Ill. App. 3d 879; 397 N.E.2d 905; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3625; 34 Ill. Dec. 233



November 30, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of La Salle County; the Hon. LEONARD HOFFMAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of La Salle County (Illinois), which convicted him of burglary.


OVERVIEW: On the night of the burglary, defendant was found to have the stolen items in his possession. The basis of his conviction was a common law inference that allowed the jury to find burglary if defendant was found in possession of recently stolen property without a reasonable explanation. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for burglary because the common law inference did not violate defendant's right to due process of law. The use of the common law inference was judged within the context of defendant's individual case and the court determined that the inference satisfied the reasonable doubt standard because the evidence indicated that defendant transported, delivered, and sold the stolen items. The use of the inference did not violate defendant's presumption of innocence because only the burden of production shifted to defendant to rebut the inference. At all times the burden of persuasion beyond a reasonable doubt remained with the prosecution. The actions of the prosecution were proper when the grand jury was reconvened for the purpose of investigating possible additional charges based upon the bill of sale that was produced by defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment that convicted defendant of burglary.

In re Estate of Ragen


No. 78-1152


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


79 Ill. App. 3d 8; 398 N.E.2d 198; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3669; 34 Ill. Dec. 523



November 30, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ROBERT C. SPRINGSGUTH, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, co-executors and legatees, appealed a judgment of theCircuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that held petitioners, mother and daughter, had proven by a preponderance of the evidence that the decedent was the father of the daughter, and therefore ordered an amendment of the heirship of the decedent's estate.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's order specifically stated that the daughter had established that the decedent was her father by a preponderance of the evidence, which evidence consisted of the decedent's attorney's testimony, and legal documents submitted in a custody proceeding in which the decedent claimed that he was the father of the daughter. The court reversed that order because Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110 1/2, para. 2--2 (1975), explicitly provided that the applicable standard of proof for paternity actions was the clear and convincing standard. Furthermore, that standard was certainly different and a higher burden of proof than the preponderance of the evidence standard. The court next held that the decedent's attorney's testimony as to their discussions regarding the daughter were not protected by the attorney-client privilege because those discussions were for the purpose of subsequent public disclosure in the custody proceedings. Also, admission of those discussions laid the foundation for introduction of documents to the same effect. Finally the motion for a blood test was properly denied because it was not reasonably made under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110A, para. 215 (1977).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that held the daughter had proven by a preponderance of the evidence that paternity with the decedent had been established, because the applicable standard of proof was the clear and convincing standard. The court then remanded the matter for further proceedings consistent with its determination.

 

1635 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Difanis v. Barr


No. 15464


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


78 Ill. App. 3d 842; 397 N.E.2d 895; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3620; 34 Ill. Dec. 223



November 28, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. ROBERT J. STEIGMANN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant members of the city council appealed from an judgment of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), in an action filed by plaintiff state attorney under the Open Meetings Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 102, para. 41 et seq. (1977), to obtain a declaratory judgment that the city counsel could not meet in closed session to discuss city council business.


OVERVIEW: Shortly before a scheduled city council meeting, eight of the nine Democrats on the city council, along with one independent member, held a caucus. The press did not receive notice of the caucus, and the public was not invited. The issues discussed at the private meeting included both issues on the agenda for that night's city council meeting as well as issues not on the agenda. The state attorney filed action to keep the counsel members from meeting in closed session to discuss city council business. The city counsel argued that the Act did not apply to political caucuses. The court affirmed, stating that characterizing a meeting as a political caucus should not distract attention from the real purpose of the meeting. In this case all the subjects that were discussed were properly business of the city council, and some of the subjects discussed were in fact on the agenda for the council meeting. The court found that the members were meeting as council members, although they were mostly Democrats, and not as a committee of a political party in violation of the Act. Further the court found that the Act was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the state attorney that the city counsel members could not meet in privet in contravention to the Act was affirmed.

 

1636 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Evans v. Bachman


No. 78-1511


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


78 Ill. App. 3d 1107; 398 N.E.2d 114; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3660; 34 Ill. Dec. 439



November 26, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. DAVID A. CANEL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed defendant hospital from the patient's medical malpractice action against it and defendant doctor, and which dismissed the patient's petition to vacate the dismissal, and denied the patient leave to file his third amended complaint.


OVERVIEW: The patient brought a medical malpractice action against defendants alleging that the doctor had committed several negligent acts in connection with the care of the patient's fractured ankle. The trial court dismissed the hospital, denied the patient's petition to vacate the dismissal, and denied the patient leave to file his third amended complaint. The patient appealed, and the court affirmed. The court concluded from the patient's pleadings that he discovered not only the nature of his affliction but also that it was allegedly wrongfully caused before the passage of the two-year period immediately following the alleged wrongdoing by the doctor. The court rejected the patient's argument that the action fell within the fraudulent concealment exception to the statute of limitations set forth in Limitations Act § 22 for the same reason the discovery rule was inapplicable. The court held that the respondent in discovery statute was inapplicable because it was available only against individuals. The court concluded that the patient had no unconditional right to amend his pleadings after final judgment for any purpose other than to conform the pleadings to the proof.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the hospital from the patient's medical malpractice action against it and the doctor, and affirmed the dismissal of the patient's petition to vacate the dismissal, and affirmed the denial of leave to file his third amended complaint.

In re Estate of Rudder


No. 78-320


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


78 Ill. App. 3d 517; 397 N.E.2d 556; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3577; 34 Ill. Dec. 100



November 20, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. JOHN S. TESCHNER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother of a minor appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which denied her petition against defendant estate administrator to reopen and set aside awards and allowances made out of decedent's estate.


OVERVIEW: Decedent's death was the result of injuries sustained in an accidental fall from a roof. His estate received wrongful death settlement proceeds, which were distributed among his spouse and children as heirs of the estate, and the estate was thereafter ordered closed. The mother of the minor brought an action seeking to open the estate and set aside the awards, based on her allegations that she and decedent had lived together and had produced a minor son who was entitled to a share in the estate proceeds. The trial court denied her request for relief and she appealed. The court affirmed the denial, holding that the section of the Probate Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110 1/2, para. 2-2 (1978 Supp.), was to be applied only to estates that had not been closed in allowing an illegitimate child to inherit from the intestate estate of a decedent father who died prior to September 12, 1978. The court reviewed the three criteria for determining retroactivity of a judicial decision and determined that prospective application was proper. Additionally, the court held that the petition required denial because although it was proper in form, she was unable to show a meritorious defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the mother of the minor's petition seeking to reopen decedent's estate and to set aside the distribution of the settlement proceeds therein.

 

1638 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Illinois Polygraph Soc. v. Pellicano


No. 78-771


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


78 Ill. App. 3d 340; 396 N.E.2d 1354; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3551; 33 Ill. Dec. 630



November 14, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. NATHAN COHEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an unlicensed deception-detection examiner, appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his motion to dismiss the complaint of plaintiffs, individual licensed polygraph examiners and an organization of licensed examiners. The licensed examiners alleged that the unlicensed examiner was in violation of the Illinois detection-of-deception-examiners act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, paras. 2401-2432 (1977).


OVERVIEW: The licensed examiners alleged that the unlicensed examiner's activities reduced their income, and they sought to enjoin him from administering exams. Instead of the polygraph, the unlicensed examiner used a psychological stress evaluator that measured the human voice rather than cardiovascular or respiratory patterns. The Act required that examiners use an instrument that recorded cardio-vascular and respiratory patterns as minimum standards. The circuit court ruled that the unlicensed examiner was subject to the Act. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the Act was unconstitutional. Even though the Act required that a licensed examiner who chose to use another device had to also use a polygraph, the Act permitted the examiner to rely on the test results produced by the other equipment to the complete exclusion of the polygraph results. By permitting an examiner to ignore the polygraph results, the Act made use of the polygraph by such an examiner superfluous. The Act granted to the polygraph a statutory preemption of the field and enhanced the sale of polygraph instruments. The Act was a denial of equal protection and granted a special statutory privilege.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment granted to the licensed examiners.

 

1639 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Josic v. Josic


No. 78-1834


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


78 Ill. App. 3d 347; 397 N.E.2d 204; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3552; 33 Ill. Dec. 871



November 14, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOHN CROWN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner husband appealed the order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his petition to modify a divorce judgment that provided for payments to respondent wife and found that § 801(c) of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act (new Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 101 et seq. (1977) governed his petition. The husband contended that § 801(c) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The parties' divorce judgment incorporated their property settlement agreement that provided that the husband would pay the wife a family living expense inclusive of child support and alimony. The agreement precluded modification by a court. Two years later the husband filed an unsuccessful petition for modification of the judgment, asserting that he had suffered a paralyzing stroke that rendered him unable to work. Three years later the husband again asked the trial court to modify the divorce judgment for the same reasons. The trial court denied the petition, finding that § 502(f) of the new Act precluded modification by a court if the separation agreement so provided. On appeal, the court found that although the legislature could not pass a retrospective law that impaired the obligation of a contract or deprived a citizen of a vested right, the husband had no vested right to modification, only an expectation that he could seek such relief under the preexisting divorce laws. The court found that § 801(a) unequivocally provided that the new Act applied to all proceedings commenced after its effective date for the modification of an order entered prior to its effective date.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

People v. Keagbine

Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District

November 13, 1979, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Pope County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and armed robbery, and upon review the court affirmed. The court remanded the cause to the trial court for assessment of costs against defendant as mandated by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 180-3 (1977). The court held that defendant's waiver of a jury trial in exchange for the State's agreement not to seek the death penalty if he were convicted was knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily entered. The court held that defendant's right to a speedy trial under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 103-5 (1977) was not violated. The court held that the trial court properly charged defendant with delay of the proceedings occasioned by the filing of his suppression motion. The court held that because defendant was brought to trial within 120 days plus the number of days of delay attributed to defendant, he had not been deprived of his right to a speedy trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause to the trial court for the assessment of costs against defendant as mandated by statute.
