Montague v. George J. London Memorial Hospital


No. 78-172


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


78 Ill. App. 3d 298; 396 N.E.2d 1289; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3545; 33 Ill. Dec. 565



November 13, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. PAUL F. ELWARD, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mental patient sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed with prejudice his claim that defendants, hospital and medical director, violated § 5-3 of the Illinois Mental Health Code of 1967 (Mental Health Code), codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 5-3 (1975), as barred by the applicable statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: The mental patient properly executed and delivered to the hospital and medical director a five-day notice pursuant to § 5-3 of the Mental Health Code after he was voluntarily admitted to the hospital. The hospital and medical director allegedly refused to allow the mental patient to leave and he was kept there against his will for an additional four months. The appellate court reversed, holding that the mental patient's cause of action was not untimely. The court found that the mental patient could bring a private cause of action pursuant to § 5-3 of the Mental Health Code and that action was subject to the five-year limitation period of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 83, para. 16 (1975).

People v. Cater


No. 78-113


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


78 Ill. App. 3d 983; 398 N.E.2d 28; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3641; 34 Ill. Dec. 353



November 13, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 15, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. MICHAEL J. ORENIC and the Hon. CHARLES P. CONNOR, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated kidnapping. He claimed that his transfer from juvenile court under the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702-7 (1977), was unconstitutional, an abuse of discretion, and not based on a bona fide determination about his amenability to treatment as a juvenile, and that it was error to refuse his necessity instruction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, at age 16, was among a group of thugs that commandeered a car entering a highway and robbed the driver at gunpoint. In affirming his conviction, the court noted summarily that the Juvenile Court Act was constitutional. The court next held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in waiving jurisdiction, noting that the offense was a serious one, the evidence tended to prove that defendant threatened the victim, and the trial court had received the testimony of a probation officer that no facilities for delinquent minors existed in the county and that the department of corrections would better serve the needs of defendant. The court held that because the transfer was merely dispositional, due process was served. The court pointed out that the trial court needed only to consider the statutory factors that were present in the case and did not have to accord equal weight to the factors. The court held that it was not error to refuse the necessity instruction in light of the issuance of a better-suited compulsion instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated kidnapping.

People v. Brisco


Nos. 78-1412, 78-1749 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


78 Ill. App. 3d 282; 397 N.E.2d 160; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3542; 33 Ill. Dec. 827



November 8, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ALBERT GREEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted them of possession of cannabis and sentenced them to one year felony probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that the two laboratory tests, which were performed on the seized substances, did not satisfy the State's burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that they were cannabis. They also argued that the State's failure to purify the substances created a reasonable doubt that the substances were cannabis and that the Cannabis Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 701 et seq. (1975) was unconstitutional. The court determined that the trial court's conclusion that the Duquenois-Levine test, when used in conjunction with microscopic analysis, was sufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the seized substances were cannabis was supported by the State's forensic chemist's testimony. The court explained that the absence of a purification process did not detract from the chemist's conclusion that the substances were cannabis because the trial court had a right to believe the chemist's opinion that no substance other than cannabis would have produced a positive reaction to both of the tests. The court concluded that the constitutional issues, concerning the State's power to make the possession of cannabis illegal, were rejected in a previous court decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Talman v. Department of Registration & Education


Nos. 78-704, 78-1101 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division

November 8, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CURRY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pharmacist sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed defendant Department of Registration and Education's (department) order that had revoked the pharmacist's license.


OVERVIEW: The complaint against the pharmacist alleged that he violated § 7-6 of the Pharmacy Practice Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91, para. 55.7-6 (1975) and §§ 102(w)(2), (3), (4), and 306 of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, paras. 1102(w)(2),(3), (4), and 1306. The court affirmed the judgment and remanded it for reconsideration of the penalty assessed against the pharmacist. The court held that the testimony of a department investigator was sufficient to have found that the pharmacist violated the "good faith" standard set out in §§ 1102(w)(2), (3), (4). The court also decided that the record keeping section in the statute was not limited to pharmacists who were registered under the Controlled Substances Act and the pharmacist came within the scope of that statute's record keeping requirements. There was no abuse of discretion in the revocation of the pharmacist's license. Finally, the court determined that the factual specificity of the allegations against the pharmacist was sufficient and there had been no constitutional due process violations.

Geneva Residential Asso. v. Geneva


No. 78-389


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


77 Ill. App. 3d 744; 397 N.E.2d 849; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3444; 34 Ill. Dec. 177



October 31, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. PAUL SCHNAKE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners, citing § 11-13-1.1 of the Municipal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-13-1.1 (1977), sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which entered judgment for defendants, city and restaurant owner, in the landowners' declaratory judgment action challenging the validity of a city ordinance granting the restaurant owner's application for a special use permit.


OVERVIEW: The landowners contended on appeal that the trial court erred in dismissing three counts of their complaint, and that the trial court' s decision that the ordinance was not unconstitutional was against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with directions. The court determined that each of the first two counts stated a cause of action based on failure to comply with Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-13-1.1 (1977), noting that the legislature required the fact-finding process for municipal special use permits to be vested in an administrative agency, to be based on evidence introduced by the applicant according to delineated standards, and to contain specific findings of fact. The court held that the two counts properly alleged that the ordinance was invalid due to procedural deficiencies by the plan commission. The court determined that the third count was not justiciable because the motives of members of a municipal authority were not proper subjects of judicial inquiry. The court did not find that the decision of the trial court on the constitutionality of the ordinance was manifestly against the weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the part of the trial court's judgment in the landowners' action against the city and restaurant owner dismissing claims that adoption of a special use ordinance was procedurally inadequate, affirmed the parts of the judgment finding that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally arbitrary or unreasonable and dismissing a claim of conflict of interest, and remanded for a determination on substantial statutory compliance.

No. 77-1569


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


78 Ill. App. 3d 896; 397 N.E.2d 845; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3626; 34 Ill. Dec. 173



October 29, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of Rehearing December 3, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. DAVID A. CANEL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, administrator in a wrongful death action, appealed from the orders of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), dismissing his first amended complaint against defendant doctors and hospital on the grounds that § 21.1 of the Civil Practice Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 21.1 (1977), was unconstitutional, and dismissing his second amended complaint as filed beyond the two-year statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: In a wrongful death action, the administrator amended his original complaint against a doctor shortly before the statute of limitations ran to include additional defendants in discovery under § 21 of the Civil Practice Act. The trial court dismissed the complaint on the basis that § 21 was unconstitutional. The administrator filed a second amended complaint naming the hospitals and doctors that was dismissed by the trial court as filed beyond the two-year statute of limitations. On review, the court affirmed, holding that because the administrator had not complied with the requirements of § 21, it need not determine the constitutionality of the statute. The court further stated that joinder of additional defendants by amendment to the pleadings after the statute limitations had run was contrary to law under § 46(1) of the Civil Practice Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 46(1) (1977), and that the one-year savings provision for involuntary dismissals under either § 24 of the Civil Practice Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 83, para. 24a (1977) or joinder of parties under § 26 of the Civil Practice Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 26 (1977) could not be applied beyond the statute.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order dismissing the administrator's amended wrongful death complaints against various doctors and hospital was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: Prior to trial, defendant attacked the constitutionality of the sections of the Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. The court concluded that defendant had no right to choose between specific sentences. The court determined that defense counsel stated that he had explained the alternatives to defendant, and defendant made no claim of inadequacy of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Adams v. Peoria


No. 78-491


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


77 Ill. App. 3d 683; 396 N.E.2d 572; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3432; 33 Ill. Dec. 183



October 22, 1979, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which dismissed the homeowners' tort action against defendant city with prejudice pursuant to § 5-103(b) of the Local Governmental and Governmental Tort Immunity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 5-103(b) (1977).


OVERVIEW: The homeowners instituted a tort action against the city after a fire that the city's fire department attempted to extinguish damaged their house. The trial court granted the city's motion to dismiss the action against it with prejudice based upon its immunity under the Local Governmental and Governmental Tort Immunity Act. The homeowners contended on appeal that § 5-103(b) of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 5-103(b) (1977) was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the judgment against the homeowners. Const. art. I, § 12.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed the homeowners' tort action against the city with prejudice.

People v. Dixon


No. 77-535


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


78 Ill. App. 3d 73; 397 N.E.2d 45; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3507; 33 Ill. Dec. 712



October 18, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. WARREN D. WOLFSON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder and sentenced him to a prison term of 14 to 15 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was unconstitutionally required to bear the burden of proof at his fitness hearing and that the trial court's exclusion of a witness as a discovery sanction denied his U.S. Const. amends. VI and XIV rights to a fair and impartial trial. The court determined that the burden of proof provisions did not affect the trial court's determination. The court explained that where the record as a whole indicated the statutory burden of proof was not a significant factor in the fitness determination, the burden of proving the issue of fitness to stand trial was not ultimately borne by defendant. The court noted that defendant was found fit to stand trial by a preponderance of the evidence because the State's expert witness testified that defendant's epileptic condition would not have prevented him from assisting in his defense. The court concluded that because the evidence of medical negligence was not relevant to any legal defense available to defendant, it was not an abuse of the trial court's discretion to exclude his medical expert's testimony when the defense failed to disclose its intent to present that testimony until after the State had rested its case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1650 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Betts v. State, Dep't of Revenue


No. 78-2046


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


78 Ill. App. 3d 102; 396 N.E.2d 1150; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3511; 33 Ill. Dec. 426



October 18, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. REGINALD J. HOLZER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff drugstore owner was convicted of selling drugs without a prescription and his business, property, and firearms were seized. Plaintiff challenged the denial by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of his motion for a temporary injunction on further action being taken against him by defendants, state and state agencies, and dismissal of his complaint alleging that defendants would continue to deny him equal protection of the law.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff drugstore owner was convicted of selling drugs without a prescription. Defendant state agencies later seized his business because of a tax lien and seized his property and unregistered firearms. Plaintiff sought a temporary injunction to keep defendants from pursuing further actions against him on the grounds that defendants' actions deprived him of his liberty and property rights. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court and dismissed the complaint because plaintiff's claim against defendants was barred by sovereign immunity under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 801 (1973). Plaintiff did not claim that defendants acted pursuant to an unconstitutional statute or that defendants exceeded their authority or acted illegally. The injunctive relief requested by plaintiff would curtail even legal and proper prosecutions and investigations by defendants. Furthermore, plaintiff's amended complaint did not allege any facts establishing a conspiracy and the need for injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of plaintiff drugstore owner's motion for a temporary injunction to keep defendants, state and its agencies, from engaging in an alleged conspiracy against him. Plaintiff's claims were barred by sovereign immunity because defendants did not act pursuant to an unconstitutional statute, exceed their authority, or act illegally. There was no factual basis to establish the need for injunctive relief.

 

1651 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Tanquilut v. Illinois Dep't of Public Aid


No. 78-1271


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


78 Ill. App. 3d 55; 396 N.E.2d 1126; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3504; 33 Ill. Dec. 402



October 16, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CURRY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, physician, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which affirmed the decision of the defendant, Illinois Department of Public Aid (IDPA), which terminated the physician's eligibility as a vendor of medical services, barring him from continued participation in the Medical Assistance Program.


OVERVIEW: The physician leased a pharmacy in the building where his medical practice was located. The practice financed the pharmacy inventory and provided heat, light, custodial service, parking, water, scavenger service, and storage. The IDPA notified the physician that his eligibility to participate in the state Medical Assistance Program was terminated, alleging violation of federal law and receipt of excessive rent from the pharmacy. The physician sought judicial review of the administrative decision, and the trial court affirmed his termination. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment affirming his termination from the program. The court held that the IDPA findings were against the manifest weight of the evidence because the only evidence the IDPA produced at the hearing concerned the lease between the medical practice and the pharmacy, and the IDPA neither proved excessive consideration nor introduced any relevant, probative data from which such a conclusion might have been derived. The court further held that there was no specific statutory direction that would have allowed it to label the lease a per se violation for which a felony could have been charged under federal law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment affirming the action of the IDPA which terminated the physician from the medical assistance program.

 

1652 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wallace


No. 78-380


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


77 Ill. App. 3d 979; 397 N.E.2d 20; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3482; 33 Ill. Dec. 687



October 15, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Saline County; the Hon. ARLIE O. BOSWELL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with transacting business under an assumed name. The Circuit Court of Saline County (Illinois) granted defendant's motion to dismiss for failure to state a cause of action. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged by criminal complaint with violating section 1 of "An Act in relation to the use of an assumed name in the conduct or transaction of business in this State," contrary to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 96, para. 4 (1977). The trial court granted their motion to dismiss for failure to state a cause of action. The court reversed the lower court and held that the complaint was sufficient to apprise defendants of the charges against them and the information was adequate for them to prepare a defense. Defendants argued that the alleged defect made the statute constitutionally vague. The court did not agree. The court concluded that defendants' solicitation, or invitation, or orders accompanied by guaranteed payments constituted the transaction of business as prohibited by statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the complaint and reinstated the charges on remand.

 

1653 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Turner


No. 78-481


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


77 Ill. App. 3d 985; 397 N.E.2d 25; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3483; 33 Ill. Dec. 692



October 15, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. JOHN J. HOBAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which following a bench trial, convicted him of armed violence and sentenced him to six years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The bill of indictment charged that defendant committed the offense of armed violence in that he, while armed with a dangerous weapon, a pistol, performed a felony prohibited by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-4(b)(1) in that he struck a woman in the head with the pistol, a deadly weapon, thereby causing her bodily harm in violation of para. 33A-2. At trial, the evidence established that defendant did in fact strike the complaining witness on the head with a pistol in a drug store parking lot. On appeal, defendant claimed that he was placed in double jeopardy because the same factor that elevated the offense from the underlying felony of aggravated battery to armed violence, i.e., the use of the gun, was an essential element of proving that underlying felony. The court disagreed, finding that the constitutional concept of double jeopardy protected a person against a second prosecution for the same offense after either acquittal or conviction and protected against multiple punishments for the same offense. Because defendant was neither tried nor punished twice for the same offense, the court found there was no violation of his constitutional guarantee against double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1654 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Woodward


No. 78-72


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


77 Ill. App. 3d 352; 395 N.E.2d 1203; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3390; 32 Ill. Dec. 822



October 11, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. HARRY D. STROUSE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which found him guilty of voluntary manslaughter. Defendant claimed that § 2-7(3) of the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702-7(3) (1977), was unconstitutional and that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury of the complete defense of self-defense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 15 years old at the time of the alleged homicide and 16 years old at the time of trial. He was convicted as an adult of voluntary manslaughter. The court rejected defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of the statute allowing his transfer to adult jurisdiction; however, it found that it was reversible error to refuse an instruction which would have given defendant the right to present to the jury a theory of complete self-defense. There was testimony that defendant had heard the victim say to defendant's father only a minute or two before the incident that he was returning home to procure a gun to kill the father. Further, an offer of proof was made to the effect that the victim had a reputation among children in the neighborhood for violence and aggression. There was further evidence that defendant was aware of the victim's reputation for ferocity and belligerence. The offer of proof also indicated that the victim had a reputation for carrying a gun. In addition, the victim indicated that he was going home to procure a gun and a gun was found near the victim as he lay on the floor of his own residence after the shooting even though it was only a pellet gun.


OUTCOME: The court found that it was reversible error to refuse an instruction on the theory of complete self-defense, reversed defendant's conviction for voluntary manslaughter, and remanded the cause for a new trial.

 

1655 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hovanec


No. 77-1913


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


76 Ill. App. 3d 401; 394 N.E.2d 1340; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3252; 32 Ill. Dec. 1



September 14, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JAMES E. STRUNCK, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which rendered judgment on a jury verdict convicting defendant on armed robbery after denying defendant's motion to dismiss the armed robbery information for failure to have a court or grand jury return a finding of probable cause.


OVERVIEW: At the preliminary hearing, the judge found that there was probable cause for the robbery charge, but made no finding on the accompanying armed robbery charge. Subsequently, the state added the armed robbery charge by information and defendant was convicted. Defendant contended inter alia that it was unconstitutional to add the armed robbery charge by information because a finding of no probable cause had previously been made on the same charge. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that: (1) because an express finding of no probable cause was not made on the armed robbery charge, it was constitutional to add the same charge by information; (2) defendant's constitutional rights were not violated where cross examination was not permitted on whether a showup identification rather than a lineup had been used because there was no constitutional right to a lineup as opposed to a showup; and (3) the state did not destroy exculpatory evidence by returning the cigarette cartons allegedly stolen from the gas station because while the state was unaware of its exculpatory nature, defendant was aware of its nature, but made no specific request for the cartons.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction against defendant.

 

1656 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Tuftee v. County of Kane


No. 78-457


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


76 Ill. App. 3d 128; 394 N.E.2d 896; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3205; 31 Ill. Dec. 694



September 10, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. JOHN S. PAGE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner filed an action against defendant county for declarative and injunctive relief after the county denied the landowner's application for the construction of a horse barn. The county sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which enjoined the county from interfering with the landowner's construction of the barn.


OVERVIEW: The landowner sought to erect a training barn for show horses on a seven-acre parcel of property. The county claimed that its zoning ordinance denied agricultural exemptions for property less than 15 acres and that the training of horses was not an agricultural purpose. The landowner claimed that the county had no authority to impose the 15-acre limitation on property that was entitled to a statutory agricultural exemption. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the county's power to regulate the landowner's property rights through zoning regulations was expressly limited by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 34, para. 3151 (1975), that the rearing of livestock was an agricultural purpose, that horses were livestock, that the landowner's use of the property was agricultural, and that the county had no authority to establish acreage minimums or to require the landowner to obtain building and special use permits. The court also held that the county's zoning ordinance was invalid and that the care and training of horses for show was within the contemplation of para. 3151.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment enjoining the county from interfering with the landowner's construction of the barn.

 

1657 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Petrie v. Illinois High School Asso.


No. 15362


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


75 Ill. App. 3d 980; 394 N.E.2d 855; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3173; 31 Ill. Dec. 653



September 6, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. ROGER H. LITTLE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Champaign County, Illinois, dismissed plaintiff male student's lawsuit for gender discrimination against defendant school for not allowing the student to play on the girl's volleyball team. The student appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court reasoned that the prohibitions against boys were classifications based on sex but were justified because they preserved, fostered and increased athletic competition for girls and prevented unfair competition. The court noted that girls were generally at a substantial physical disadvantage in playing volleyball and that classification of a high school volleyball team to limit its membership to girls was consistent with a long-standing tradition in sports of setting up classifications whereby persons having characteristics likely to make them more proficient were eliminated from certain classes of competition. The court held that to furnish exactly the same athletic opportunities to boys as to girls would be most difficult and detrimental to the compelling governmental interest of equalizing athletic opportunities. The court recognized that Ill. Const. art. I, § 18 imposed a stiffer test than federal constitutional requirements, but considered the equalization of general athletic opportunities to be the essence of the application of that section to the public schools of the State and to be a practical, though not absolute, necessity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1658 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Chicago v. Abdullah


No. 78-695


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


76 Ill. App. 3d 325; 395 N.E.2d 50; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3242; 32 Ill. Dec. 103



September 4, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. BEN EDELSTEIN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of the improper display of a Chicago flag insignia in violation of Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code ch. 173, § 173-9 (1977) after a bench trial and fined him $ 25. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the municipal ordinance as unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant worked as a special police officer in a day care center. A police officer testified that on June 15, 1977, he arrested defendant because he was wearing what appeared to be a special police uniform, and on his right sleeve, he was wearing the official patch of the Chicago Police Department. Section 173-9 of the Municipal Code of Chicago provided that every special policeman had to wear a suitable badge, not in the form of a star, which had to be issued to him by the superintendent of police. Although the testimony of the officer suggested that he presented the official patch of the Chicago Police Department to the trial court, the patch was not admitted into evidence. There was no suggestion that the trial court inspected or examined any physical evidence. The prosecution also failed to introduce evidence that showed that defendant had not received the necessary approval to wear the uniform with the patch. The court reversed the conviction without deciding the constitutionality of the ordinance. The court held that the prosecution had failed to establish that defendant had violated the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1659 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Chicago Title & Trust Co. v. Tully


No. 78-1119


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


76 Ill. App. 3d 336; 395 N.E.2d 42; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3244; 32 Ill. Dec. 95



September 4, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied September 25, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RAYMOND S. SARNOW, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a trustee and land trust beneficiaries, sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, the Assessor of Cook County, a deputy assessor, and commissioners. The lower court had held that adjudication of the issues asserted by plaintiffs, in their action challenging the valuation and resulting assessment of their property, was barred by a prior judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that plaintiffs' suit was a collateral action and was barred either by public policy or by res judicata. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment for defendants. The court found that plaintiffs' case was barred by res judicata by virtue of a judgment entered on a collector's application. The court noted that plaintiffs had not pursued their statutory remedy under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 716 (1977) of objecting to the collector's application and were thus bound by the judgment and order of sale. The court rejected plaintiffs' argument that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 578 and 597 (1977) unconstitutionally delegated legislative powers because assessment officials were authorized to revise assessments as should appear to them "just." The court also rejected plaintiffs' argument that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 675 (1977) was unconstitutional as applied. The court stated that if there were any irregularities in the hearings afforded to plaintiffs or the method of valuation, they would have been only procedural and would not have rendered the assessment one "unauthorized by law" which might have exempted plaintiffs' from pursing their statutory remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision granting summary judgment in favor of defendants on the ground that plaintiffs' suit challenging the valuation and resulting assessment of their property was barred by a prior judgment.

 

1660 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Melbourne Corp. v. Chicago


No. 78-465


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


76 Ill. App. 3d 595; 394 N.E.2d 1291; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3272; 31 Ill. Dec. 914



September 4, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied October 15, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ABRAHAM W. BRUSSELL and the HON. REGINALD J. HOLZER, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed and cross-appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found it liable and awarded damages in appellee nursing home's action for damages resulting from the city's denial of renewal of its city nursing home license and from the city's failure to comply with a circuit court order mandating issuance of the city nursing home license. The nursing home cross-appealed seeking damages for loss of profits.


OVERVIEW: The nursing home alleged that the city, through its licensing board, failed to renew its license based upon an ordinance later adjudged unconstitutional. The court reversed the judgment because the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, paras. 1 -- 101 et seq. (1971), precluded liability and held (1) the "constitutional tort" doctrine did not apply, and the Act was applicable because the city's action did not constitute a knowing or malicious violation of the nursing home's clearly established constitutional rights; (2) the city could assert any immunity granted to an employee, in this case its licensing board, to preclude its own liability; (3) the city was immune because its licensing determination constituted discretionary action; (4) the legislative classification within the Act, which provided immunity to local public entity licensing decisions but not for the state, was rationally designed to further a legitimate purpose, and (5) contempt remedies were not available because the nursing home was required to seek its remedy from the court which issued the injunction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment on the issue of liability. Accordingly, contentions concerning damages were not addressed.

Carbondale ex rel. Ham v. Eckert


Nos. 78-428, 78-552, 78-536 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


76 Ill. App. 3d 881; 395 N.E.2d 607; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3312; 32 Ill. Dec. 377



August 31, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied September 27, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County; the Hon. THOMAS W. HANEY, the Hon. BROCTON LOCKWOOD, and the Hon. RICHARD E. RICHMAN, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant buyers and dismissed the actions that were brought by taxpayers on behalf of the city, contesting the city's sales of certain real estate to the buyers under the provisions of Carbondale, Ill., Ordinance 1651 (Sept. 14, 1971).


OVERVIEW: The city passed an ordinance allowing it to sell parcels of urban renewal property for redevelopment. The taxpayers filed suits contesting the resulting sales. The circuit court entered judgment in favor of the buyers, and the court affirmed. The court upheld the ordinance and the sales of property, finding that (1) the city became a home rule municipality that could perform any function relating to its government and its affairs; (2) the ordinance expressly authorized the sales pursuant to the city's home rule powers and compliance with Department of Housing and Urban Development guidelines, which contained no requirement of public sale of property that was held for a certain period; and (3) urban renewal matters were matters of local government affairs and were not limited by the general assembly under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(g), (h), (i).


OUTCOME: The court upheld the ordinance and affirmed the judgment.

 

1662 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Flatt


No. 78-197


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


75 Ill. App. 3d 930; 394 N.E.2d 1049; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3164; 31 Ill. Dec. 731



August 29, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. STEPHEN J. COVEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state filed an interlocutory appeal pursuant to § 114 -- 12 of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 114 -- 12 (1977) of the order of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion in limine to suppress fingerprint evidence in a burglary trial because the state had not preserved a piece of glass from which the police lifted defendant's fingerprints.


OVERVIEW: Police technicians lifted the fingerprints from a broken window that the owner of the premises subsequently discarded. On appeal, the court addressed the threshold question of whether the order was appealable by the state under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(a)(1), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110A, para. 604(a)(1) (1977), because the suppression was not based on an involuntary confession or an unlawful search and seizure. The court noted that the motion was based on an alleged deprivation of the constitutional rights to due process and a fair trial and held that the state may appeal an order that had the substantive effect of suppressing evidence. The court then reversed and held that it was not a violation of defendant's due process rights for the state to fail to preserve the object from which latent fingerprints were lifted for defendant's inspection. The court ruled that in the absence of claims that the police forged evidence or framed defendant, it was sufficient that the technician was available for cross-examination, and the fingerprint card was available for inspection by defense experts. The court found that the preservation of objects would be impractical and burdensome.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court that suppressed the fingerprint evidence, and the court remanded the cause for trial.

 

1663 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Galati


No. 78-423


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


75 Ill. App. 3d 860; 393 N.E.2d 744; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3155; 30 Ill. Dec. 708



August 28, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. HELEN C. KINNEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his two to six years' sentence in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), after a jury trial, for one count of theft over $ 150 and one count of theft under $ 150.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the theft of a bicycle and a moped. After being convicted by a jury, defendant elected to be sentenced under the laws that existed at the time of his offense. Defendant claimed that the trial judge enhanced his sentence based on her belief that he had committed perjury during the trial and improperly required him to elect sentencing without advising him of the sentence. The court affirmed defendant's sentence. The court held that the trial judge explained the range of sentences under the laws that existed at the time of the offense and the laws in effect at the time of sentencing, that the judge was not required to disclose defendant's particular sentence, that defendant's sentencing followed the requirements of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 1001-1-2(a), 1005-3-2(a)(3) (1977), and that the trial judge did not sentence defendant for the additional offense of perjury. The court also held that the substantial disparity in a co-defendant's sentence did not justify a reduction in defendant's sentence under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(b)(4), that defendant's sentence was based on proper factors, and that the trial judge did not abuse her discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's two to six years' sentence for two counts of theft.

 

1664 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Paramount Consulting Agency, Inc. v. Johnson


No. 78-219


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


75 Ill. App. 3d 749; 394 N.E.2d 672; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3139; 31 Ill. Dec. 470



August 24, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CURRY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff employment agency's action pursuant to 110 Ill. Comp. Stat. 264-279 (1975), the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) affirmed the decision of defendant Department of Labor (department) to revoke the employment agency's license to operate a private employment agency. The trial court denied the department's motion to dismiss the action and held that 48 Ill. Comp. Stat. 197i (1973) was unconstitutional. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The department's seven-count complaint against the employment agency alleged numerous violations of the private employment agencies act, 111 Ill. Comp. Stat. 197a-197o (1973) including false or misleading and blind newspaper ads and invoices to employers as well as failing to personally interview applicants and to send referral slips to the prospective employers and applications. The employment agency alleged that the department's decision was against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court affirmed the trial court and held that the department's order revoking the employment agency's license was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The employment agency's appeal focused on a redetermination of the credibility of the witnesses, but the court's review was limited to whether or not the agency's decision was against the manifest weight of the evidence. The trial court erred in its sua sponte determination that 48 Ill. Comp. Stat. 197i (1973) was unconstitutional. The employment agency did not challenge the constitutionality of the statute or allege that the requirement to pay for the transcript violated its constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders denying the department's motion to dismiss and affirming the department's order revoking the employment agency's license to operate a private employment agency. The court reversed the trial court's ruling that the statute requiring the employment agency to pay the cost of transcribing the department's record was unconstitutional and remanded to the trial court to determine the costs to each party.

In re Marriage of Thompson


No. 78-1720


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


79 Ill. App. 3d 310; 398 N.E.2d 17; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3707; 34 Ill. Dec. 342



August 22, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Opinion Filed on Denial of Rehearing December 19, 1979, Reported at 79 Ill. App. 3d 310 at 317.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ALBERT S. PORTER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which after granting a divorce and custody of the parties' children to appellee ex-wife, made a distribution of the parties' marital property under the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, paras. 101-802 (1977).


OVERVIEW: The ex-wife was granted a divorce and custody of the parties' children. Subsequently, the trial court made a disposition of the parties' marital property pursuant to the Act. The ex-wife was awarded the marital residence, subject to the ex-husband's lien interest. The ex-husband appealed, contending that the Act under which the property distribution was made was unconstitutional because it covered more than one subject in violation of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d), that the trial court erred in its child support order, and in determining his marital residence interest. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part, ruling that all of the provisions of the Act related to domestic relations and were necessary to accomplish the Act's legislative purpose. Thus, they did not violate the constitutional single subject requirement. However, the trial court's finding of an arrearage in child support was incorrect. The court concluded that the ex-husband was entitled to one-half interest in the marital residence when it was sold, rather than the fixed amount awarded by the trial court because fairness required that he shared in any appreciation of his interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment ordering the ex-husband to pay all of the future medical expenses of the minor children, reversed the finding that he was in arrears for child support, and reversed the fixed award of interest to the ex-husband in the marital residence, holding that the ex-husband was entitled to a one-half interest in the marital property at the time of its sale.

 

1666 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Boucher


No. 78-131


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


75 Ill. App. 3d 322; 394 N.E.2d 60; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3073; 31 Ill. Dec. 144



August 21, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. IVAN L. YONTZ, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of felony escape.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of felony escape for escaping from a penal institution while awaiting trial for a charge of arson. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. Defendant argued that the felony status of the crime was unconstitutional because an escape while awaiting a trial on a misdemeanor charge was only a misdemeanor. The court explained that defendant was subsequently found guilty of the arson charge, so defendant was not in a position to challenge the constitutionality of the felony escape charge. The court held that defendant's conduct clearly violated Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 31--6 (1977). The court determined that the legislature had the authority to establish the criminal statutes and corresponding sentences for crimes, and the court would not interfere with the legislature's actions unless the acts shocked the moral sense of the community.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which convicted defendant of felony escape.

 

1667 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Barrington Hills v. Hoffman Estates


No. 78-1944


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


75 Ill. App. 3d 461; 394 N.E.2d 599; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3098; 31 Ill. Dec. 397



August 21, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RAYMOND K. BERG,Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff municipalities appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted the motion to dismiss plaintiffs' complaint filed by defendants, municipality, realty company, and other related property owners. The complaint alleged that defendants' adoption of the zoning ordinances and construction of a theater created a nuisance and interfered with the present character of development in the area.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs objected to defendants' plans to build an open air theatre on land in close proximity to them. The court reasoned that to establish standing to challenge a zoning decision determining the use to which defendants' property may be put, plaintiffs had to prove that they suffered a special damages by reason of such use that differed from that suffered by the general public. Plaintiffs had to be persons interested in the controversy and possess a personal claim, status, or right which was capable of being affected. On appeal, the court affirmed defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint. The court reasoned that plaintiffs lacked standing to litigate the validity of the zoning ordinance. The court did not find that plaintiffs' allegations of decreased economic value of their property and that the proposed development would adversely affect their street systems satisfied the standing requirement. Plaintiffs needed to show that the ordinance would have had a demonstratively unique impact and effect on its proprietary functions to give it a real interest in the subject matter of the controversy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of defendants' motion to dismiss plaintiffs' challenge to defendants' zoning decision.

 

1668 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Galich v. Catholic Bishop of Chicago


No. 79-664


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


75 Ill. App. 3d 538; 394 N.E.2d 572; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3112; 31 Ill. Dec. 370



August 17, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOSEPH M. WOSIK, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff church members appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted the motion to dismiss filed by defendant Catholic Bishop for lack of subject matter jurisdiction in the church members' suit to enjoin the Catholic Bishop from closing and demolishing a certain church to which the Catholic Bishop held the record title.


OVERVIEW: An application to preserve the church property as a landmark was pending and the Catholic Bishop decided to close and demolish the church because of the cost of needed repairs, the utility of the building, and the availability of priests. The church members' action to stop the closing and demolition was dismissed. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the church members had no protectible property rights in the church building because there was no statutory trust created and no implied covenant requiring the property to be used for church purposes. The court held that the First Amendment, as applied to the states through the Fourteenth Amendment, precluded examination of the merits of the church members' claim because the decision to close and demolish the church were matters of church government and as such were ecclesiastical in nature and the mere assertion of a property right was not sufficient to invest a civil court with jurisdiction over what was essentially a religious dispute. The court concluded that the decision was within the exclusive province of the Catholic Bishop, subject only to the decision of the Pope and, therefore, the court lacked jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the church members' suit to enjoin the Catholic Bishop from closing and demolishing a certain church in favor of the Catholic Bishop.

 

1669 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hamelin


No. 78-1028


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


75 Ill. App. 3d 445; 394 N.E.2d 566; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3095; 31 Ill. Dec. 364



August 15, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ANTHONY J. SCOTILLO, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found defendant guilty of indecent liberties with a child and contributing to the sexual delinquency of a child. Judgment was entered on the indecent-liberties verdict, and defendant was sentenced to a term of four to six years.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found defendant guilty of indecent liberties with a child and contributing to the sexual delinquency of a child. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's contention that the evidence was insufficient to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The victim's testimony was substantially corroborated. The victim's prompt complaint to her family and police, her torn brassiere, her disheveled appearance and tearful behavior after leaving defendant's car, and defendant's thrown rugs found at the scene of the incident were all factors which substantially corroborated the victim's testimony and demonstrated that it was clear and convincing. Any shortcoming in the victim's testimony merely went to her credibility as determined by the jury. Further, the court held that the trial judge properly required defense counsel, for the purpose of establishing a proper foundation, to ask the witness whether she understood that she was to write down all important conversations. Even if there were error regarding the impeachment by omission, it was not grounds for reversal since it did not result in manifest prejudice to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1670 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Palcek v. Chicago Heights


No. 78-1744


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


74 Ill. App. 3d 702; 393 N.E.2d 1218; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2799; 30 Ill. Dec. 871



August 9, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that was in favor of defendant city. The police officer's action concerned his discharge. He contended that the discharge was arbitrary and that a statement was improperly used at a hearing.


OVERVIEW: The city's fire and police commissioners' board found that the police officer had taken goods from a store. At a restaurant, a lieutenant asked the police officer about the goods. The police officer stated that he stole the goods. After the two went to the lieutenant's house, the police officer made verbal and written statements to the same effect. There was a hearing before the board. The board discharged the police officer. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case. To avoid equal protection implications regarding warnings before interrogations, the requirements under the Municipal Code of 1961 at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 10-1-18 (1977) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 10-1-18.1 (1977) had to be read as incorporated into Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 10-2.1-17 (1977). At the restaurant, the lieutenant never apprised the police officer of the offense the police officer allegedly committed, failed to tell the police officer that any statements could be used for disciplinary purposes, and did not inform the police officer to his right to counsel at questioning. Therefore, the police officer's statements were improperly admitted at the hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that was for the city and remanded the action.

 

1671 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Drogolewicz v. Quern


No. 78-1247


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


74 Ill. App. 3d 862; 393 N.E.2d 1212; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2820; 30 Ill. Dec. 865; 19 A.L.R.4th 136



August 9, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CURRY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which upheld defendant state public aid department's decision denying him Medicaid benefits.


OVERVIEW: The applicant was severely disabled. While in the hospital, the applicant gave $ 6,000 to his children. The applicant then sought Medicaid benefits, applying for the same with the state public aid department. The public aid department denied his benefits, alleging that he had transferred property for inadequate consideration to obtain public aid. The applicant appealed to the trial court, which affirmed. The applicant appealed and the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the Social Security Act expressly forbade the blanket disqualification procedure of § 3-1.3 of the Illinois Public Aid Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, art. III, para. 3-1.3 (1977). The court found that non-available assets could not have been deemed available, and that the availability of specific assets could not have been given a currency beyond their actual value by a failure to have applied their worth to the debt in question. The court found that the five-year ineligibility provision of § 3-1.3 of the Illinois Public Aid Code and the state public aid department's regulation promulgated under it violative of the Social Security Act and the supremacy clause of the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court and remanded the cause to the state public aid department for a redetermination of the applicant's eligibility for Medicaid, taking into account only the actual value of the asset he transferred and providing assistance for any medical expenses that may still have been owing after such a computation.

People v. Anderson


No. 15169


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


74 Ill. App. 3d 363; 392 N.E.2d 938; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2890; 30 Ill. Dec. 173

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. HAROLD L. JENSEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) that was entered upon jury verdicts and the several sentences imposed for unlawful possession of cannabis, possession of more than 500 grams of cannabis with intent to deliver, possession of more than 30 grams of cocaine, possession of more than 30 grams of cocaine with intent to deliver, possession of MDA, and possession of methaqualone.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his convictions for unlawful possession of cannabis, possession of more than 500 grams of cannabis with intent to deliver, possession of more than 30 grams of cocaine, possession of more than 30 grams of cocaine with intent to deliver, possession of MDA, and possession of methaqualone. The court reversed in part because the prosecution conceded that the convictions for unlawful possession of cocaine and the unlawful possession of marijuana were improperly entered. Affirming the remaining judgments of convictions, the court stated in part that probable cause to support the issuance of a search warrant was shown by the affidavits of two police officers, which detailed the strict search and surveillance of an informant and his return with a supply of cocaine. The court rejected the argument that defendant's conclusory denial of the purchase of cocaine by the informant as alleged in his affidavit constituted a sufficient challenge to the credibility of the officers upon the hypothesis that they could not have received "that which defendant did not sell."

Champaign v. Elliott


No. 15256


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


73 Ill. App. 3d 373; 391 N.E.2d 1099; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2904; 29 Ill. Dec. 416



July 3, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. HAROLD L. JENSEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which found him guilty of violating Champaign, Ill., Municipal Code § 13-6(a)(5) (1975) and which denied his motion to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: Defendant rented a house, which was listed for sale, and defendant granted permission for potential buyers to go into the house to view it at defendant's convenience. A salesperson, who was African American, came to the house to show it, but when he saw her, defendant refused to allow her into the house based upon her race. The salesperson filed a complaint with the Fair Housing Board, which found that defendant had violated § 13-6(a)(5). The city then instituted legal action against defendant, and he was found guilty. Defendant alleged that his actions did not constitute a violation of the ordinance and that it was unconstitutional. In reversing the decision, the court stated that § 13-6(a)(5) was to be strictly construed because it was punitive in nature. To be guilty of an unlawful real estate practice under § 13-6(a)(5), the city had to establish that the disposition of the property was prohibited to any person because of race, color, religion, or national origin and that defendant knowingly acted or undertook to act with respect to the property. The court held that there was no proof in the record that the disposition was prohibited on the basis of defendant's acts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment of conviction.

 

1674 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Wright v. County of Winnebago


No. 77-359


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


73 Ill. App. 3d 337; 391 N.E.2d 772; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2898; 29 Ill. Dec. 347



June 22, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. WILLIAM R. NASH, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which denied their request for injunctive relief and a declaratory judgment against appellee county. The owners claimed that the denial of their request for a special use permit to allow them to use their property as a Restricted Landing Area (RLA) violated the due process clauses of the United States and Illinois Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The owners' property was zoned for agricultural use. They petitioned the county for a special use permit to use the property as an RLA. It was denied. The trial court found the county's denial reasonable. The owners filed a post-trial motion that contended the basis for denying the special use permit had been preempted by state and federal statutes, which was denied. Upon review, the court reversed. It found that trial court's finding that the county had drawn a line and determined a saturation point was erroneous because there was no evidence in the record that such a "line" existed. The owners properly preserved the issues of a local government's power to regulate aircraft noise and safety for review by filing their post-trial motion. The county did not zone properly on the basis of aircraft noise because there were no standards for noise set out in the ordinance and there was no objective determination of the effects of such noise on the owners' neighbors. Because the Illinois State Division of Aeronautics had approved the use of the RLA, the county had to bring forward some objective evidence of a particular safety problem or hazard specific to the owners' RLA.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of the owners' request for injunctive relief and a declaratory judgment against the county because of the county's denial of their request for a special use permit.

Chicago v. Pioneer Towing, Inc.


No. 78-1470


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


73 Ill. App. 3d 867; 392 N.E.2d 132; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3001; 29 Ill. Dec. 575



June 18, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOHN J. McDONNELL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Orders reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed from judgments of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which had sustained the motions to quash filed by defendants, towing companies, officers, and directors, dismissed complaints alleging violations of the City of Chicago, IL, Mun. Code ch. 27, § 27-381.3, and declared City of Chicago, IL, Mun. Code ch. 27, § 27-381.4, the applicable penalty provision, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The challenged provisions had required towing companies to post signs indicating that unauthorized cars would be towed from premises serviced by the companies. The city argued that the towing companies lacked standing to attack the penalty provision of the ordinance. The court found that: (1) the towing companies had possessed standing to attack the ordinance on constitutional grounds because they were clearly affected by the ordinance's operation; (2) the proscribed conduct was clearly and definitely articulated in the ordinance, which gave sufficient notice for due process purposes; (3) it was possible to impose vicarious liability on the directors and officers without depriving the directors and officers of due process of law; and (4) the ordinance in question was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders sustaining the motions to quash the complaints against the towing companies and held the ordinance in question constitutional.

 

1676 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Ziebell v. Board of Trustees


No. 78-1430


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


73 Ill. App. 3d 894; 392 N.E.2d 101; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3005; 29 Ill. Dec. 544



June 14, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CURRY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant officer challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his mandamus action in which he sought to compel appellee Board of Trustees of the Police Pension Fund to restore his retirement pension to the amount he was receiving prior to the Board's reduction of his pension.


OVERVIEW: In 1973, the law provided a police officer a pension if he had 20 years or more of service and had reached the age of 50, with the pension increased by one percent for each year of service over 20 years, to a maximum limit of 60 percent of his salary prior to retirement. In 1975, the one percent increment was increased to two percent for each additional year of service and the maximum limit was increased to 75 percent of salary. The officer retired in 1973, at age 47, and upon attaining the age of 50, he was given his pension. Originally his pension was based on the 1975 statute; however, it was subsequently reduced to the amount due under the 1973 statute. The officer sought mandamus relief to require the Board to return his pension to the amount under the 1975 state. The trial court dismissed his action and the court affirmed. It found that when the statute was amended to increase pension amounts, deductions from the salaries of police officers also increased. As the officer was not subject to the increased deductions, his construction of the amended statute was unconstitutional, as it would allow him to an increased payment without making additional payments into the fund.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed the officer's mandamus action seeking to compel the Board to restore his retirement pension to the amount he was receiving prior to the Board's reduction of his pension.

Walker v. State Bd. of Elections


Nos. 78-1234, 78-1268 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


72 Ill. App. 3d 877; 391 N.E.2d 507; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2708; 29 Ill. Dec. 244



June 6, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PETITION for review of order of State Board of Elections.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate sought review of a judgment from respondent State Board of Elections, which required him to file reports mandated by the Illinois Campaign Disclosure Act pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 9-22 (1975).


OVERVIEW: The candidate had established organizations to raise funds to retire debts incurred during his gubernatorial campaign. The association filed a complaint with the Board that alleged that the candidate's organization retained campaign contributions in a bank account and decided not to file campaign disclosure reports with the Board as was required pursuant to the Act, Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 9-22 (1975). The Board found after a hearing that the organizations had accepted and disbursed campaign contributions after the effective date of the Act, therefore the candidate was in violation of the Act's reporting requirements and should have been mandated to file these reports. The court affirmed on appeal. The court held that the Act required that all political committees that received funds in excess of $ 1,000 were to have filed a statement with the Board pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, paras. 9-1.9, 9-10 (1975) because the Act was designed to require full public disclosure of the amounts of campaign contributions. The court rejected the candidate's contention that he was not bound by the Act because he was not a declared candidate after the date it went into effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding of the Board that the candidate had violated the reporting requirements of the Illinois Campaign Disclosure Act and that he should have been made to file campaign contribution disclosure reports.

Rawlings v. Illinois Dep't of Law Enforcement


No. 78-268


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


73 Ill. App. 3d 267; 391 N.E.2d 758; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2750; 29 Ill. Dec. 333



June 5, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County; the Hon. JOHN DONALD O'SHEA, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Illinois Department of Law Enforcement denied plaintiff applicant's application for a firearm owner's identification card based on §§ 4 and 8 of the Firearms Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 83-4, 83-8 (1977). The Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois) affirmed. The applicant appealed pursuant to § 13 of the Administrative Review Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 276 (1977), challenging the constitutionality of the Act.


OVERVIEW: The Department denied the applicant a firearm owner's identification card under §§ 4 and 8 of the Act on the ground that the applicant had been in a mental institution within the past five years. The trial court affirmed and assessed costs against the applicant. The applicant appealed, challenging the constitutionality of §§ 4 and 8 of the Act. On appeal, the court held (1) §§ 4 and 8 of the Act did not violate the applicant's right to due process because § 10 of the Act allowed an aggrieved party to appeal to the Department's director, requesting a hearing; (2) §§ 4 and 8 of the Act did not impermissibly create an irrebutable presumption under the Due Process Clause of the U.S. Constitution because the continued viability of the irrebuttable presumption doctrine was of considerable doubt; (3) the classification of persons who had been in mental institutions within the past five years did not violate the Equal Protection Clause of the U.S. Constitution or the Constitution of the State of Illinois because status as a mental patient was not a suspect class; and (4) the applicant was not liable for costs pursuant to § 5 of the Costs Statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 33, para. 5 (1977).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment to the extent that it upheld the constitutionality of the relevant sections of the Firearms Act. The court reversed the trial court's judgment to the extent that it assessed costs against the applicant.

People v. Dean


No. 78-369


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


73 Ill. App. 3d 501; 392 N.E.2d 57; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2930; 29 Ill. Dec. 500



June 4, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. GEORGE J. MORAN, JR., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged her conviction by the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) for three counts of gambling.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that her reliance upon an order of the Illinois Appellate Court, which enjoined the State from enforcing the provisions of the Illinois Horse Racing Act of 1975, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 8, paras. 37-39.1 (1977), justified her belief that her conduct was not illegal. On appeal, the court reversed defendant's conviction upon finding that the evidence was insufficient to sustain a finding that she was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court noted that the appellate court order in question had been entered in a civil action brought by defendant's employer, an off-track messenger services for horse bettors. Despite the fact that the appellate court's order did not apply to the criminal statute prohibiting gambling, defendant, a lay person, reasonably believed that, by virtue of the order, her questioned employment activities were protected from interference by the State. The spirit of the rule of the statutory defense of reliance, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 4-8(b)(3) (1977), had been abridged where defendant's testimony established that she carried out her employment duties in the reasonable belief that her duties were not unlawful in reliance on the order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and defendant's conviction of gambling.

W. Side Org. Health Servs. Corp. v. Thompson


No. 77-1386


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


73 Ill. App. 3d 179; 391 N.E.2d 392; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3917; 29 Ill. Dec. 129



May 31, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOSEPH M. WOSIK, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed and case was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a health services corporation, individuals, and a judge, challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their action, brought on behalf of operators of drug abuse treatment programs, certain drug addicts, and resident-taxpayers, to prevent defendant state executive branch officials from withholding funds appropriated by the general assembly for the use of the Dangerous Drugs Commission (DDC).


OVERVIEW: The DDC was charged with the responsibility of administering drug abuse treatment programs. The complaint alleged that the general assembly had passed an appropriations bill that included a line item amount to be used by the DDC for the purchase of drug abuse treatment services. The Governor, through his agent, reserved a specific amount of this appropriation for state budgetary reasons. Plaintiffs sought to prevent the Governor and his agents from interfering with the allotment and expenditure of funds. On appeal, the court held that the important issue was whether the appropriations act authorized the Governor to reserve part of the funds essentially eliminating them from the DDC budget and circumventing the commission's discretionary decision making power. The court held that there was no statutory basis for permitting the Governor to withhold the funds. The court reasoned that the general assembly was vested with the ultimate authority to determine the level and allocation of public spending. The court held that the Governor was given no express authority by the state constitution to reserve appropriated funds in frustration of the general assembly's expressed intent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remand the case for further proceedings.

Phillips Petro. Co. v. Pollution Control Bd.

Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District

May 24, 1979, Filed
