DISPOSITION: Order reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner petroleum company sought review of an order of respondent Pollution Control Board (Illinois), which found that the petroleum company and defendant transportation company had violated § 9(a) of the Environmental Protection Act (EPA), codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1009(a) (1975). Respondent Illinois Environmental Protection Agency had filed a compliant against the petroleum company and the transportation company.


OVERVIEW: A tank car owned by the petroleum company, which was filled with anhydrous ammonia, derailed. The tank car was punctured and the chemical was released into the air. The immediate area was evacuated. Some property damage occurred and some individuals suffered physical reactions from exposure to the gas. Respondent Illinois Environmental Protection Agency filed an action against the petroleum company and the transportation company, which maintained control over the tank car until the derailment. The Board found that the petroleum company and the transportation company violated § 9(a) of the EPA. The petroleum company appealed. In reversing as to the petroleum company, the court held that (1) the Board had jurisdiction to hear the case because it dealt with a matter of local regulation regarding air pollution; (2) the record did not show any admissible evidence that indicated that the petroleum company exercised sufficient control over the source of the pollution in such a way as to have caused, threatened, or allowed the pollution; and (3) it was error to find that the petroleum company violated § 9a of the EPA.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Pollution Control Board's judgment, which found a violation of the Environmental Protection Act as to the petroleum company only.

Kraus v. Board of Trustees


No. 78-525


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


72 Ill. App. 3d 833; 390 N.E.2d 1281; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2702; 28 Ill. Dec. 691



May 22, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the board of trustees of the police pension fund, appealed from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied its motion to reconsider an order of the circuit court wherein that court reversed a decision of the board regarding pension benefits payable to plaintiff policeman. The policeman asserted entitlement to a pension under Ill. Rev. Stat. § 3-114 (1971), and protected by Ill. Const. art. XIII, § 5.


OVERVIEW: The policeman worked for 11 years as a patrolman and then was placed on disability, at which time the policeman ceased making contributions to the police pension fund and began receiving a disability pension. Upon retirement, the policeman claimed that under Ill. Rev. Stat. § 3-114 (1971), he was entitled to elect to be paid a regular pension, in lieu of his disability pension, equal to one-half of the salary attached to his rank the year preceding his retirement on regular pension. The board asserted that Ill. Rev. Stat. § 3-116.1 (1973), which repealed § 3-114, applied, and that the policeman's regular pension was equal to one-half of the salary attached to his rank at the date of his retirement on disability pension. In affirming the lower court, the court held that § 3-116.1 could not constitutionally apply to the policeman, and that he was entitled to receive benefits under the relevant sections of the Pension Code as in effect at the time the constitutional provision became effective. The court held that the purpose of Ill. Const. art. XIII, § 5, was to guarantee that the policeman would receive not less than the benefits the policeman would receive under that pension.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Rosewell v. Bulk Terminals Co.


Nos. 78-748, 78-749, 78-750


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


73 Ill. App. 3d 225; 390 N.E.2d 1294; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3911; 28 Ill. Dec. 704



May 22, 1979, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ROBERT J. DEMPSEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant county treasurer applied for judgment and for the determination of the correct amount of real estate taxes paid under protest by objectors, real property lessees, in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). The trial court entered a judgment in the treasurer's favor and the lessees appealed.


OVERVIEW: The principal issues on appeal where whether the assessor's imposition of a back tax on the lessees' leasehold estates was valid and whether the assessed value of one of the leasehold interests was excessive and constructively fraudulent. The court held that: (1) the back tax assessments would be authorized if the property in question was omitted from assessment or was defectively described or assessed; (2) a rational basis was evident for the statutory scheme challenged and there was no denial of any constitutional right; (3) because the lessee failed to contradict the assessor's valuation by clear and convincing evidence that the market rental of similarly improved property was much less, the trial court properly denied the valuation relief sought by the lessee; (4) whether the lessee owned the improvements or leased them, it was the market rental for the land as improved, rather than the contractual rent or the market rental for unimproved land, that was the appropriate basis for computing the fair cash value of the leasehold; and (5) the lessee had not sustained its burden of demonstrating by clear and convincing evidence that the original assessment was fraudulently excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Peoples


No. 78-480


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


71 Ill. App. 3d 842; 390 N.E.2d 554; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2554; 28 Ill. Dec. 387



May 18, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. JOHN F. MICHELA, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois), which convicted him of burglary and sentenced him to a term of from two to six years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant challenged the sufficiency of the election given him by the trial court on "due process" and "equal protection" grounds. The court found no support for the defense position that the election statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch., para. 1008-2-4(b), (1978), required a defendant be given a choice between specific sentences. Defendant was informed of his right to elect under which law he would have been sentenced, and he was also informed of the differences and consequences, which would have flowed from an election under either sentencing law. Defendant's election, so far as the trial court needed to provide, was a knowing and informed one. The two classes of persons identified by the defense as similarly situated were differently situated so far as applying the sentencing laws was concerned. There was no denial of due process or equal protection to the person situated, as was defendant, who had elected to be sentenced under the sentencing law in effect at the time of his offense. Regardless of the ultimate construction of § 3-3-2.1 of the Unified Code of Corrections, the court found no lack of due process or equal protection in the legislation under consideration.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction and sentences.

 

1685 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Sturm v. Block


No. 78-323


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


72 Ill. App. 3d 306; 390 N.E.2d 912; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2621; 28 Ill. Dec. 553



May 16, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 3, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Bureau County; the Hon. THOMAS R. CLYDESDALE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff horse owners filed an action against defendants state officials, humane society and agents in the Circuit Court of Bureau County (Illinois). The horse owners sought declaratory relief with respect to certain portions of the Humane Care for Animals Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1977, ch. 8, pars. 701-716, and damages. The trial court dismissed the complaint for declaratory relief and the horse owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court based its decision upon the failure of the horse owners to pursue review remedies set forth in the Administrative Review Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1977, ch. 110, pars. 264-279. The court found that the authorization for impoundment of the horse owners' horses and the impoundment by the state agency was not a final administrative action by the agency. Rather, that action was subject to further administrative review procedures within the agency. Therefore, the decision in the case was not a final administrative decision authorizing judicial review under the Administrative Review Act, and the trial court's conclusions that it was a final decision and that the failure of the horse owners to pursue review waived their right to review was clearly erroneous. The court further held that the administrative review procedures available to the horse owners under the agency's rules and regulations afforded them an adequate remedy within which to challenge the actions they complained of. Since they failed to pursue the administrative remedies available to them, they could not obtain judicial review in the courts in this proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1686 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Clark


Nos. 77-445, 77-446 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


71 Ill. App. 3d 381; 389 N.E.2d 911; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2478; 27 Ill. Dec. 680



May 4, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 4, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. JOHN A. KRAUSE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a former county treasurer and banker, were convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) on charges including bribery, violation of a county treasurer's act, official misconduct, and corrupt practices in connection with an arrangement under which the treasurer caused public funds to be deposited in the banker's institutions in return for favorable personal credit terms. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The treasurer and the banker appealed their convictions for bribery, corruption, official misconduct, and violation of the County Treasurer's Act (CTA). The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court rejected challenges to the CTA's imposition of sanctions based on county population, finding that its classification was reasonable and that its prohibition against payment of "fees, perquisites and emoluments" adequately described targeted conduct. Venue was proper in the place where the treasurer served. The court upheld the lower court's refusal to sever the trials, rejected various claims of evidentiary errors as meritless or harmless, approved the denial of a continuance, found no errors as to venire, and turned away a statute of limitations claim. Challenges to jury instructions were also rejected. However, the court reversed the treasurer's CTA and corruption convictions because the indictment failed to charge a culpable mental state. Finding that the remaining convictions for misconduct (the treasurer) and for bribery (the banker) were based on the same underlying conduct as the more specific charges, the court reversed the convictions for the more general offenses.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the treasurer's conviction for violating the CTA, for violating the corrupt practices act, and on counts of official misconduct, and affirmed his conviction for bribery. The court also reversed the banker's convictions for bribery and affirmed his convictions for violating the county treasurer's act.

Layfer v. Tucker


No. 77-490


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


71 Ill. App. 3d 333; 389 N.E.2d 252; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2366; 27 Ill. Dec. 440



May 3, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. LLOYD A. VAN DEUSEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants Illinois Attorney General and Illinois State Treasurer appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which ordered the counties to pay plaintiff taxpayers their attorney's fees out of a tax fund set up by the county treasurer.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed a class action suit on behalf of Illinois taxpayers residing outside of the county. The complaint sought to hold that the provisions of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 394 (1973), § 21 of the Inheritance and Transfer Tax Law, were unconstitutional due to the adoption of Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(a). In a related suit the Illinois Supreme Court found the statutory provision in question to be unconstitutional. The circuit court therefore granted a judgment on the pleadings to the taxpayers, order the county to file an accounting of the funds, enjoined the county from transferring or disposing of these funds, and, in a later order, awarded attorneys' fees to the taxpayer. The award of attorneys' fees was appealed. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision to award attorney's fees. The court held that the money from which the attorney's fees were to be paid were the property of the State, so that the State had standing to appeal. The court further held that the State had not waived its sovereign immunity to permit any court other than the court of claims to grant a judgment against the State's funds.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court, which had ordered the county to pay the taxpayers' attorney's fees out of funds that belonged to the State of Illinois.

People v. McNair


No. 78-566


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


71 Ill. App. 3d 782; 390 N.E.2d 142; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2545; 28 Ill. Dec. 160



May 1, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. EARL E. STRAYHORN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered judgment convicting defendant of burglary and unlawful use of a weapon in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 19-1, 24-1(a)(10), and 24-1(b) (1977). Following sentencing, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: While completing an arrest in a resident hotel, a police officer observed a man pointing a rifle through a partially opened door. The officer and others entered the apartment behind the door and discovered defendant and two others. Defendant was subsequently arrested. An investigation revealed a gun dropped by defendant was stolen in a burglary. On appeal, defendant contended that the State failed to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt because the evidence of his possession of the proceeds from the recent burglary did not support the inference that he committed burglary beyond a reasonable doubt. In addition, he asserted the State failed to demonstrate that when arrested carrying a loaded weapon, defendant was not in his own abode as required by statute. The court affirmed the two convictions for burglary and unlawful use of a weapon because the State sustained its burden of proving defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court, however, remanded because the failure to impose two sentences rendered the judgment of convictions incomplete.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered upon the convictions for burglary and unlawful use of a weapon. The court also affirmed the one sentence imposed. However, the court remanded with directions to clarify the record as to which offense sentence was imposed and for entry of a second sentence for the conviction upon which no sentence was previously imposed.

 

1689 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Rockford Drop Forge Co. v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 73-293


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


71 Ill. App. 3d 295; 389 N.E.2d 212; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2362; 27 Ill. Dec. 400



April 30, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for review of order of Pollution Control Board.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner companies sought review of stationary source noise emission regulations which were adopted by respondent Pollution Control Board (PCB) pursuant to title VI of the Environmental Protection Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, paras. 1023-1025 (1973).


OVERVIEW: The companies which operated forging facilities within the state brought the petition. The companies challenged the stationary source noise emission regulations promulgated by the PCB, claiming that title VI of the Act and the regulations, themselves, were unconstitutional. The court held that the regulations were valid and affirmed them. Pursuant to § 29 of the Act, the court's review was limited only to the rules and regulations promulgated by the PCB. Nowhere was there authority for the court to consider, as a trial court of original jurisdiction, a challenge to title VI of the Act. Thus, the court was without jurisdiction to consider the constitutionality of title VI of the Act. Pursuant to case law precedent, the stationary noise source regulations did not violate equal protection. The appropriate standard of review of the PCB regulations was whether they were arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable. Thus, the court was without authority to reweigh the evidence and invalidate the regulations. No federal act expressly reserved the exclusive power to regulate the field of noise control. Thus, there was no express or implied preemption.


OUTCOME: The court held that the regulations promulgated by the PCB for the control of stationary source noise emissions were valid and, therefore, were affirmed.

 

1690 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Gerage v. Dixon


No. 78-885


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


71 Ill. App. 3d 645; 390 N.E.2d 122; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2516; 28 Ill. Dec. 140



April 30, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CURRY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trucking company challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the decision of defendant Secretary of State to revoke the trucking company's vehicle registration for failure to pay the required registration fee within the time due and to assess a statutory 25 per cent late fee. The trucking company argued that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 3-704(3) (1977), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Secretary of State revoked the trucking company's vehicle registration for failure to pay the required registration fee within the time due and assessed a 25 per cent late fee. The trucking company filed suit with the circuit court for administrative review of the Secretary's decision. The court held that the trucking company lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 3-704(3) of the Illinois Motor Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 3-704(3) (1977), because it had not been aggrieved by the absence of a hearing provision in the statute. The court found that: (1) the trucking company had been afforded a hearing on the matter and allowed to continue his business pending the outcome of the hearing; (2) § 3-704(3) gave the Secretary the power to suspend or revoke the registration of vehicles when the required fees had not been paid; (3) nothing in the statute or its history indicated that the Secretary should have prorated late fees in order to minimize vehicle registration revocations; and (4) the trucking company failed to tender payment within the time limit prescribed and accordingly subjected his vehicle registrations to suspension or revocation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court that had affirmed the decision of the Secretary of State to revoke the trucking company's vehicle registration.

People v. Althide


No. 78-63


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


71 Ill. App. 3d 963; 389 N.E.2d 240; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2572; 27 Ill. Dec. 428



April 30, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Hancock County; the Hon. U. S. COLLINS and the Hon. SCOTT I. KLUKOS, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the Circuit Court of Hancock County (Illinois) for theft over $ 150 for purchasing eight stolen hogs.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for theft over $ 150 and the court reversed and remanded. The court held that defendant's request for a jury trial was not an unequivocal demand for trial that triggered the 160-day period in which to try defendant under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 103-5(b) (1975). There was sufficient evidence that defendant knew or should have known that the hogs were stolen when he bought them. However, the testimony of the four thieves who sold the hogs to defendant might have been fruit of the poisonous tree and could have been required to be suppressed. The trial court issued an ambiguous suppression order after finding that defendant's statements to the police naming the thieves were involuntary. On remand, the trial court had to determine whether the statements had to be excluded from the trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded defendant's theft conviction.

Horwath v. Parker


No. 77-1387


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


72 Ill. App. 3d 128; 390 N.E.2d 72; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2598; 28 Ill. Dec. 90



April 24, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. DONALD J. O'BRIEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff beneficial owner appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the beneficial owner's complaint against defendants, seller, other owners, and trustee, for failure to exhaust her remedies pursuant to an arbitration agreement. The beneficial owner had sought an injunction to restrain a sale of the property, a termination of the trust, a partition of the property, a declaratory judgment, and damages.


OVERVIEW: The beneficial owner, seller, and other owners shared an interest in property. The seller offered her interest for sale to the beneficial owner and other owners. The beneficial owner objected to the sale to one of the other owners and filed a complaint. The trustee and the seller filed motions to dismiss. One of the other owners filed an answer and requested dismissal. The trial court dismissed the beneficial owner's complaint. The beneficial owner appealed, and the court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the case to consider the motions to dismiss. The court held the law in existence at the time and place the contract was made was deemed part of the contract to the same extent as though expressly referred to or incorporated in the contract. The court found Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 10, para. 1 et seq. (1949) on arbitration governed the case since the new law did not apply retroactively. Based on the statute, the arbitration agreement to settle future disputes was unenforceable and void. The court found the seller's motions to dismiss was governed by § 45 of the Civil Practice Act (Act) and the trustee's motion was by § 48 of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court which dismissed the beneficial owner's complaint against the seller, other owners, and trustee, for failure to exhaust her remedies pursuant to an arbitration agreement. The court remanded the case.

Murphy v. Policemen's Annuity & Ben. Fund


No. 77-1135


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


71 Ill. App. 3d 556; 390 N.E.2d 45; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2500; 28 Ill. Dec. 63



April 23, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CURRY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former police officer filed a class action in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on behalf of himself and other officers whose pensions were terminated by defendant, Retirement Board of the Policemen's Annuity and Benefit Fund, upon their convictions of felonies relating to their service as policemen. The court dismissed the complaint for failure to exhaust administrative remedies. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the Retirement Board of the Policemen's Annuity and Benefit Fund was established under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 8 -- 101 et seq. (1977) to provide retired policemen with pensions and other benefits. After leaving the police force, plaintiff was convicted in a United States District Court of extortion in relation to his duties as a police officer. After an administrative hearing, the Board revoked his pension under para. 5 -- 227. Plaintiff appealed the order of dismissal and asserted that the pursuit of administrative remedies would impose a mere procedural duty to engage in a time-consuming and expensive administrative review process to secure a predictable outcome. The court held that plaintiff's purported class action was not filed in accordance with the Administrative Review Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 264 et seq. (1977) and was therefore barred. The court affirmed the order dismissing the class action.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the trial court's order that plaintiff failed to pursue and exhaust his administrative remedies. The court held that the complaint in question was therefore barred.

People v. Clark


No. 78-97


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


70 Ill. App. 3d 698; 388 N.E.2d 1107; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2420; 27 Ill. Dec. 144



April 10, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Perry County; the Hon. ROBERT BASTIEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Perry County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated battery, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-4(b)(8) (1977).


OVERVIEW: The victim of the battery testified that on the night in question, defendant invited him to take a ride in his recently acquired pickup truck. After they reached the turnaround of a dirt road off the highway, defendant parked and started an argument about $ 20 that the victim had taken from defendant months earlier. Without provocation, defendant hit the victim above his left eye with a bottle. The resulting cut in the victim's eyebrow was cleaned at a hospital, but no stitches were required. Defendant was convicted of aggravated battery under para. 12-4(b)(8) because the trial court found that the battery took place "on or about a public way." Defendant appealed, and the court reversed. The court held that the incident involved in the case, which occurred some 95 to 100 feet from the public way, did not occur "on or about a public way." However, although defendant was not proved to have committed aggravated battery, the trial court found and the court concluded that defendant was proved guilty, beyond a reasonable doubt, of "simple" battery, which was a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-3 (1977). Thus, the court reduced the conviction under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(b)(3).


OUTCOME: The court reduced the offense for which defendant was convicted from aggravated battery to simple battery, and it remanded for resentencing.

Bodine Electric Co. v. Allphin


No. 77-255


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


70 Ill. App. 3d 844; 389 N.E.2d 168; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2443; 27 Ill. Dec. 356



April 5, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. F. EMMETT MORRISSEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer filed a claim with defendant, Illinois Department of Revenue, for tax refunds for a net operating loss. The Department sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which ordered the refunds to the taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer reported a net operating loss on its state income tax return. The taxpayer claimed that it was entitled to carry back the net operating loss on its two prior income tax returns. The Department claimed that the taxpayer's entire loss was absorbed by its federal taxable income and that the loss could not be carried back. The trial court found that the taxpayer was entitled to carry back the loss. The court reversed the trial court's decision. The court held that the Illinois Income Tax Act did not specifically adopt all federally allowed deductions, that the Act did not allow a deduction for net operating loss or for providing for a carry back or carry forward of the loss to other taxable years, and that the taxpayer was entitled only to a net operating loss deduction in the same manner and amount as it would have been entitled on its federal income tax return. The court also held that the taxpayer's federal income tax return completely absorbed the loss, that the taxpayer was not entitled to carry back the loss, and that the taxpayer was not entitled to a deduction under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 4-403(a) (1971).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision ordering the refunds to the taxpayer and reinstated the determination of the Department that the taxpayer was not entitled to the refunds.

People v. Bauer


No. 78-267


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


70 Ill. App. 3d 537; 388 N.E.2d 1013; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2391; 27 Ill. Dec. 50



April 3, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Bond County; the Hon. VICTOR J. MOSELE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Bond County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion for discharge under the speedy trial act.


OVERVIEW: In April of 1977, defendant was charged with unlawful possession of cannabis. Three days later defendant's counsel filed a demand for immediate trial. After several delays attributable to defendant, defendant was filed in July 18, 1977. The State's motion to dismiss the information with leave to reinstate due to the mysterious disappearance of a material witness was granted. The missing witness was subsequently located and, in January of 1978, defendant was indicted. In February, defendant filed motion to discharge under the speedy trial act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 103-5 (1977). The motion was granted. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that defendant was entitled to trial within 160 days of the demand for speedy trial made in July of 1977. The statute was not tolled, as the State contended, when the original information was dismissed because the circumstances suggested that the State sought to circumvent the statutory time requirement by dismissing the action rather than petitioning the circuit court for a continuance to locate the material witness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Boytor v. Aurora


No. 78-28


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


70 Ill. App. 3d 303; 388 N.E.2d 449; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2308; 26 Ill. Dec. 734



March 30, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. JOHN S. PAGE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mayoral candidate filed an action against defendants, a city and its election commission, for declaratory and injunctive relief after the candidate's name did not appear on a ballot in a primary election for mayor. The candidate sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which dismissed the candidate's action.


OVERVIEW: The candidate filed as a partisan candidate for mayor for a primary election that was to have been held in February. The voters adopted a referendum that all city elections would be nonpartisan and that the primary election would be held in March and the general election would be held in April. The candidate's name did not appear on the March ballot. The candidate claimed that he was denied the opportunity to run for mayor and that the referendum and primary were unlawful. The court dismissed the candidate's appeal. The court held that the candidate instituted his action 95 days after the general election, that the candidate waited too long to assert the illegality of the referendum and the elections, that the candidate lacked standing to prosecute the litigation, and that the candidate was estopped from instituting his action. The court also held that the candidate was not without a remedy, that the candidate could have brought a quo warranto proceeding, that the candidate's action was barred by the doctrine of res judicata, and that the public interest of the city mandated the dismissal of the candidate's appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the candidate's appeal.

Sneddon v. State Emples. Ret. Sys.


No. 15208


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


69 Ill. App. 3d 992; 388 N.E.2d 229; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3912; 26 Ill. Dec. 605



March 30, 1979, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 4, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. JAMES T. LONDRIGAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the widow of an employee of the State of Illinois, appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which affirmed a decision of the Board of Trustees of defendant, the Illinois State Employees' Retirement System, denying the widow's claim for a survivors annuity.


OVERVIEW: The employee, who had previously been divorced from the widow, died about seven months after marrying her a second time. The System's claims committee found that the widow was not entitled to a survivors annuity under § 14-160(a)(1) of the Illinois Pension Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 14-160(a)(1) (1975), because she was married to the employee less than one year before his death. In affirming the denial of the widow's claim, the court held that classification of spouses into those married less than one year before a State employee's death and those married one year or more was rationally related to prevention of "deathbed" marriages entered solely to enable another person to become eligible for System benefits. Section 14-160(a)(1) of the Illinois Pension Code referred to a particular marriage contract and did not permit "tacking" of separate marriage contracts to meet the one-year requirement. The System's regulations authorized use of a bystander's report of proceedings before the claims committee; due process did not require that the committee pay a stenographer's fees as long as there was a means to allow for effective appellate review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the System.

People v. Natoli


No. 77-1485


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


70 Ill. App. 3d 131; 387 N.E.2d 1096; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2286; 26 Ill. Dec. 266



March 28, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. MARVIN J. PETERS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), after a jury trial, for possession and delivery of a controlled substance and sought review of his concurrent sentences of one to three years for delivery and two to six years for possession.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of delivering the controlled substance to an informer, who was accompanied by a police officer. Defendant claimed that he was entrapped, that the trial court improperly admitted evidence of defendant's prior conviction, and that the statutory classifications of possession and delivery of the controlled substance violated his equal protection rights. The State claimed that the prosecutor's errors were harmless. The court reversed defendant's convictions. The court held that the prosecutor cross-examined defendant about a prior conviction and prior charges, that the prosecutor's cross-examination was prejudicial, that the prosecutor's closing argument, which made reference to defendant's parole and business, was improper and prejudicial, and that defendant was entitled to a new trial. The court held, however, that the statutory sentence for delivery of the controlled substance was valid, that defendant could be retried on the charge of delivery, but that the statutory sentence for possession, which authorized a higher penalty, denied defendant equal protection of the law, and that defendant could not be retried on the charge of possession.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions for possession and delivery of the controlled substance and granted defendant a new trial on the delivery charge only. The court ordered that defendant could not be retried on the possession charge.

People v. Kirkpatrick


No. 14986


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


70 Ill. App. 3d 166; 387 N.E.2d 1284; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2290; 26 Ill. Dec. 356



March 26, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. ROGER H. LITTLE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of two felony murders and sentenced him to concurrent terms of imprisonment of 200 to 500 years for each.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in the commission of a robbery with two other men when the murders occurred. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in permitting a portion of defendant's statement about a gasoline station robbery the previous night to go to the jury. The court held that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in concluding that the probative value of the evidence for its limited purpose outweighed its prejudicial effect. Defendant argued that the instruction confused the jury into believing that there was a lesser standard for determining defendant's accountability. However, some evidence supported every element of the instruction. The giving of the instruction was not error. Defendant objected to the introduction into evidence of two pictures of the torn-up faces of the victims. As these items were not shown to the jury, defendant was not prejudiced by their admission. Further, the trial court was not in error in admitting, for impeachment purposes, evidence of defendant's federal convictions. The trial judge performed the balancing test and did not abuse his discretion in admitting the evidence. The convictions and sentences of defendant were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and sentences of defendant for two felony murders.

 

1702 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Guzzardo


No. 78-19


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


69 Ill. App. 3d 252; 387 N.E.2d 896; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2164; 26 Ill. Dec. 66



March 19, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. JOHN W. NIELSEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction on charges by the State for pandering in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-16(a)(2) (1975) by the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) on grounds that para. 11-16(a)(2) was unconstitutionally vague, his guilt was not proven beyond reasonable doubt, and reversible errors were made at trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant offered to pay a witness wearing a wire money to perform prostitution and to provide her with a hotel room in exchange for some of her receipts. The recording was inaudible, and the witness gave a written statement concerning defendant's offer. The trial court denied defendant's motion in limine to exclude a detective's testimony, but limited the scope of his testimony to matters within the State's offer of proof. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction by the trial court. Para. 11-16(a)(2) was not unconstitutionally vague because the plain and ordinary meaning of the statute's language was of sufficient specificity to provide notice of what conduct was prohibited. The State's opening statement was not a basis for reversible error because the State made a good faith effort to provide evidence related to defendant's motive, intent, or design. Instruction to the jury negated prejudice from the detective's testimony that exceeded the scope allowed by the trial court. The designation of one of the State's witnesses as a court witness was justified by the State's surprise at her testimony. The evidence was sufficient to support the jury's guilty verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for pandering by the trial court.

 

1703 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Wheeler v. Rockford


No. 77-537


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


69 Ill. App. 3d 220; 387 N.E.2d 358; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2158; 25 Ill. Dec. 702



March 15, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. JOHN S. GHENT, JR., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment action, plaintiff sauna owner appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) holding that Rockford, Ill., Massage Establishments and Massage Services Ordinance §§ 13, 16 were constitutional. Defendant city appealed from that portion of the judgment, which held that § 8 of the ordinance was unconstitutional under Ill. Const. 1970 art. I, § 18.


OVERVIEW: Rockford, Ill., Massage Establishments and Massage Services Ordinance § 8 provided that it was unlawful for any person holding a permit under the section to treat a person of the opposite sex except in certain specified circumstances. The city argued that a compelling interest, which would be necessary to prohibit a person from massaging a person of the opposite sex, existed in prohibiting conduct which was obscene or which was a public nuisance. In affirming that part of the trial court, which found § 8 of the ordinance to be unconstitutional, the court held that it could not say that there existed a compelling state interest for the sex-based classification. The court reversed that part of the judgment, which held that § 16 was constitutional. Section 16 allowed police to inspect massage establishments twice a year. Because the ordinance allowed warrantless administrative searches of nonpublic areas of business buildings, it was unconstitutional. Section 13 regulating advertisement was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the judgment of the trial court, which held that the ordinance prohibiting massages by members of the opposite sex was unconstitutional and the ordinance regulating advertising was constitutional. The court reversed the part of the judgment of the trial court, which held that the ordinance allowing inspections of massage establishments by police, without a warrant, was constitutional.

 

1704 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Harris


No. 77-173


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


69 Ill. App. 3d 118; 387 N.E.2d 33; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2145; 25 Ill. Dec. 576



March 14, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. ANGELO F. PISTILLI, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action filed by the People of the State of Illinois, defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois) that assessed him costs in a proceeding held pursuant to § 410 of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1410 (1975). Defendant had previously been placed on first offender probation under § 410. The parties currently disagreed over whether a recent case controlled the cost issue.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been convicted of a heroin possession. He was placed on first offender probation and was required to pay the costs of the proceeding as a condition of the probation. The cause was then continued. Defendant filed a notice of appeal. Subsequently, the Illinois Supreme Court held in another case that imposing fines and costs under § 10 of Cannabis Control Act, which, similarly, dealt with first offender probation, was not authorized. The People contended that because defendant made no objection to costs at sentencing, the cost issue was waived. The court reversed the order. Defendant had not waived the costs issue because the supreme court case was not decided when the costs were assessed. The legislature's attempt to retroactively apply the part of the 1978 amendments to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, paras. 710, 1410 (1977), violated separation of powers under Ill. Const. art. 11, § 1. The amendment at issue was also an unconstitutional ex post facto law because it increased the punishment for a crime through an amendatory act that took effect after the crime. The court held that the supreme court case applied prospectively. The supreme court's decision bound the court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that assessed defendant costs.

 

1705 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Vanthournout v. Burge


No. 78-273


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


69 Ill. App. 3d 193; 387 N.E.2d 341; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2152; 25 Ill. Dec. 685



March 12, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. DONALD T. ANDERSON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff automobile owner filed a small claims complaint against defendant father for damage sustained when the father's 11-year-old son took the automobile owner's automobile. The Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) found that the son willfully drove the automobile off the road causing property damage and entered judgment against the father. On appeal, the father challenged the constitutionality of the Parental Responsibility Act (Act).


OVERVIEW: The appeal challenged the constitutionality of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 70, paras. 51 to 57 (1977). The father contended that the Act deprived the parent of property without due process of law by imposing liability without regard to fault, created an unreasonable classification by imposing vicarious liability on a parent or guardian of a minor from 11 to 18 years of age, and was not a valid exercise of the police power and did not have a reasonable relationship to the objectives sought to be attained. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the father had not met the burden of showing that the Act was unconstitutional. The court noted that the purpose of the Act was two-fold: (1) to compensate innocent victims of juvenile misconduct that was willful or malicious; and (2) to place upon the parents the obligation to control a minor child so as to prevent intentional harm to others. The court held that the purpose of the Act was a proper one and that the means employed was substantially related to the end sought and that therefore it was a fair and reasonable exercise of the police power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which entered judgment against the father in the automobile owner's action for damages sustained when the father's son took the automobile owner's automobile.

 

1706 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Department of Transp. on behalf of People v. Collins


No. 77-434


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


69 Ill. App. 3d 269; 387 N.E.2d 6; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2167; 25 Ill. Dec. 549



February 28, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of McDonough County; the Hon. WILLIAM L. RANDOLPH, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of McDonough County (Illinois), which denied their traverse and motions to dismiss and granted the state's motion for the immediate vesting of title in certain condemned property.


OVERVIEW: The property owners' land was to be taken as part of a road improvement project. The state sought immediate vesting of title because the project was to be let for bidding within a matter of days and the state had to be in possession of the property before that process could take place. The property owners asserted that the state had not properly exercised its right of eminent domain. The court affirmed the denial of the property owners motions to dismiss and for a continuance to conduct discovery. The court refused to consider constitutional challenges to the quick-take statute and the payment of judgment interest because they were not raised before the trial court. The request for discovery was properly denied because there was no good cause found for the discovery and the property owners admitted they were not prejudiced by any lack of discovery. And, while the property owners' traverse should have been considered before the state's quick-take motion, the trial court's failure to do so was not reversible error. The property owners induced the error by requesting that the quick-take motion be heard first. The court affirmed the quick-take order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which denied the property owners' traverse and motions to dismiss and granted the state's request for immediate vesting of title in the condemned property.

 

1707 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Board of Education v. Cronin


No. 78-85


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


69 Ill. App. 3d 472; 388 N.E.2d 72; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2195; 26 Ill. Dec. 448



February 27, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. DONALD J. O'BRIEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, State Superintendent of Education (superintendent) and the Illinois Office of Education (office of education), sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment and entered an order in favor of plaintiff school district. The school district sought to restrain the superintendent and the office of education from withholding certain reimbursement funds from the school district.


OVERVIEW: The school district provided transportation between home and school for students residing a distance away from their schools. Additional trips were made in the late afternoon to accommodate students who remained after classes for scholastic consultation, disciplinary action, sports programs, and other activities. The school district was told that the late afternoon trips should not have been reimbursed because those trips constituted transportation between "co-curricular activities" and home and that § 29-5 of the Illinois School Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 29-5 (1975) did not contemplate such trips. The funds were to have been recouped by withholding future reimbursements. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted summary judgment and entered an order in favor of the school district. The students were not only transported to and from the physical site of the school, but also were at that site primarily for the purpose of attending school. Thus, the transportation provided was occasioned primarily by the students' attendance at school and was appropriately classed by the school district as coming within § 29-5.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which granted summary judgment and entered an order in favor of the school district in its action to restrain the superintendent and the office of education from withholding certain reimbursement funds from the school district.

Miller v. Illinois Dep't of Public Aid


No. 78-530


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


69 Ill. App. 3d 477; 387 N.E.2d 810; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2196; 25 Ill. Dec. 934



February 27, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOSEPH M. WOSIK, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff recipient appealed orders from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied him a preliminary injunction, granted the motion by defendants, Illinois Department of Public Aid (IDPA), IDPA director, and the county director, to dismiss the complaint for failure to exhaust administrative remedies as provided for in Public Aid Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 1-1 et seq. (1977), and denied the recipient's motion to vacate.


OVERVIEW: The recipient filed an action challenging IDPA policies denying him eyeglasses and nonemergency dental care. The trial court dismissed the recipient's complaint because he failed to exhaust his administrative remedies. The court reversed, holding that the trial court erred in dismissing the recipient's complaint for failure to exhaust his administrative remedies. The court found that the Administrative Review Act (ARA) was not applicable to the recipient's claims because it was not expressly adopted by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 11-8.7 (1977) of the Public Aid Code. Even assuming the ARA was applicable, the recipient did not need to exhaust his administrative remedies because he attacked the administrative rule on its face, which was strictly a question of law. The court also found that the recipient's pursuit of the administrative remedies provided in §§ 11-5 through 11-8 of the Public Aid Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, paras. 11-5 - 11-8 (1977) would have been futile.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the recipient's complaint for failure to exhaust administrative remedies and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

1709 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lewis


Nos. 76-108, 76-199, 76-200 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


73 Ill. App. 3d 361; 386 N.E.2d 910; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2902; 25 Ill. Dec. 436



February 15, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. MICHAEL A. ORENIC, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), convicting them of violating § 3-6-4(a) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1003-6-4(a) (1975), relating to enforcement of prison discipline. Defendants challenged the definiteness of § 3-6-4(a), their selection for prosecution, an alleged double jeopardy violation, and their absence during a communication between the judge and jury.


OVERVIEW: Several guards were assaulted and taken hostage, and an entire cellblock was held under prisoner control. The court held that § 3-6-4(a) met due process standards. Although the words "participate" and "disturbance" could be too vague if found in a general "breach of the peace" ordinance, they were sufficiently precise in a statute written specifically for the prison context where the prohibited disturbances were easily measured by their impact on the normal activities of the prison. Moreover, the record indicated that defendants were among the most active participants in both the holding of the hostages and the disturbance as a whole. Although other inmates who participated in the disturbance were not criminally prosecuted, defendants did not show that the selection for prosecution was deliberately based upon an arbitrary classification. There was no double jeopardy violation because administrative discipline of a prisoner did not prohibit criminal prosecution for the same event. Finally, defendants were not prejudiced by their absence during the communications between the trial court and the jury because defense counsel was present and the jury's question was a purely legal one.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Pinson v. Allstate Ins. Co.


No. 76-290


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


68 Ill. App. 3d 788; 386 N.E.2d 638; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2094; 25 Ill. Dec. 367



February 8, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insured sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed that portion of the insured's complaint that sought treble damages against appellee insurer for the insurer's discontinuance of benefit payments.


OVERVIEW: The insured obtained a policy of insurance from the insurer that contained a rider that provided for excess personal injury protection. The insured was seriously injured in a car accident and the insurer paid benefits under the policy, including the rider. The insurer made payment for 14 months and then terminated benefits. The insured filed an action seeking reinstatement of the benefits and treble damages under article 35 of the Insurance Code, § 603(b). The trial court granted summary judgment to the insurer on the issue of treble damages because § 603(b) had been declared unconstitutional and the insured challenged the decision. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the insurer impliedly waived its unconstitutionality defense to the payment of treble damages because it continued to pay benefits to the insured for 12 months after the statute was declared unconstitutional. The matter was remanded for a determination of whether the refusal to pay benefits was willful as required by the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the insurer on the insured's claim for treble damages for the wrongful termination of benefits.

Echo Lake Concerned Citizens Homeowners Asso. v. Lake Zurich


No. 76-243


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


68 Ill. App. 3d 219; 386 N.E.2d 117; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2012; 24 Ill. Dec. 913



February 7, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. HENRY H. CALDWELL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied, order affirmed in part and appeal dismissed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners' association appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), that dismissed one count of its complaint against defendants, village, the property owner, and two of its officers. The court denied the association's motion for leave to file a second amended complaint. The association filed a motion to dismiss count II of the first amended complaint.


OVERVIEW: The association filed an amended two-count complaint against defendants. Count I challenged the constitutionality of the rezoning. It did not seek directly to void the annexation. In count II, plaintiff, a not-for-profit corporation, asked to be declared the sole owner of Echo Lake and to enjoin defendants from using the lake for any purpose. Count I was dismissed. The village alleged that count I was barred by the statute of limitations. On appeal, the court noted that one issue was whether the association could attack the rezoning without attacking the annexation. The court found that if the pre-annexation agreement was to be given any legal force, a successful attack on the rezoning could result in a lawsuit by the owners to declare the annexation void. The association argued that the one-year statute of limitations did not apply if the officials annexing the territory did not have jurisdiction of the subject matter. The court held that the elected officials of the village had the lawful power to grant applications for zoning; thus, they had the subject matter jurisdiction required by the statute. The court affirmed the order of the circuit court in regard to count I.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court dismissing count I of association's first amended complaint. The court dismissed the appeal with regard to the order denying the association leave to file a second amended complaint and denied the association's motion to dismiss count II of the first amended complaint.

People v. Estrada


No. 77-452


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


68 Ill. App. 3d 272; 386 N.E.2d 128; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2020; 24 Ill. Dec. 924



February 7, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Carroll County; the Hon. JOHN W. RAPP, JR., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged a decision from the Circuit Court, Carroll County (Illinois), which granted the defendant's motion to suppress evidence on the grounds that the search of his car and the seizure of cannabis violated his Fourth Amendment rights in a prosecution for unlawful possession of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was stopped a part of a systematic check conducted by the police, who pulled cars over to verify the safety of vehicles on the road. The police discovered cannabis and the defendant was arrested for possession. The trial court granted the defendant's motion to suppress that evidence on the ground that no statute authorized the police to make the investigatory stops they were conducting. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded because systematic safety checks were an appropriate and constitutional exercise of the state's police power to make public roads safe for use. The promulgation of safety laws carried an implied authorization for the enforcement of those laws.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that granted the defendant's motion to suppress and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1713 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Makowicz v. County of Macon


No. 15018


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


68 Ill. App. 3d 322; 385 N.E.2d 917; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2029; 24 Ill. Dec. 776



February 7, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. JOHN P. SHONKWILER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Superintendent of the Veterans Assistance Commission of Macon County, initiated an action for declaratory relief against defendant, the County of Macon, to determine whether the Commission's dismissed workers were employees of the County under the Bogardus Law, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 3081 et seq. (1977). The Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) held that they were County employees, and the County appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Bogardus Law, the Commission was established in the County to assist needy veterans and their surviving family members. The executive powers of the Commission were vested in the Superintendent, who was elected by members of the Commission. The Commission employed several workers to assist the Superintendent. The workers were dismissed. The Superintendent initiated an action for declaratory relief. The trial court held that the workers were employees of the Commission and were subject to hiring and discharge under the Commission's rules. The County claimed that portion of the Bogardus Law, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 3090 (1977), which authorized the Commission to appoint its Superintendent, was unconstitutional. In reversing the decision and remanding, the court found that paragraph 3090 was unconstitutional because it provided for the selection by the Commission of the Superintendent, who exercised the sovereign power of the government. Once the proper chain between the Superintendent and the electorate was established, the Superintendent had the power to hire and fire workers. The workers could not then be subject to the County's policies.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who pleaded guilty to aggravated battery and was initially sentenced to probation, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which revoked her probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated battery and was initially sentenced to probation. Thereafter, a petition to revoke her probation was filed, and the trial court found the allegations of the petition were proven by the preponderance of the evidence. People v. Griffith


No. 77-258


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


68 Ill. App. 3d 188; 385 N.E.2d 843; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 2008; 24 Ill. Dec. 702



January 26, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. JOHN J. HOBAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which convicted him of felony murder after a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the cumulative prejudicial effect of evidentiary errors by the trial court, ineffective representation by defense counsel, and improper argument by the prosecutor deprived him of a fair trial. The evidence at trial established that defendant and an accomplice robbed a victim at gunpoint with a sawed-off shotgun. A shot was fired, and the victim was found dead. An informant told police that defendant admitted to the crime. Police forced their way into defendant's home while he was away and recovered blood-stained clothes. The accomplice turned State's evidence and testified that defendant held the shotgun on the victim. Defendant argued that the evidence against him was tainted fruit of an unconstitutional search. Finding no prejudicial error, the court affirmed the judgment of conviction because when the officers arrived at defendant's home, they clearly had probable cause to arrest him. The court held that the fact that defendant was known to be armed justified the warrantless entry. As to whether the accomplice was truthful, the court held that it was immaterial because defendant would have been guilty of felony murder even as an accomplice.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

People v. Childs


Nos. 78-87, 78-79, 78-82, 78-85, 78-86 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


67 Ill. App. 3d 473; 385 N.E.2d 147; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 1963; 24 Ill. Dec. 380



January 9, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. ROBERT L. DANNEHL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, in Will County (Illinois), which convicted him of theft after he sold stolen property to undercover police.


OVERVIEW: On appeal defendant raised the issue that the circuit court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence from electronic eavesdropping devices because the authorization to eavesdrop was overbroad and violated his rights under Ill. Const. art. I, § 6. The court affirmed the conviction. Only those eavesdrops which were made without the consent of at least one party to the conversation were unconstitutional. Because the application for judicial approval of the eavesdropping device recited the consent of the undercover officers who participated in the conversations, the court found that it was not faced with a constitutional question. The restrictions on the recording of a conversation were statutory and not constitutional. As Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 108A -- 3(a)(2)(d) (1977), provided for that type of approval and as there was apparently no other complaint regarding the application, there was no error in admitting the evidence of the videotape.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court that convicted defendant of theft after he sold stolen property to undercover police.

People v. Keeven


No. 77-514


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


68 Ill. App. 3d 91; 385 N.E.2d 804; 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 1996; 24 Ill. Dec. 663



January 9, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. JOHN W. DAY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff government filed suit to enjoin defendant apartment building owners from violating § 12(a) of the Illinois Environmental Protection Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1012(a), and Rules 951 and 952 of the Illinois Pollution Control Board Rules and Regulations (Rules). The Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) entered an order dismissing the complaint with prejudice and denying a preliminary injunction. The government appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's order also dissolved a previously issued temporary restraining order and found Rule 951 unconstitutional although the validity of the Rules were never challenged by the apartment building owners. On appeal, the government contended that the complaint was legally sufficient to state a cause of action and established its right to injunctive relief. The government also contended that Rule 951 was a valid exercise of the state's police power and did not violate the Illinois Constitution or the United States Constitution. The court reversed and held that the trial court erred in dismissing the complaint for failure to state a cause of action. The court found that the well-pleaded facts, and the reasonable and fair inferences therefrom, alleged all essential elements of a violation of § 12(a) of the Illinois Environmental Protection Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1012(a). Further, the court held that the government was not required to prove irreparable damage or an absence of an adequate remedy at law where the Act authorized the government to bring an action for injunctive relief upon a violation of the Act by the apartment building owners.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the cause to the trial court for entry of a preliminary injunction and for trial on the merits.

 

1719 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. White


No. 77-1861


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


69 Ill. App. 3d 830; 387 N.E.2d 728; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3945; 25 Ill. Dec. 852



December 29, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Opinion Filed on Denial of Rehearing April 12, 1979, Reported at: 69 Ill. App. 3d 830 at 842.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. MARK E. JONES, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of criminal abortion in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 81-13(g) (1973).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a chiropractor, was arrested on the charge of having illegally performed an abortion. He was convicted based on evidence that he had knowingly performed an abortion on a minor female, and he appealed. On appeal, he argued that the abortion control statute was unconstitutional and that there was insufficient evidence to convict him. Both arguments were rejected. As to the constitutional challenge to the abortion statute, the court noted that a federal decision deeming the statute unconstitutional dealt with the portion of the statute that criminalized the causing of a miscarriage. That clause was not in issue, as there was no dispute that defendant performed an abortion. The portion of the statute requiring that one be a physician was not unconstitutional, and thus defendant could properly be convicted under it. As to defendant's insufficiency claim, the court noted that all defendant was arguing was that the prosecution's witnesses were unworthy of belief. That was a trial court question, not an appellate court question.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for performing an illegal abortion was affirmed.

 

1720 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Griffiths


No. 14892


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


67 Ill. App. 3d 16; 384 N.E.2d 528; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3774; 23 Ill. Dec. 734



December 29, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Coles County; the Hon. RICHARD E. SCOTT, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with, among other things, failing to make and keep records of controlled substances administered, dispensed, or professionally used by him as a dentist as required by § 406(a)93) of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1406(a)(3) (1977). The Circuit Court of Coles County (Illinois) dismissed the charge as time-barred under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 3-5(b) (1977). The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: In addition to dismissing the charge, the circuit court granted the State leave to file an amended count before a certain date. Defendant requested that his bond be returned. The bond was not discharged. On appeal from the dismissal of the charges, the State contended that the offense alleged was a continuing one and that the last date upon which the offense was alleged to have occurred was within the 18-month limitation period, thereby rendering that limitation inapplicable. Defendant contended that the court lacked jurisdiction because the order of dismissal was not appealable. The court first determined that the circuit court's order was appealable because the "substantive effect" of the order was to dismiss the charge; the record did not show whether the circuit court ruled upon defendant's request to discharge his bond. In reversing the order, the court held that the circuit court erred in dismissing the charge as time-barred because the offense could have been a continuing one; the references to "keeping" records in both Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1406(a)(3) and 21 U.S.C.S. § 827 compelled a conclusion that such an offense was to be construed as a continuing one.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the case to the circuit court for further proceedings.

 

1721 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Morton Grove Park Dist. v. American Nat'l Bank & Trust Co.


No. 77-1573


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


67 Ill. App. 3d 709; 385 N.E.2d 123; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3874; 24 Ill. Dec. 356



December 29, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant trustee for the condemnee appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied its request for the income earned on a condemnation award deposited with the Treasurer of Cook County by the condemnor, Morton Grove Park District, after the property had been taken in condemnation proceedings.


OVERVIEW: After the jury determined the value of the property, the Park District deposited the amount, with accrued interest, with the Treasurer. The condemnee could not accept the amount and appeal at the same time. It argued that it had neither the benefit of the property nor the use of the money, thus, it was entitled to receive the interest earned on the amount deposited during the pendency of the appeal as part of its just compensation. The court rejected the argument. When the Park District deposited the award with the Treasurer, the statutory and constitutional requirements of just compensation were satisfied. The award when paid fixed the rights of the parties as of the date of the taking. The condemnee next contended that the interest earned should be paid to it because the Treasurer acted as its trustee while the award was on deposit. The court found no trust relationship existed. It also found no legislative grant of authority to the Treasurer to pay out any earnings accruing on deposited condemnation awards. To the contrary, the Treasurer was required by statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 36, para. 17 (1977) to credit such earnings to the county corporate fund.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment appealed from.

 

1722 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Keller v. Board of Education


No. 78-152


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


68 Ill. App. 3d 7; 385 N.E.2d 785; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3905; 24 Ill. Dec. 644



December 29, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Union County; the Hon. ROBERT L. LANDSEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Union County, which dismissed their claim against defendant board of education (board). The homeowners brought an action for damage to their yard caused by stray baseballs from the school property. The board's motion to dismiss for failure to state a cause of action was granted. The homeowners elected to stand on their pleadings and the action was dismissed with prejudice.


OVERVIEW: Stray baseballs from the board's school were landing in the homeowners' yard, causing damage. The homeowners filed a lawsuit claiming willful and wanton negligence, and a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for the unauthorized invasions of baseballs from the school in violation of the homeowners' 5th and 14th Amendment rights under the United State Constitution. The court affirmed the dismissal of the homeowners' claim. The court affirmed the dismissal of the claim in negligence based on Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 3- 106 and 108(a) (1977), which granted immunity for ordinary negligence by a local public entity on property used as a park. The court also held that the negligent conduct of a State agency, although resulting in damage to a person's property, did not amount to a deprivation of that person's constitutional right to property. The court held that conduct that could be actionable under common law did not necessarily arise to a constitutional dimension merely because a public body was involved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the homeowner's negligence claim and claim for deprivation of constitutional rights as a result of stray baseballs damaging the homeowner's yard.
