Ming Kow Hah v. Stackler


No. 77-536


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


66 Ill. App. 3d 947; 383 N.E.2d 1264; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3930; 23 Ill. Dec. 237



December 29, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 66 Ill. App. 3d 947 at 954.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of November 3, 1978, Reported at 66 Ill. App. 3d 947.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor sought rehearing of the court's decision in favor of appellee Director of the Department of Registration and Education, arguing that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91, para. 16a(11) of the Medical Practice Act was unconstitutional. The challenged statute permitted the Department to revoke the doctor's Illinois licenses on the basis of the revocation of his license in another state. The doctor also sought recall of the court's mandate.


OVERVIEW: The doctor was licensed to practice medicine in Illinois and in Michigan. The revocation of his license in Michigan was the basis for the Department to revoke his license in Illinois, and the doctor filed an action against the Department challenging its revocation. The trial court ruled in favor of the Department and the doctor appealed. The court ruled in favor of the Department and the doctor sought rehearing, arguing that the court erred in refusing to consider his argument that para. 16a(11) was unconstitutional in that it improperly delegated authority over Illinois licenses to other states. The court noted that the doctor had not raised his issues in the trial court and stated that where no constitutional question was presented to or passed upon by the trial court and the only question was the interpretation of a statute, a constitutional question was not present on appeal. The court found further that the arguments that the doctor was attempting to raise on rehearing had not been raised in his original appellate brief, therefore under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 341(e)(7), those arguments were waived and could not be raised on a petition for rehearing.


OUTCOME: The court denied the doctor's petition for rehearing and denied the request for a recall of the court's mandate.

 

1724 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In Interest of Serna


No. 77-1903


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


67 Ill. App. 3d 406; 385 N.E.2d 87; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3835; 24 Ill. Dec. 320



December 26, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. PETER F. COSTA, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that revoked his supervision, found him delinquent, adjudged him a ward of the court, and committed him to the Department of Corrections. Although not previously found delinquent, he had been placed on supervision for charges of criminal damage to property, a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 21--1(a), when he painted signs on a school wall.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was placed on supervision, he was ordered to follow the rules he would be given. However, the trial court did not provide him with written rules. While under supervision, he stopped attending school. He was charged with violating of the terms and conditions of his supervision. He admitted his truancy. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in revoking defendant's supervision on the basis of his violation of the conditions of supervision because there was no evidence the trial court had ever specified the terms and conditions of the supervision, as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 705--3(9). If the trial court had formulated written rules, there was nothing in the record to indicate that defendant received them. A child was still entitled to constitutional due process protections. Because he was never told what rules to obey, defendant could not found to have violated them. The trial court's statements admonishing him to listen to his mother and stay out of trouble were too vague to satisfy constitutional concerns. Under those admonishments, defendant was required to guess as to whether truancy would fall within their scope.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that revoked defendant's supervision, found him delinquent, ordered him a ward of the court and committed him to the Department of Corrections.

People v. Thingvold


Nos. 77-470, 77-564 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


66 Ill. App. 3d 1002; 384 N.E.2d 489; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3761; 23 Ill. Dec. 695



December 21, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. JOHN C. LAYNG, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which convicted him of indecent liberties with a child.


OVERVIEW: Two women notified the police when they observed defendant touching a young girl and rubbing or punching her dress above her knees and below her waist. Defendant was arrested by the police and admitted to kissing the girl, but denied any sexual activity with the girl. The court affirmed the conviction and held that the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of indecent liberties with a child because even though there was no direct evidence of defendant's contact with a sex part of the child because the act of defendant in kissing and touching the child, coupled with the mental intent to arouse the sexual desires of either the child or himself was sufficient to give defendant notice that he was violating the indecent liberties with a child statute. The court held that it was improper to allow the introduction of evidence of prior incidences with young girls and defendant's prior confinement where there was insufficient similarity between the previous acts and the current offense to constitute a common scheme or design. However, the court found that the error was harmless because the remaining evidence was sufficient to warrant a conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for indecent liberties with a child.

Eagle Books, Inc. v. Rockford


No. 78-27


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


66 Ill. App. 3d 1038; 384 N.E.2d 493; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3769; 23 Ill. Dec. 699



December 21, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. JOHN C. LAYNG, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a company and an individual, appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which found that an obscenity ordinance was constitutional. Defendant city appealed from the decision dismissing the city's cross-complaint to find the materials possessed for sale by plaintiffs to be in violation of the statute.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought an action for declaratory judgment and for injunctive relief to have a municipal obscenity ordinance declared unconstitutional on its face and to enjoin its enforcement against them. The court reversed the trial court's denial of the declaratory judgment, determining first that although the ordinance had not been enforced against plaintiffs, they had a protectable interest - the continued sale of certain materials - which would be adversely affected by the enforcement of the ordinance. The court held that the ordinance was not vague or overbroad, but that it improperly made possession of materials a crime and that it was invalid for failing to provide for the application of a statewide community standard for evaluating obscenity and failed to adopt the utterly without redeeming social value test in defining obscenity. The court affirmed that portion which denied the city's cross-complaint, holding that where the item complained of was not entered into evidence, the cross-complaint was deficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that portion of the trial court judgment dismissing the city's cross-complaint, but reversed that portion denying plaintiffs' request to have the ordinance declared unconstitutional.

The court also held that the sections of the Act of which defendant was convicted were not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

Advocates for the Handicapped v. Sears, Roebuck & Co.


No. 76-875


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


67 Ill. App. 3d 512; 385 N.E.2d 39; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3852; 21 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 506; 24 Ill. Dec. 272; 19 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P8957



December 20, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. L. SHELDON BROWN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a handicapped man, others similarly situated, and the advocates for the handicapped, sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their class action suit for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendant employer under the Illinois Constitution and the Equal Opportunities for the Handicapped Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 65-21 et seq. (1975).


OVERVIEW: As a result of kidney transplant surgery, the handicapped man had work restrictions against heavy lifting. His application for employment with the employer was denied on the basis that he was not insurable. Plaintiffs brought a class action declaratory and injunctive relief suit against the employer, alleging disability employment discrimination in violation of Ill. Const. art. I, § 19 and the Act. The trial court dismissed the suit, and upon review, the court affirmed. The court held that the handicapped man's disability was of the nature which falls within the commonly understood meaning of the term "physical handicap" because it did not severely limit him in performing work-related functions. Thus, the court held, he was not handicapped within the meaning of the constitution or the Act. The court held that because the advocates' standing in the suit hung on the handicapped man's maintenance of the suit, the trial court properly dismissed them as well.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing plaintiffs' suit under the Illinois Constitution and the Equal Opportunities for the Handicapped Act.

People ex rel. Wordell v. Chicago


No. 77-296


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


67 Ill. App. 3d 321; 384 N.E.2d 894; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3815; 24 Ill. Dec. 27



December 13, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the City of Chicago and its Commissioner of Buildings (Illinois), appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted plaintiff landowners a writ of mandamus to compel issuance of a building permit.


OVERVIEW: The landowners owned two adjoining lots in the City, which they divided into three lots. They applied for a building permit from the City to construct a house on one of the lots. Defendants denied the permit because the division of the lots did not comply with the bulk regulations in Chicago, Ill., Mun. Ordinances ch. 194(A), art. 5, para. 5.7-2 (1974). The court determined that some of the consequences of the landowners' division of the improved zoning lots were exactly those intended to be prevented by the enactment of bulk regulations prescribing the width of the side yards. The court concluded that the landowners did not demonstrate a clear and unambiguous right to the issuance of the permit. The court determined that while their infraction of § 5.7-2 may have been slight, it made their claim for a permit equivocable. The court explained that the record did not disclose evidence that the application of § 5.7-2 through the strict enforcement of the side yard bulk regulation was unreasonable or arbitrary. The court noted that no evidence in the record overcame the presumption that the minimum width requirement for side yards bore a relationship to the public welfare.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1730 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Elmhurst Stamping & Mfg. Co. v. Amax Plating, Inc.


No. 77-974


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


67 Ill. App. 3d 257; 384 N.E.2d 839; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3806; 23 Ill. Dec. 932



December 11, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. MEYER H. GOLDSTEIN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff creditor appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied its motion for summary judgment and granted defendant successor corporation's motion for dismissal in the creditor's action for an outstanding debt owed by the successor corporation's predecessor.


OVERVIEW: The creditor sought to recover from the successor corporation an outstanding debt owed by the successor corporation's predecessor, which had been liquidated. The circuit court dismissed the creditor's action on the basis that the creditor had failed to file a timely claim with the receiver in liquidation proceedings against the predecessor and was therefore barred from relitigating the claim under §§ 87, 89 of the Business Corporation Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 32, para. 157.87, 157.89 (1977). On the creditor's appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that Illinois statutory law did not require service by summons for creditors because trial courts were vested with the discretion to determine what type of notice was to be afforded. Further, § 89 of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 32, para. 157.89 (1987), complied with state and federal due process requirements because due process required only that the form of notice should have been likely to be received and plain to understand. In the instant case, the notice provided the creditor afforded sufficient due process protections and indeed, it was shown that the creditor had actual notice. There was no error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which denied the creditor's motion for summary judgment and granted the successor corporation's motion for dismissal of the creditor's action for an outstanding debt.

People v. Conner


No. 77-1662


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


67 Ill. App. 3d 133; 384 N.E.2d 737; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3788; 23 Ill. Dec. 830



December 4, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. KENNETH R. WENDT, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for possession of more than 30 grams of heroin. She filed a motion to quash the search warrant and suppress the evidence on the basis that the evidence obtained was the result of an illegal search. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied the motion and convicted her of possession. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police obtained a search warrant for defendant's home based on information given by a reliable informant who had been present when a shipment of heroin was delivered there earlier that day. Early the next morning, police officers executed the search warrant by making an unannounced, forced entry into the premises by breaking through a second floor bedroom window. Police officers believed that the unusual method of executing the search warrant was necessary because burglar bars secured every door and window on the first floor, defendant had 12 dogs, and heroin was easily disposable. On appeal, defendant argued that there were no exigent circumstances that would have permitted such entry. The court agreed, holding that the fortress-like qualities of the premises, even when coupled with the probability of easily disposable heroin, did not make the entry by police officers within the standards of reasonableness required under the Fourth Amendment. Further, there was no evidence that defendant was expecting the police at the time of the raid and was attempting to dispose of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress.

Hamer v. Board of Education


No. 77-495


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


66 Ill. App. 3d 7; 383 N.E.2d 231; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3597; 22 Ill. Dec. 755



November 29, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. FRED H. GEIGER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff student challenged the decision from the Circuit Court, Lake County (Illinois), which dismissed the complaint in which the student sought declaratory judgment, an injunction, and other relief against defendant board of education (board) for alleged due process violations.


OVERVIEW: On a Friday, the student left school during the lunch period on an emergency matter without advising any teacher or staff member. On the following Monday, the student returned and presented to the school authorities a note from her mother excusing her absence of the preceding Friday afternoon. The student's grades were reduced by three percent as punishment for the unauthorized absence. On appeal, the student argued that there was no statutory authority for the reduction of a grade average of the student as a disciplinary sanction and that to do so deprived the student of both procedural and substantive due process. The court reversed the decision in favor of the board and held that the student's complaint was sufficient to require an appropriate response by the board and a hearing to determine whether her right to due process had been violated by procedural infirmities or substantively by the application of arbitrary grade reduction penalties that had no reasonable relationship to the disciplinary objectives sought to be attained by the board.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the board was reversed and the action was remanded.

Coleman v. Coleman


No. 77-1322


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


66 Ill. App. 3d 694; 384 N.E.2d 116; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3714; 23 Ill. Dec. 480



November 22, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 12, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. CHARLES J. GRUPP, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner daughter appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied her motion to substitute parties, to strike the special appearance of the executor of the estate of defendant father, and dismissed her petition to recover the support owed to plaintiff mother.


OVERVIEW: A divorce decree awarded custody of the daughter to the mother and ordered the father to pay support and alimony. Subsequently, the mother filed a petition, alleging that the father had not paid the support as ordered. She waived all claims to alimony and requested that a judgment be entered holding the father responsible for child support only from the entry of the divorce decree until her 21st birthday, which had occurred. The judgment was entered. The daughter, as administratrix of her mother's estate, sought to recover from the estate of her father the amount of support that had not been paid to the mother. She claimed support until the death of her mother. The trial court granted the father's executor leave to appear specially and dismissed the action. The court held that the mother's waiver, request for child support through the end of the child's minority, and the resulting judgment conclusively determined the extent of any monetary obligation the father owed under the divorce decree. Any subsequent attempt to relitigate that issue was barred. The court made no finding as to how the daughter could enforce that judgment, but ruled that the petition she brought was improper.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court was affirmed.

Valley View Community Unit School Dist. v. Cronin


No. 78-206


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


65 Ill. App. 3d 870; 382 N.E.2d 1298; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3568; 22 Ill. Dec. 600



November 21, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. THOMAS W. VINSON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school district challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which dismissed, for lack of jurisdiction, its action for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendants, the state superintendent of education and the state comptroller. The district sought to preclude defendants from withholding state aid from it.


OVERVIEW: The district was conducting a full-year school program under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 10-19.1 (1975). The district was notified by the state department of education that a substantial amount in state assistance would be withheld from the district in 1977-78 because it had not held school for 180 days in each of the school years 1973-74 and 1974-75. The district brought an injunctive action against defendants, alleging that their actions were illegal because Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, par. 10-19.1 (1975) provided for a special framework applicable to all-year schools and that the district had complied with such provisions. It also alleged that it did conduct school for 180 days in the years in question. A preliminary injunction was issued, and defendants answered, asserting immunity from suit. The trial court dismissed the action for lack of jurisdiction, and the district appealed. The court reversed, holding that where the suit charged that an officer of the state acted unconstitutionally, illegally, or without lawful authority, the conduct was deemed not to be that of the state, and the doctrine of sovereign immunity was not applicable. Thus, the trial court had jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, and it remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Harrawood


No. 77-556


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


66 Ill. App. 3d 163; 383 N.E.2d 707; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3630; 22 Ill. Dec. 899



November 21, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Wayne County; the Hon. ROBERT W. WHITMER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Wayne County (Illinois), which entered a judgment of conviction against him after a jury found him guilty of the offense of unlawful delivery of less than 200 grams of substance containing phencyclidine. The State filed a motion to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The State asserted that because defendant failed to file any post-trial motion, written or oral, he had waived consideration of all the errors he raised. The court noted that Illinois courts had long required some form of post-trial review in the trial court in order to preserve allegations of error for the purposes of appeal. Generally, the failure to raise an issue in a motion for a new trial constituted a waiver of that issue and defendant could not then assert such as a ground for reversal on appeal. However, exceptions to the application of the waiver rule had been made with regard to allegations of the insufficiency of the evidence that could have been raised for the first time on appeal. The court held that two of defendant's assertions went to the sufficiency of the evidence and therefore the waiver rule did not apply. However, the court did not find merit in either of defendant's contentions and concluded that there was sufficient evidence to support his conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1736 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Illinois Norml, Inc. v. Scott


No. 76-1082


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


66 Ill. App. 3d 633; 383 N.E.2d 1330; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3704; 23 Ill. Dec. 303



November 16, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. NATHAN M. COHEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cannabis advocates (advocates) challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their action against defendant, attorney general and others, for a declaratory judgment that the Cannabis Control Act (Act) (Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 701 (1975) et seq.) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The advocates sought to establish a right to possess and use cannabis in the home. On appeal, the advocates argued that the constitutional right of privacy protected the private use and possession of cannabis. The court affirmed the dismissal, holding that neither the United States Constitution nor the Illinois Constitution protected the private use and possession of cannabis. The court also held that the Act was constitutional because the legislature clearly had a rational basis for finding societal harm arising from the private use and possession of the drug. Because the Act was supported by scientific evidence, even though disputed by other studies, the Act had a rational basis and should have been upheld. The court further held that the trial court could have properly taken judicial notice of the harmfulness of cannabis because studies indicated such harmful effects as genetic damage, reduction in fertility, and even sterility.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the advocates' declaratory judgment action against defendants to overturn the Act was affirmed.

Landry v. Smith


No. 77-799


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


66 Ill. App. 3d 616; 384 N.E.2d 430; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3700; 23 Ill. Dec. 636



November 15, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. MILTON SOLOMON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tenant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted relief to defendant landlord on the landlord's suit for arrearages and to regain possession of the apartment.


OVERVIEW: The landlord delivered a five-day notice, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. Ch. 80, § 8 (1975), to the tenant that if the past-due rent was not paid within five days, her tenancy would have been terminated. The tenant allegedly offered to pay the rent, but it was refused. At trial, the tenant moved for a directed verdict because Evanston, Ill., Residential Landlord and Tenant Ordinance § 23 1/2-4.101(b) (1975) (ordinance) required a 10-day notice prior to eviction. The trial court denied the motion and granted judgment to the landlord. The tenant filed a motion to vacate the judgment, which was denied, and she appealed. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the ordinance was enacted after Ill. Rev. Stat. Ch. 80, § 8, which deemed it controlling. The court determined that an ordinance enacted by a home rule unit superseded a conflicting statute enacted prior to the effective date of the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had granted the landlord relief on his suit to repossess the apartment and recover arrearages.

Diamond Jim's, Inc. v. Department of Revenue


No. 77-607


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


66 Ill. App. 3d 613; 384 N.E.2d 428; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3699; 23 Ill. Dec. 634



November 15, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. EARL ARKISS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the taxpayer's complaint for administrative review. The taxpayer had filed its complaint to review two assessments issued by appellee Department of Revenue of the State of Illinois.


OVERVIEW: After filing his complaint, the taxpayer failed to comply with the requirement of Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 451 (1975) that it either file a bond or cause the circuit court to impress a lien upon its property in lieu of bond. On appeal, the taxpayer argued that the 20-day time requirement in para. 451 for filing a bond referred only to the time period within which the taxpayer could file a bond. If the time requirement also applied to the period in which the court could impress a lien in lieu of bond, the taxpayer asserted that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 451 (1975) was unconstitutionally vague and, therefore, deprived the taxpayer of its property without due process. The court held that para. 451 was neither unconstitutionally vague, nor violative of due process. The taxpayer's argument that the action of the department in seizing all of the taxpayer's assets made it impossible for the taxpayer to obtain a bond was not persuasive. The trial court could have imposed a lien on any property the taxpayer might have acquired in the future if the taxpayer had acted within the time limit established by the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court.

 

1739 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. McPherson


No. 14876


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


65 Ill. App. 3d 772; 382 N.E.2d 858; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3552; 22 Ill. Dec. 468



November 9, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Piatt County; the Hon. DONALD W. MORTHLAND, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Piatt County (Illinois), which found defendant guilty of the offense of failure to keep or produce controlled substance records in violation of § 406(a)(3) of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1406(a)(3) (1975).


OVERVIEW: The trial court found defendant guilty of the offense of failure to keep or produce controlled substance records. On appeal, the court stated that there was one dispositive issue: whether the recordkeeping requirement of § 312 of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1312(d) (1975), was unconstitutionally vague. The court stated that a law failed to meet the requirements of due process if it was so vague and standardless that it left the public uncertain as to the conduct it prohibited or left judges and jurors free to decide, without any legally fixed standards, what is or was not prohibited in any given case. The court stated that no numerical definition of "small quantities" was expressed in the statute. A "small quantity" could vary from one controlled substance to another, particularly in relation to potency, manufacturer's form, and dosage application. In this respect, a high degree of subjectivity and uncertainty was involved in a practitioner's determination of whether dispersing records were necessary. The court held that the use of the phrase "small quantities" rendered § 312 unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court reversed.

 

1740 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Central Illinois Public Service Co. v. Gibbel


No. 14923


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


65 Ill. App. 3d 890; 382 N.E.2d 846; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3571; 22 Ill. Dec. 456



November 8, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 12, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Macoupin County; the Hon. JOSEPH P. KOVAL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner public service company appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Macoupin County (Illinois), which awarded damages to respondent property owners in the company's eminent domain proceeding. The property owners cross-appealed, alleging that the company should not occupy their property during the pendency of the company's appeal.


OVERVIEW: The company brought a condemnation action in order to gain property on which to install new power lines. One witness, in describing damages beyond the required easement, calculated the replacement cost of a house in addition to the land on which it was situated. The jury accepted this and returned a verdict of $ 17,500 for damage to the property outside the easement strip. The company appealed, and the court reversed and remanded on this point. The court found that the house could not be valued separately from the land; instead, the improved value of the land as a whole had to be calculated. On the cross-appeal, the court found that § 13 of the Eminent Domain Act did apply to cases where the condemnor had initiated the appeal. Thus, a bond would sufficiently protect the property owners during the course of the appeal and the company's occupation of the land. Consequently, the court affirmed the remainder of the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the jury's determination as to the value of land actually taken and as to the damage to the part of the easement not occupied by structures. The court remanded for a new trial only on that part of the jury's verdict which dealt with damage to property outside the easement strip.

Aladdin's Castle, Inc. v. North Riverside


No. 77-1651


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


66 Ill. App. 3d 542; 383 N.E.2d 1316; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3687; 23 Ill. Dec. 289



November 8, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a village and its officials, appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found certain sections of a village ordinance void and inapplicable as applied to plaintiff amusement center operator.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance severely restricted the use of coin-operated amusement devices. The trial court found that portions of the ordinance bore no reasonable relation to the health, safety, or general welfare of the people of the village, and were therefore void as applied to the operator. On appeal, the court reversed, because the operator's liberty and property rights in the premises it leased were superseded by the valid exercise of police power to regulate the public safety. The removal of coin-operated amusement devices from a statutory list of gambling devices did not by implication repeal Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-42-2 (1977), which provided for municipal regulation over certain amusements, because gambling was not the only concern, and because repeal by implication occurred only when reconciliation was impossible. The court noted that the ordinances were clothed with presumptive validity which could only be rebutted by clear and affirmative evidence that their adoption was arbitrary or capricious. While the evidence was conflicting, the village had offered testimony tending to prove that the use of coin-operated amusement devices led to increased juvenile crime.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court, which held that the ordinances were void and inapplicable as applied to the operator.

Ming Kow Hah v. Stackler


No. 77-536


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


66 Ill. App. 3d 947; 383 N.E.2d 1264; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3751; 23 Ill. Dec. 237



November 3, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Opinion Filed on Denial of Rehearing December 29, 1978, Reported at 66 Ill. App. 3d 947 at 954.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff physician filed a complaint under the Administrative Review Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 264 et seq. (1975) for administrative review of defendant, Director of the Department of Registration and Education's, final order to revoke the physician's license. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) affirmed the order. The physician appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Director filed a complaint with the Medical Disciplinary Board charging that pursuant to the Medical Practice Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91, para. 16a(11) (1975), the physician's license should be revoked or suspended because his license had been revoked in a sister state. The Board recommended revocation, and the Director accepted the Board's findings. The circuit court affirmed, but stayed the revocation pending the outcome of the physician's appeal. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The Act clearly stated that revocation in a sister state was grounds for revocation by the Director. Failure of the sister state to observe technical rules in its revocation proceeding did not materially affect the physician's rights or result in a substantial injustice. The court did find a conflict between provisions in the Administrative Review Act and the Act regarding whether the revocation imposed by the Director could be stayed pending appeal. The Act prevailed, and the circuit court's order staying revocation of the physician's license pending appeal was reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed as to the revocation of the physician's license. The circuit court's stay order of the revocation pending appeal was reversed and the cause was remanded.

Rothner v. Chicago


No. 77-971


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


66 Ill. App. 3d 428; 383 N.E.2d 1218; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3672; 23 Ill. Dec. 191



October 31, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RAYMOND K. BERG, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city, commissioner, and corporation counsel, challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted declaratory and injunctive relief in favor of plaintiffs, nursing home officers and directors, in their action to prevent enforcement of a municipal code amendment requiring the installation of automatic sprinkler systems.


OVERVIEW: The city amended its municipal code to require nursing homes of fire-resistive or noncombustible construction to provide automatic sprinkler systems while it did not require the same of other institutional units. The trial court found that this amendment arbitrarily discriminated against nursing homes and declared the amendment violative of the equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the city, in the exercise of its police powers, had the authority to enact the amendment and to make it applicable to existing buildings. The amended ordinance did not effect a taking of private property without due process or just compensation because it was reasonably related to and tended to accomplish its purpose, which was to prevent deaths from fires in nursing homes. It also did not violate federal and state constitutional equal protection clauses because the classification of nursing homes was reasonably and fairly related to its purpose and did not invidiously or arbitrarily discriminate against nursing homes. There was no violation of the state constitutional prohibitions against special legislation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that granted declaratory and injunctive relief in favor of nursing home officers and directors in their action to prevent enforcement of a municipal code amendment requiring the installation of automatic sprinkler systems.

 

1744 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Moczarney


No. 77-238


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


65 Ill. App. 3d 410; 382 N.E.2d 544; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3505; 22 Ill. Dec. 224



October 20, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. SAUL A. EPTON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of involuntary manslaughter in the shooting death of another in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9 -- 3(a) (1975). Defendant was sentenced to probation and work release.


OVERVIEW: During a party at which defendant was intoxicated, he took a loaded gun onto a crowded back porch, where the victim was sitting on the railing. The gun went off while defendant was holding it, killing the victim. No witnesses testified that they saw the actual shooting. Defendant alleged that he tripped. On appeal, he contended that his guilt was not proved beyond a reasonable doubt. The court affirmed his conviction. Under para. 9 -- 3(a), a defendant was guilty of involuntary manslaughter if his acts were likely to cause death or great bodily harm, and the acts were performed recklessly. It had been held that carrying a loaded gun into a crowded space, particularly when one was intoxicated, was sufficient to support a finding of recklessness as contemplated by para. 9 -- 3(a). The trial court's statement that the incident may or may not have been an accident was not evidence that the trial court was not convinced beyond a reasonable doubt of defendant's guilt, particularly in light of the judge's other comments. The court also held that defendant was not denied an opportunity to make a closing argument. His counsel did not request the opportunity to make such an argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

People v. Silverstein


No. 77-1735


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


65 Ill. App. 3d 235; 382 N.E.2d 439; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3471; 22 Ill. Dec. 119



October 10, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. WALTER B. BIESCHKE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant trustees appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found them liable for personal property taxes in plaintiff State's action to recover personal property taxes for two taxable years.


OVERVIEW: The trustees, as individuals, along with a corporation, a bank, and the trustees entered into a voting trust agreement to assure that the stock of the bank, which formed the trust res, would be voted in accordance with the wishes of the trustees. Stock dividends paid by the bank were to be paid to the trustees, who in turn were required to distribute the dividends to the individual owners of the trust certificates. The State sued the trustees to recover personal property taxes, and the actions were consolidated. The trial court entered judgment against defendants, and they appealed, contending that they were exempt from the personal property tax because they held the stock in question as individuals. In affirming, the court noted a distinction regarding the imposition of personal property taxes upon property held in a fiduciary relationship that was created involuntarily and by operation of law and a voluntary fiduciary relationship. The court held that the voting trust did not come into being by operation of law. Rather, the parties to the agreement intentionally and voluntarily created it. Consequently, the trial court properly imposed personal property taxes on the trustees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1746 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stoutenborough


No. 14911


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


64 Ill. App. 3d 489; 381 N.E.2d 415; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3376; 21 Ill. Dec. 306



October 6, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. RODNEY A. SCOTT, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which sentenced him to seven years' imprisonment for his conviction for indecent liberties with a child and which denied his subsequent motion to withdraw his plea of guilty to that offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was allowed to withdraw his plea of not guilty and to enter a plea of guilty to the offense of indecent liberties with a child. He subsequently elected to be sentenced pursuant to the provisions of amendments to the Unified Code of Corrections. Defendant was sentenced to seven years' imprisonment. Thereafter, he moved to withdraw his guilty plea contending that the trial court failed to follow the new sentencing procedures. The trial court denied the motion. The court affirmed the sentence. The trial court, at the time of imposing sentence, had before it sufficient presentence information. In determining the sentence, the trial court was not bound by the usual rules of evidence but was allowed to search anywhere within reasonable bounds for facts which tended to aggravate or mitigate the offense. Moreover, defendant's history of prior delinquency or criminal activity was a factor for consideration in aggravation. Thus, there was no error in including information in the presentence report and allowing testimony at the sentencing hearing regarding defendant's alleged prior sexual contact with the complaining witness and other children for which he had not been charged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

In re Marriage of Marsh


No. 14853


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


64 Ill. App. 3d 572; 381 N.E.2d 804; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3390; 21 Ill. Dec. 477



October 6, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 8, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Douglas County; the Hon. WORTHY B. KRANZ, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner former wife challenged a decree entered in the Circuit Court of Douglas County (Illinois), which dissolved the marriage between the wife and respondent former husband, provided for the custody of their children, divided their property, and awarded the wife child support and maintenance. The wife appealed from the portion of the decree awarding the husband a tract of land and the husband cross-appealed from the award of maintenance.


OVERVIEW: The wife contended that the trial court erred in awarding the husband a tract of land based on a theory of repayment. On appeal, the court affirmed the order. The court ruled that a party's property was properly invaded upon a grant of divorce for the purpose of recognizing special equities in the property or to award alimony in gross. The court ruled that the trial court properly applied the new Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 101 et seq. (1977), and the wife was not deprived of due process. The court held that the trial court properly found that there was a repayment by the husband of the cost of the land. The court found that the wife made no objection when the husband's counsel made reference to repayment in his opening statement and when evidence of repayment was received. Further, the court found that the trial court properly awarded the wife maintenance to pursue her education. The court ruled that if a party was "otherwise without sufficient income," an award could be made for the time necessary to acquire sufficient education or training to enable the party seeking maintenance to find appropriate employment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Des Plaines v. Gacs


No. 76-304


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff City of Des Plaines sought review of a judgment entered in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which acquitted defendant, a city resident, of keeping pigeons within the city limits, a violation of Des Plaines, Ill., Code § 6-3-14.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found the resident not guilty on the ground that the ordinance was unconstitutional. On appeal, the City contended that the ordinance was a legitimate exercise of its police powers and was constitutional as applied to the resident. Reversing the trial court's judgment, the court ruled (1) that the ordinance was a proper exercise of the City's authority under Ill. Rev. Vill. of S. Elgin v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 77-416


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


64 Ill. App. 3d 565; 381 N.E.2d 778; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3389; 21 Ill. Dec. 451



October 2, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PETITION for review of order of Pollution Control Board.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, village and residents (petitioners), sought review of an order of the Illinois Pollution Control Board (board), which denied their request to withdraw their complaint and dismissed it with prejudice. Petitioners sought revocation of permits issued by respondent, Illinois Environmental Protection Agency, to respondent waste management corporation for development and operation of a sanitary landfill site adjacent to the village.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners filed a complaint with the board for revocation of permits issued by the agency for development of a landfill. Petitioners then requested to withdraw the complaint with leave to reinstate it or, alternatively, to continue the matter. The board denied the request, dismissed the complaint with prejudice, and stated it did not favor forum shopping and that the hearing process for dismissal did not require an actual adjudicatory hearing. Petitioners appealed, and the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the board abused its discretion by arbitrarily depriving petitioners of the hearing to which they were entitled under the board's Procedural Rule 503. The alleged forum shopping was petitioners' challenges to the constitutionality of the procedures for issuance of landfill permits. Petitioners were entitled to have sought such injunctive and judicial relief. Also, the allegation of undue delay was not a valid ground for dismissal. Under § 52 of the Civil Procedure Act, Ill. Rev. Stat., ch. 110, para. 52 (1975), the agency had no more discretion to refuse petitioners' motion for voluntary dismissal than would a court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the board, which dismissed petitioners' complaint, which sought revocation of a landfill permit, with prejudice and denied petitioners' motion to withdraw their complaint without prejudice. The court remanded to the board for further proceedings.

Greenock v. Rush Presbyterian St. Luke's Medical Center


Nos. 77-1016, 78-524 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


65 Ill. App. 3d 266; 382 N.E.2d 321; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3478; 22 Ill. Dec. 1



September 27, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 6, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JAMES C. MURRAY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital petitioned for leave to appeal a certified question after the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied its motion to dismiss plaintiff administrator's medical malpractice action. The hospital filed a collection action for unpaid services to plaintiff's decedent. Counter-plaintiff filed a counterclaim alleging that the collection action was wrongfully brought. The collection and malpractice actions were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The hospital's motion to dismiss claimed that the administrator's malpractice action was time-barred by the Wrongful Death Act's two-year filing period under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 70, § 2 (1975). The circuit court denied the motion. It found that the action was brought properly under § 17 of the Limitations Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 83, para. 18 (1975), because of the pendency of the counter-plaintiff 's counterclaim in the collection action. On appeal, the court found that § 17 did not rescue the administrator's malpractice action because the filing of a counterclaim in an action unrelated to the allegations in a later, independent action did not toll the running of the statute of limitations on the later action. The administrator also claimed that § 21.1 of the Limitations Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 83, para. 21.1 (1975), superseded the two-year limitation period of the Wrongful Death Act in actions alleging malpractice. On appeal, the court disagreed because under § 21.1, the date of the claimant's knowledge of the death commenced the running of the statute. The court reversed the order of the circuit court denying the hospital's motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the circuit court denying the hospital's motion to dismiss the administrator's medical malpractice action.

Fure v. Sherman Hospital


No. 77-177


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


64 Ill. App. 3d 259; 380 N.E.2d 1376; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3302; 21 Ill. Dec. 50



September 25, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 20, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. MARVIN D. DUNN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, surviving spouse and estate of decedent (estate), challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which dismissed the estate's complaint against appellees, hospital, physicians, and related entities (hospital), for wrongful death.


OVERVIEW: The estate filed a wrongful death suit against the hospital related to the decedent's care. The hospital filed a motion to dismiss the complaint on the ground that the action was not brought within two years of the date of the death, as required by the Wrongful Death Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 70, para. 2(c) (1975). The estate argued that it was not advised of the actual cause of death until a later date and that it had acted within the limitations period. The trial court granted the hospital's motion to dismiss. The estate appealed, alleging that the discovery rule applied to an action for wrongful death. The court determined that, under the Limitations Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 83, para. 22.1 (1971), the discovery rule applied to a medical malpractice action. The court held that the discovery rule applied to the case because although the date of death was known and did not have to be discovered, the negligence behind the death was not discovered until sometime after the date of death.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part the dismissal of the estate's action, and remanded for further proceedings.

Motion Picture Appeal Bd. v. S. K. Films


No. 78-1


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


65 Ill. App. 3d 217; 382 N.E.2d 103; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3469; 21 Ill. Dec. 809



September 22, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. DONALD J. O'BRIEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant film company appealed a judgment entered in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which issued an injunction requested by plaintiffs, a city's Motion Picture Appeal Board and its members, pursuant to Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code ch. 155, para. 7.2, enjoining the film company from showing a film in the city's theaters to persons under the age of 18 years.


OVERVIEW: The film company created a film with the subject matter of making a pornographic movie. The film company applied for a permit to exhibit the film in the city to general audiences. The city's rating system provided for permits to allow viewing by all audiences or only by those over the age of 18. The film was viewed by the police department, which refused the permit. The film company appealed to the board, which screened the film and conducted a hearing at which evidence was introduced by both parties. The board affirmed the denial of a permit to show the film to anyone under the age of 18 years of age and, pursuant to § 7.2, filed a complaint for an injunction. The trial court reviewed the matter, including the film, de novo and granted the injunction. The court held that the city's ordinance met due process requirements through its stringent requirements of review, placing the burden on the board at all stages of the proceedings to establish the reasons for denying a permit. The board met its burden of establishing that the film was obscene with respect to children and that a general permit should not have been issued.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting the injunction.

 

1753 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Elliot v. Board of Education


No. 63062


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


64 Ill. App. 3d 229; 380 N.E.2d 1137; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3298; 20 Ill. Dec. 928



September 13, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. DANIEL A. COVELLI, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff handicapped student appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that dismissed the student's complaint seeking a declaration that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 14-7.02 (1977) was unconstitutional in that it limited the amount of tuition which the state, through its school districts, must pay for the special education of handicapped student who were excluded from public schools and received a private education.


OVERVIEW: The complaint also sought injunctive relief that mandated the school districts to pay the full tuition of all handicapped public school students attending private schools. Following the handicapped child's exclusion from the public schools, his mother was required to pay the difference between the tuition charged by the private school and the amount contributed by defendant Board of Education of the City of Chicago (board). The court reasoned that the state constitution, Ill. Const. art. X, § 1 (1970), established the right of handicapped persons to tuition-free education through the secondary level. Parents and guardians were not required to pay tuition for the education of their handicapped child. No discretion was left with the legislature to deny free education to the public or to require any state resident to pay for schooling through the secondary level. Thus, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 14-7.02 (1977) violated the provisions of the education article of the state constitution when it deprived the handicapped student of a tuition-free education. The court reversed and remanded the case on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the handicapped student's complaint alleging that the law was unconstitutional when it limited the amount of tuition that the state would pay for the private education of handicapped students excluded from public schools. The court remanded the case to the trial court.

Lurie v. Skokie


No. 78-408


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


64 Ill. App. 3d 217; 380 N.E.2d 1120; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3297; 20 Ill. Dec. 911



September 12, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment in favor of appellees, village, its president, and developer (village), in the landowners' suit seeking to declare various ordinances of the village unconstitutional, invalid, and void.


OVERVIEW: Landowners filed a complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief against the village, seeking to declare various ordinances of the village unconstitutional, invalid, and void. The challenged ordinances were passed to permit the sale of certain municipal property to a developer for the construction of low-income housing for the elderly. The trial court granted partial summary judgment for the village pursuant to § 57 of the Civil Practice Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 57 (1975). At the close of the landowners' case, the trial court entered judgment for the village. The landowners contended that the trial court erred in granting partial summary judgment in favor of the village because the local ordinance was not validly enacted. The court found the issue moot because the ordinance did not apply to the case. The landowners also contended that there was a conspiracy between the developer and the village to choose the developer as the successful bidder of the subject property. The court held that the circumstances of the case did not support a finding that there was a conspiracy between the village and the developer regarding the bids on the subject land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the village in the landowners' suit challenging a village ordinance and alleging a conspiracy.

 

1755 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Shaw


No. 14718


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


63 Ill. App. 3d 227; 379 N.E.2d 949; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3163; 20 Ill. Dec. 116



August 18, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. DONALD W. MORTHLAND, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, in Macon County (Illinois), which convicted her of obstructing justice.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with obstructing justice following a warrantless search of her residence by the police that resulted in the capture of her brothers who were being sought pursuant to warrants for armed robbery. The charge against her was based on statements made by her prior to the search to the effect that her brothers were not in her residence. Defendant asserted that the search was illegal thereby making the evidence obtained inadmissible and that the evidence presented at trial was not sufficient to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt she was guilty of obstructing justice. The court agreed with defendant's latter contention. The totality of circumstances shows that defendant made a voluntary and knowing consent to the search, thus, the search was legal and the evidence obtained was admissible. However, the court held that it could not conclude that the presence of the brothers alone established beyond a reasonable doubt an intent on the part of defendant to obstruct justice as there was evidence that defendant did not believe her brothers were in the house.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court that convicted defendant of obstructing justice.

 

1756 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cowherd


No. 14743


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


63 Ill. App. 3d 229; 380 N.E.2d 21; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3164; 20 Ill. Dec. 344



August 18, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. RODNEY A. SCOTT, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed, sentence modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of armed robbery pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18-2 (1975) and imposed a sentence of 10 to 30 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction, alleging that the trial court failed to instruct sua sponte that the intent to permanently deprive the victims of property was an essential element of the offense, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel as a result of joint representation, and that the trial court imposed a more severe sentence because of its belief that defendant committed perjury. On appeal, the court held that the trial court's failure to give an instruction on defendant's intent was harmless error because the evidence supported a finding that defendant had the requisite intent. Regarding the issue of effective assistance, the court found that there was no conflict of interest between defendants that resulted in a denial of effective assistance of counsel. The court found that defendant was not tried with his co-defendant and that no representations of conflict of interest were ever raised. Regarding defendant's sentence, the court held that because defendant did not admit that he committed perjury and because defendant was never convicted of perjury, the trial court improperly enhanced defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for armed robbery, but modified his sentence by reducing it to 7 to 15 years in prison.

 

1757 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. McCord


No. 77-31


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


63 Ill. App. 3d 542; 379 N.E.2d 1325; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3158; 20 Ill. Dec. 257



August 9, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. DELMAR KOEBEL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from judgments of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) after jury verdicts found both defendants, a husband and wife, guilty of unlawful delivery of a controlled substance, a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(a)(6) (1973).


OVERVIEW: After their indictment, defendants chose to wait for a state supreme court decision before proceeding to trial. At trial, one attorney represented both defendants. A chemist testified that the substance defendants were selling was amphetamines, based on his testing of one percent of the pills. Defendants were convicted. The wife filed a supplemental brief alleging ineffective assistance of counsel. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that defendants were not denied the right to a speedy trial because they acquiesced in the delay between indictment and trial. The court determined that the chemist's opinion was properly admitted and that it was for the jury to determine the weight to be given the expert opinion in light of the methods by which it was reached. The court determined that the wife's right to effective representation was not violated by the joint representation of her and the husband. The court noted that the defense strategy was clearly to argue that the husband should take the blame in the hope that the jury would exonerate the wife. The court held that the trial court did not have a duty to ask defendants if they wanted or needed separate counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which convicted defendants of unlawful delivery of a controlled substance.

People v. Mendoza


No. 14763


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


62 Ill. App. 3d 774; 379 N.E.2d 380; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3070; 19 Ill. Dec. 716



August 4, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. WILLIAM T. CAISLEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction by the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) for retail theft over $ 150.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with stealing items from a store. On appeal, she contended that the valuation provision of the retail theft act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16A-2.2 (1975), was unconstitutional because it constituted special legislation. The court rejected this argument, stating that the valuation provision of the retail theft act was not special legislation, but was in fact a clarification of the theft statute with reference to retail items. The court also rejected defendant's argument that the trial court erred in admitting the merchandise into evidence because the chain of custody was not established and also because the witnesses did not specifically identify the price tags as being unchanged from the time of the offense. The prosecution did not have to prove the chain of custody because the items were identified by the security officers when they testified. The witnesses were not required to testify that the price tags were substantially unchanged because the price tags were attached to the exhibit at the inventory as well as at trial. Defendant's retail theft conviction was upheld.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
