South Elgin v. Waste Management of Illinois, Inc.


No. 77-208


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


62 Ill. App. 3d 815; 379 N.E.2d 349; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3078; 19 Ill. Dec. 685



July 28, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 30, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. BARRY PUKLIN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, village, county, and state attorney, appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which granted the motions to dismiss filed by defendants, Waste Management of Illinois and the Environmental Protection Agency (agency), in plaintiffs' action for an injunction seeking to have certain developmental and operational permits issued declared void, and to enjoin operation of a landfill under the permits.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought an injunction to enjoin certain developmental and operational permits issued by the agency declared void, and to have waste management enjoined from taking any action to operate a landfill under the permits. Defendants filed motions to dismiss, and the trial court granted the motions, sustaining the constitutionality of the applicable provisions of the Environmental Protection Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1001 et seq. (1977), and dismissing the complaint for failure of plaintiffs to exhaust their administrative remedies before the Illinois Pollution Control Board. Plaintiffs appealed, and the court affirmed. The court concluded that plaintiffs failed to show that the act was unconstitutional, and the court found that it did not create any unreasonable classification which would run afoul of the requirements of equal protection. The court concluded that the act did not violate due process, and the agency did not have to hold an adversarial hearing, with notice to any conceivably interested third party, prior to issuing a permit for a sanitary landfill. The court concluded that plaintiffs had an adequate administrative remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of the motion to dismiss plaintiffs' action seeking to have certain developmental and operational permits issued declared void, and to enjoin operation of a landfill under the permits.

 

1760 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jovicevic


No. 77-127


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


63 Ill. App. 3d 106; 379 N.E.2d 665; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3011; 19 Ill. Dec. 793



July 26, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 6, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CURRY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Three defendants, two brothers and their co-defendant, challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found them all guilty of aggravated battery causing great bodily harm. All defendants claimed error in a refusal to give a requested instruction and the imposition of a prison sentence instead of a probation term. The brothers also asserted a conflict in a joint representation by their retained counsel.


OVERVIEW: The brothers and their codefendant contended that the trial court erred in holding that § 115-4(f) of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-4(f) (1975), was unconstitutional and in conflict with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 234, which related to voir dire. The court held that this ruling was correct because the statute had been declared void. The court also held that each defendant was accountable for the criminal acts of all because they were all positively identified as participants in the beating. Further, the trial court fully and properly instructed the jury on the law of accountability, and defendants could not complain where they failed to tender their own instruction. Moreover, the court rejected the brothers' conflict of interest argument based on their unequal culpability in the aggravated battery. A joint representation by their privately retained counsel did not create a conflict where one brother admitted to striking the final, most serious blow because it actually benefited the other less culpable brother. Finally, the prison sentences imposed by the trial court were appropriate based on defendants' attitudes and the seriousness of the attack.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments and sentences of the circuit court.

 

1761 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Swansey


No. 77-109


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


62 Ill. App. 3d 1015; 379 N.E.2d 1279; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3045; 20 Ill. Dec. 211



July 20, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JAMES M. BAILEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for murder and rape. Defendant sought a new trial and contended that evidence should have been suppressed due to an illegal search, the finding that defendant was sane at the time of the murder was contrary to the weight of the evidence, a competency hearing should have been held, and his attorneys were incompetent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and rape. The court affirmed on appeal, and concluded that defendant was not entitled to a new trial. The court held that the trial court did not err in failing to suppress evidence because it was obtained during a legal, consensual search. The police had searched defendant's home under the consent of defendant's mother. The next day, the police entered defendant's home after defendant's 13 year old brother had invited them in. After the brother advised the police of a good hiding spot in the house, the police conducted the search out of concern that the victim may still have been alive. The brother had the capacity and authority to consent to the search, and his consent had been given voluntarily. The evidence supported the trial court's finding that defendant was sane at the time of the murder. Also, there was no error in the trial court's failure to sua sponte order a fitness hearing to determine whether defendant was competent to stand trial. Finally, defendant failed to establish that he had been denied a fair trial by the incompetence of his trial counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction for murder and rape. Defendant was not entitled to a new trial because the challenged evidence was obtained during a consensual search. The court also upheld the finding that defendant was sane at the time of the killing. The trial court did not err by failing to sua sponte order a fitness hearing, and defendant failed to establish that the trial counsel was incompetent.

 

1762 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mosley


No. 77-217


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


63 Ill. App. 3d 437; 379 N.E.2d 1240; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3142; 20 Ill. Dec. 172



July 13, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. ROBERT L. GAGEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged an order from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which granted defendant's request to suppress two tape recordings that were made in the course of an investigation by the Illinois Bureau of Investigation (IBI) and which further suppressed the testimony of any person concerning either of the conversations contained in the tape recordings.


OVERVIEW: The IBI was investigating alleged payoffs from tavern owners to city officials. Defendant was charged with bribery, intimidation, official misconduct, and conspiracy to permit gambling as a result of his conversations with an IBI agent that were tape recorded with the agent's consent. The trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress the tape recordings because of noncompliance with the eavesdropping statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 14-2(a) (1975). The trial court also ordered the suppression of testimony concerning the conversations. On appeal, the court reversed. The statute did not require a written request specifically naming defendant or a request that originated with the state's attorney's office. One of the parties to the conversation consented to the taping and the state's attorney authorized the eavesdropping. The exception of § 14-2(a) was established and the recording should have been admitted. The agent's testimony about the conversations was admissible even if the tape recordings were properly suppressed. His testimony was derived from a source completely independent of the recordings and was admissible without regard to the legality of the tapings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the suppression of the tape recordings, which were made with the approval of the state's attorney and to which one of the parties to the conversation had consented. The court also reversed the suppression of independent testimony regarding the content of the tapes. The action was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1763 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Warren Realty Co. v. Illinois Dep't of Revenue


No. 77-1710


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


62 Ill. App. 3d 450; 379 N.E.2d 100; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2970; 19 Ill. Dec. 585



July 10, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. EARL ARKISS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Missouri corporation challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed its suit for refund of assessment of income taxes and penalties against defendant, the Illinois Department of Revenue. At issue was the constitutionality of the Illinois Income Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 1-101 et seq. (1977).


OVERVIEW: The corporation deducted a valuation limitation amount from its federal taxable income in arriving at its net income for Illinois tax purposes. The Department disallowed the deduction on the ground that a corporate taxpayer was not entitled to it. The corporation paid the tax claimed as due under protest and sued for a refund. The trial court dismissed the suit. The corporation argued that the Act violated Ill. Const. art. IX, § 3(a) (1970) by allowing individuals certain deductions not available to corporations and that the Act violated the Illinois Constitution to the extent that it taxed depreciation which was not allowed as a deduction, so that the tax was not measured by income. The court stated that Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 (1970) recognized that there would be differences in the deductions granted to various classes of taxpayers and merely imposed a requirement of reasonableness on these deductions. Any variance that existed in the case was extremely limited in its application. A tax on appreciation occurring prior to the effective date of a taxing act, but not realized until after that date, was a tax on income within the authority granted by Ill. Const. art. IX (1970).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

People v. Wilson


No. 77-416


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


61 Ill. App. 3d 1029; 378 N.E.2d 378; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3128; 18 Ill. Dec. 914



July 10, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Williamson County; the Hon. WILLIAM A. LEWIS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that he was unconstitutionally placed in double jeopardy when he was indicted for "felony murder" and convicted in 1977 because the state had nolle prossed the original 1970 "felony murder" indictment after a guilty verdict had been returned. The court affirmed. The court did not believe that nolle prossing the "felony murder" count actually had any effect, much less a double jeopardy implication. The court found that count was redundant after the verdicts were returned because it represented merely another theory of murder. The court agreed that the county court's order was in fact a premature ruling that the jury would not be instructed on "felony murder" and as such was not appealable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

1765 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stillman


No. 14481


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


61 Ill. App. 3d 446; 378 N.E.2d 360; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2856; 18 Ill. Dec. 896



July 7, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Pike County; the Hon. FRED W. REITHER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered a plea of guilty in the Circuit Court of Pike County (Illinois) to the offense of murder and was sentenced to 75 to 225 years' imprisonment. Defendant filed a timely motion pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d) to withdraw his plea. When that motion was denied, defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to murder. He had made three statements to the police about the occurrence of the murder prior to the entry of his plea, and another statement during sentencing. All four statements were substantially different and implicated defendant in varying degrees. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in accepting his plea without an adequate showing of a factual basis and by requiring him to carry the burden of proving his lack of fitness to stand trial when a hearing was held on that issue. The court disagreed and affirmed his conviction. The court noted that the mental state for the murder charged was intent. Defendant's claim that he was intoxicated was first made at sentencing, long after the plea was accepted. And, the trial court was not required to accept defendant's motion to withdrawal his plea merely because he stated a defense for the first time at sentencing. Especially in light of the fact that his testimony in support of that defense could be impeached by his prior statements. The court also held that because the only evidence on defendant's competency proved that he was fit to stand trial, a directed verdict of fitness was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Rincon v. License Appeal Com.


No. 76-1172


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


62 Ill. App. 3d 600; 378 N.E.2d 1281; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2992; 19 Ill. Dec. 406; 100 A.L.R.3d 840



July 6, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RAYMOND K. BERG, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tavern owner appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed a decision of defendant city license appeal commission to sustain the revocation of the tavern owner's liquor license by the local liquor control commissioner.


OVERVIEW: Proceedings were initiated by the local liquor control commissioner to revoke the retail liquor license of the tavern owner. He was found guilty of committing two aggravated batteries upon patrons, through an agent, and of being in possession of an unregistered weapon. On appeal, the tavern owner contended that the Dramshop Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 153 (1977) created an unconstitutional classification by providing different procedures based on population for reviewing revocation orders of local liquor control commissioners. Section 8 of article VII of the Act provided that appeals from all orders of local liquor control commissioners in municipalities of 500,000 or more were to be determined by the License Appeal Commission. The court held that the classification based on population was not arbitrary or discriminatory. De novo reviews in densely populated municipalities would be unreasonable. The tavern owner also urged that the commissioner's decision was contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence. The court found that the commissioner's decision was supported by substantial competent evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the city license appeal commission that sustained the revocation of the tavern owner's liquor license.

Knupper v. Property Tax Appeal Bd.


No. 77-207


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


61 Ill. App. 3d 884; 378 N.E.2d 340; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3108; 18 Ill. Dec. 876



July 3, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of De Kalb County; the Hon. CARL A. SWANSON, JR., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nursery owners sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of De Kalb County (Illinois) that sustained appellee property tax appeal board's assessment on the nursery properties. The assessment was based upon Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 506 and the nursery owners claimed that the different tax treatment that was accorded the stock of nurseries was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The lower court sustained the property tax appeal board's assessment on the nursery owners' properties. The court found no merit to the nursery owners' claim that the different tax treatment provided for nurseries as opposed to other agricultural crops was violative of the equal protection provisions of the state and federal constitutions. The court found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 506 did not violate the fundamental concept of equal protection because there was no clear showing that the state's tax scheme was arbitrary and unsupportable by any set of facts. The court found that there were real and significant differences between nursery stock and other growing crops, and that those differences more than justified the different tax treatment accorded to each.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court that sustained the property tax appeal board's assessment of the nursery owners' properties.

People v. Virgin


No. 77-138


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


60 Ill. App. 3d 964; 377 N.E.2d 846; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2766; 18 Ill. Dec. 361



June 22, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. JOHN F. MICHELA, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois), which, following a bench trial, convicted defendant on charges of battery and cruelty to a child. Defendant was sentenced to a term of from one to three years imprisonment on the basis of the cruelty to a child conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, among other things, that the child abuse statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 2368 (1977) was unconstitutionally vague and did not give proper notice of what conduct was proscribed, that the State did not prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty of cruelty to a child, and that the convictions of defendant for battery and cruelty to a child were based upon the same physical acts and, therefore, the battery conviction should be vacated. The court found that defendant inflicted extensive physical injuries upon her child by striking the child with a wooden switch. The court concluded that such conduct was clearly proscribed by the statute and the court would not consider the statute's application to other borderline circumstances, which might be advanced theoretically. The court concluded that there was sufficient evidence presented to allow the trial court to find defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. But battery was a lesser included offense of the crime of cruelty to a child and therefore, the conviction for battery could not stand.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction on the charge of cruelty to a child was affirmed but her battery conviction was vacated.

People v. Foy


Nos. 77-1968, 77-1969, 77-1970 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


61 Ill. App. 3d 137; 377 N.E.2d 1282; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2804; 18 Ill. Dec. 646



June 22, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ROBERT J. COLLINS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a judgment entered in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), dismissing counts of an indictment charging defendant with violations of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act after defendant had claimed that phendimetrazine was not a controlled substance under § 208 of the Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1208(b)(6) (1975).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with numerous violations of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act. At the time defendant allegedly committed the offenses charged in the indictments, § 208(b)(6) of the Act contained the term "pheudimetrazine," not "phendimetrazine," as alleged in the indictments. The State maintained that the term was simply misspelled and, alternatively, that the substance was controlled by virtue of § 201(d) of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1201(d), which provided for scheduling of substances previously scheduled under Federal law. The trial court dismissed the counts of the indictment concerning "phendimetrazine." On appeal the court concluded that the counts of the indictments charging defendant with possessing and illegally dispensing phendimetrazine did state an offense under § 208(b)(6). The court found that the intent of the legislature was to ban phendimetrazine and, through some legislative oversight, the technical term, contained in the statute along with many other technical terms, was simply misspelled. The court also held that the statute, despite the misspelling, was not unconstitutionally vague and did not deny defendant due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing the counts of the indictment and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

1770 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Taylor


No. 77-230


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


61 Ill. App. 3d 37; 377 N.E.2d 838; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2785; 18 Ill. Dec. 353



June 21, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. JOHN S. GHENT, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which convicted him of burglary, armed robbery, and rape after admitting into evidence his oral confession.


OVERVIEW: An elderly woman was raped and robbed during a burglary. After defendant was arrested for the offenses, he requested an attorney. He left a message at an attorney's office. While waiting for the attorney's return call, the police questioned defendant. The attorney called, refusing to accept the case. Upon additional questioning, defendant signed a written confession stating that he went to the victim's house but never entered. Later that day, he signed a second confession, stating that he committed all but the rape. The next morning, he orally stated that his second confession was correct except that he also committed the rape. The trial court suppressed the first and second confessions but admitted the third. Defendant was convicted of armed robbery and rape. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, finding that upon defendant's request for an attorney, all questioning should have ceased. Because defendant's request for an attorney had not sufficiently dissipated by the time he made his third confession, which related to the second confession, that confession should not have been admitted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which convicted him of burglary, armed robbery, and rape after admitting into evidence his confession to the crimes.

 

1771 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Raicevich


No. 77-335


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


61 Ill. App. 3d 143; 377 N.E.2d 1266; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2806; 18 Ill. Dec. 630



June 21, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 27, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Warren County; the Hon. STEPHEN G. EVANS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Warren County (Illinois), which entered an order suppressing all handguns seized, except the handgun identified by serial number, during the execution of a search warrant at defendant's apartment. Defendant cross appealed seeking the suppression the handgun identified by serial number on grounds that it was unlawfully seized as part of an unreasonable search of defendant's premises.


OVERVIEW: While posing as a buyer, an officer obtained the serial number of one of many handguns in defendant's possession, which defendant admitted were all probably stolen. The serial number later revealed that the gun and many others were stolen from a gun shop, on which basis a search warrant was obtained for the seizure of the identified handgun and "any other handguns which may be stolen." Defendant contended that the failure to particularize the items to be seized converted the search into a general one. The court held that the generic description in this case was sufficient to comply with the Fourth Amendment. The court further held that a general description was permissible for items requiring some discernment, and even after-the-fact testing, but having at bottom, an objective basis for recognition. The court reasoned that the "stolen guns" in this case were easily verifiable as such by the officer's list of stolen guns. The court concluded that when the circumstances make an exact description of items impossible, the officer could only be expected to describe the generic class of items to be seized.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the judgment refusing to suppress the identified handgun, reversed that part of the judgment that suppressed the other handguns, and remanded for further proceedings.

Hamer v. Dixon


No. 77-83


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


61 Ill. App. 3d 30; 377 N.E.2d 820; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2783; 18 Ill. Dec. 335



June 15, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. HARRY D. STROUSE, JR., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which denied the taxpayer leave to file a first amended complaint in his action seeking to enjoin the disbursement of public funds by defendants, the state treasurer and the state comptroller.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer brought an action pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 102, paras. 11-16 (1975), to restrain and enjoin the disbursement of public moneys by defendants. The trial court denied the taxpayer leave to file a first amended complaint. On appeal, the court stated that the sole issue on appeal was whether the trial court erred in denying the taxpayer's request to file his proposed amended complaint. The taxpayer's basic contention was that the trial court should have granted leave to file because the request was neither frivolous nor malicious. The court held that the taxpayer's arguments constituted an impermissible collateral attack on the constitutionality and propriety of existing differences in inter-county uniformity of assessments. The Supreme Court of Illinois had upheld such assessments. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the taxpayer leave to file his amended complaint where the taxpayer's amended complaint amounted to a collateral attack on the prior judgment by the Supreme Court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1773 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Skokie Federal Sav. & Loan Asso. v. Illinois Sav. & Loan Bd.


Nos. 76-953, 76-954, 76-955, 76-956, 76-1168 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


61 Ill. App. 3d 977; 378 N.E.2d 1090; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 3122; 19 Ill. Dec. 215



June 15, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant federally-chartered savings and loan associations sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed decisions of appellees, the Illinois Savings and Loan Board and the Commissioner of Savings and Loan Associations, permitting state-chartered savings and loan associations to compete in appellants' respective market areas.


OVERVIEW: The Board allowed five state-charted associations to compete in the same market areas covered by the federally-charted associations. That action was affirmed in the circuit court. The court affirmed in four of the cases, but reversed and remanded the fifth case. The statutes in question permissibly granted discretion to the Commissioner to make decisions regarding the relocation of state-chartered savings and loan associations. The criteria for establishment of a facility requiring that "a need exist" and "undue injury not occur" were set forth in the statute pertaining to establishment or relocation of an association, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 32, paras. 724, 744(h) (1975). The federally-charted associations asserted that these criteria for establishment of a facility were vague and uncertain and did not constitute controlling standards to be applied by the Commissioner. But the court held that these concepts were legislatively recognized as not subject to precise definition. The criteria were established in the four cases that were affirmed but not in the fifth case, which was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed four of the judgments of the circuit court. The court vacated the judgment in the fifth matter and the cause with directions to dismiss the complaint for administrative review.

 

1774 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nichols


No. 76-295


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


60 Ill. App. 3d 919; 377 N.E.2d 815; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2759; 18 Ill. Dec. 330



June 14, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. PATRICK M. BURNS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted in the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois) for forgery and theft by deception. The trial court denied defendant's motion for mistrial on the ground that the state failed to fulfill the requirements under § 2-7 of the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702-7 (1975) for prosecution of a minor. Defendant was convicted as charged. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 17 years old at the time of alleged offense. The criminal indictment was suppressed and a capias was issued but not returned until nearly three years later. The cause did not proceed to trial until an additional eight months. The total delay between indictment and arrest was 33 months. The trial court denied the mistrial motion on the ground that the Illinois Supreme Court's ruling that § 2-7 did not apply to 17 years did apply retroactively to allegations against defendant. The court reversed and held that the trial court erred by refusing to grant a mistrial. The state was required to have first filed a petition with the juvenile court alleging the offenses committed before the state had discretion as to which court the minor could have been tried in. Because the supreme court's ruling affected substantive rights under a procedural statute, the ruling could not have applied retroactively. Second, although defendant failed to assert in a post-trial motion alleging denial of her speedy trial rights, violation of that right was plain error. The state conceded the delay was caused by its incompetence. The delay was exceedingly long and prejudiced defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for mistrial and reversed defendant's convictions for fraud and theft by deception. The court dismissed the indictment.

Haymond v. Haymond


No. 77-247


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


60 Ill. App. 3d 969; 377 N.E.2d 563; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2767; 18 Ill. Dec. 274



June 13, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Stephenson County; the Hon. EVERETT LAUGHLIN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Stephenson County (Illinois), which confirmed certain prior orders that reduced to judgment arrearages and temporary support payments to appellee former wife under an earlier interlocutory order of the trial court.


OVERVIEW: A former wife brought a divorce action and sought temporary support from her former husband in Illinois. The former wife obtained various orders reducing arrearages and temporary support payments against her husband. Next, the husband brought a divorce action in West Virginia, his state of new residence, and was ordered to pay his former wife support. The former wife then brought an action in Illinois seeking to hold her former husband in contempt and further reduce arrearages owed by former husband. For the first time, the former husband attempted to contest the matter in Illinois through entering a special appearance. Illinois granted the former wife's action, and the former husband appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that: (1) even though the wife failed to allege that jurisdictional acts forming the basis for divorce had occurred in Illinois, the defect was not fatal; (2) alleged condonation of acts of cruelty forming the basis for divorce did not deprive the court of jurisdiction; and (3) there was no error in the court's refusal to act on issues of setoff against the judgment on arrearages and temporary support that were pending before an out-of-state court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the former wife.

Johnston v. Bloomington


No. 14700


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


61 Ill. App. 3d 209; 377 N.E.2d 1174; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2819; 18 Ill. Dec. 538



June 9, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 31, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. CHARLES E. GLENNON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ordinance violator (violator), individually and as a class representative, filed suit in the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) seeking the recovery of fine money paid to defendant city for violations of a void ordinance. The violator appealed an order dismissing the complaint.


OVERVIEW: After an ordinance was declared unconstitutional, the violator who had paid a fine to the city sought a refund. In reversing an order which dismissed the complaint because it was not timely filed, the court held that the case did not involve a criminal conviction, as ordinance violations were "quasi-criminal," nor was it an attempt to collaterally attack judgments based on constitutional error. The city's prosecution of its ordinance was not a criminal prosecution under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 1-2-1.1 (1975), but was an action for debt, and a void judgment could be attacked at any time. The court held that it was highly fictitious to say that one charged with violating an ordinance should later be precluded from recovering fine money paid under the void ordinance simply because he "voluntarily" paid it. On remand, the violator could ask the trial court to declare the ordinance unconstitutional as alternatively prayed in its original motion, or could attempt to use the prior judgment of unconstitutionality as collateral estoppel against the city.


OUTCOME: The court held that the violator had stated a cause of action which was not time barred, reversed the order dismissing the complaint against the city, and remanded with directions.

People v. Sanders


No. 77-170


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


61 Ill. App. 3d 566; 378 N.E.2d 275; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2875; 18 Ill. Dec. 811



June 9, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. MOSES W. HARRISON, II, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which convicted him of armed robbery after finding him competent to stand trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of robbing a golfer. He demanded a fitness hearing. Defendant was found unfit to stand trial because his intellectual abilities were significantly impaired and because he was schizophrenic. Defendant was remanded to a mental health center where he was declared not in need of hospitalization. A second hearing was held on defendant's petition for review of competency. The trial court again found defendant unfit to stand trial. He was remanded to the sheriff pending his release on bail. The defendant filed another petition for review of competency and another hearing was held. The trial court found defendant fit for trial and convicted him. The court affirmed on appeal. The court found that defendant could be made to carry the burden of proof for proving his own fitness, once he had been found unfit. The court noted that this applied only to the 1973 version of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-2-1. Defendant's argument that he had been "coached" to appear fit was patently absurd. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to conduct another fitness hearing prior to trial or before sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's armed robbery conviction.

Polyvend, Inc. v. Puckorius


No. 77-1740


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


61 Ill. App. 3d 163; 377 N.E.2d 1160; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2810; 18 Ill. Dec. 524



June 7, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractor appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), granting a motion for summary judgment filed by defendant Illinois Department of Administrative Services, in the contractor's action, which sought a declaration that the Illinois Purchasing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 132.10-1 (1977) was unconstitutional on the grounds that it deprived him of his right to due process.


OVERVIEW: The contractor was the sole bidder on the Department's contract for the manufacture of license plates. The Department rejected the contractor's bid based on the Act, which stated that no person or business entity was to be awarded a contract if that entity or person had been convicted of bribery or attempting to bribe a State officer on behalf of such entity. The Department had determined that the contractor, in his capacity as an official for a predecessor corporation, had pled guilty to a charge of robbery of a State official. The contractor sought declaratory and injunctive relief, asserting that the Act found him guilty of bribery without providing any due process such as notice of the charge or a right to review the decision. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred by granting the Department's motion for summary judgment. The court determined that although the contractor did not have a "right" to do business with the State, debarring him from any opportunity to contract with the State was a protectable interest under State and federal due process guaranties. The court concluded that the Act, by not providing some procedural safeguards, was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which granted the Department's motion for summary judgment. The court reversed the trial court's order, which denied the contractor's motion for summary judgment, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

People v. Stewart


No. 77-1390


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


61 Ill. App. 3d 111; 377 N.E.2d 1112; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2797; 18 Ill. Dec. 476



June 2, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. FRED G. SURIA, JR., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, sentence vacated and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order issued on February 14, 1977, from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which revoked his probation and sentenced him to a term of 12 to 14 years in the county jail. Previously, on September 6, 1972, defendant pleaded guilty to attempt armed robbery, and was sentenced to five years' probation when the court revoked his probation.


OVERVIEW: The trial court gave defendant credit for the time he spent on probation only prior to the date upon which credit for probation became discretionary. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8-4(c)(3), 1005-8-1(b)(4), (c)(4), which was in effect from January 1, 1973, until October 1, 1973, classified attempt armed robbery as a Class three felony for which the maximum term was three years four months to 10 years. Defendant contended that he erroneously elected sentencing pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8-4 (1971), under the mistaken belief that attempt armed robbery was a Class two felony. On appeal, the court vacated the sentence. The court ruled that fundamental fairness dictated that defendant should have been sentenced under the Unified Code of Corrections as initially enacted. Further, the court found that because the record did not establish with certainty the sentence defendant was serving at the time his probation was revoked, the court could not determine the effect of a consecutive sentence. The court ruled that in order to impose a consecutive sentence, the trial court must find that such a sentence was required to protect the public from further criminal conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order revoking probation, vacated the sentence, and remanded for resentencing.

Highcrest Management Co. v. Woodridge


No. 77-80


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


60 Ill. App. 3d 763; 377 N.E.2d 315; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2732; 18 Ill. Dec. 162



June 1, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. WILLIAM V. HOPF, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), granting a motion filed by defendant Village of Woodbridge (Illinois), to dismiss the owners' action, which sought to recover alleged overcharges for sewer service. The owners argued that the trial court erred in interpreting a village ordinance under which the charges were imposed.


OVERVIEW: The owners were managers and owners of multifamily residential structures in the village. Charges for sewer service were provided in the village ordinance, which stated that single family units were to be charged a fixed sum, whereas multi-family structures were to be charged either the fixed sum, or 75 percent of the monthly water bill, whichever was greater. The multi-unit buildings did not have individual meters. The owners argued that the ordinance showed a clear legislative intent to determine sewer fees by reference to structures as entities and not by reference to individual users within those structures. The trial court interpreted the ordinance to mean that the charge was the greater of the fixed sum multiplied by the number of individual units within the structure, or 75 percent of the water bill for the entire structure. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly interpreted the village's ordinance. The court, interpreting the village's ordinances as a whole, determined that the terms used showed a clear intent to treat multifamily structures as collections of individual units rather than single entities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which entered in favor of the village.

Health Resources Foundation v. Department of Health


Nos. 77-158, 77-348 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


61 Ill. App. 3d 335; 377 N.E.2d 1056; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2838; 18 Ill. Dec. 420



May 31, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. NATHAN M. COHEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Health (Department) sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which ordered the Department to issue a permit nunc pro tunc that would allow appellee corporation to establish a hospital and held that the Illinois Health Facilities Planning Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1151 et seq. (1975) did not apply to the corporation.


OVERVIEW: The corporation sought to obtain a permit to establish a hospital, and the circuit court entered an order reversing the Department's denial, ordering them to issue a permit nunc pro tunc. On appeal, the court upheld the order reversing the Department's denial because the refusal of the Department to apply its modified rule 1-1.4(a) to the corporation under which the corporation would have qualified for a permit was arbitrary; however, that part of the order the required the issuance of a permit nunc pro tunc was reversed because there was no omission or misprision to correct. Thus, the court also reversed that part of the judgment that held that the corporation did not fall under the Act. Also, the court held that the corporation did not need to exhaust its administrative remedies prior to filing its suit because it was attacking an administrative rule on its face. Finally, the corporation filed a motion to dismiss the Department's appeal on the grounds that the Department waived its appeal by issuing the permit the corporation sought, and the court denied that motion because the permit had only been issued under compulsion of judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the judgment of the trial court, which ordered the Department to issue a permit that would allow the corporation to establish a hospital. The court reversed that part of the judgment that ordered that the permit be issued nunc pro tunc. Thus, the court held that the Act applied to the corporation.

People v. Nicholson


No. 76-727


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


61 Ill. App. 3d 621; 377 N.E.2d 1063; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2880; 18 Ill. Dec. 427



May 31, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ROBERT COLLINS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for robbery from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) arguing that (1) the trial court committed error in instructing the jury on the lesser included offense of robbery, (2) the trial court committed error in conducting voir dire, (3) defendant was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt, and (4) error occurred by a witness' inadvertent disclosure of defendant's prior criminal record.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for robbery for a purse-snatching incident in which the victim testified that the defendant may have wielded a knife during the incident. Defendant was convicted and the court affirmed, holding that there was a question of fact concerning whether the defendant had any weapon during the commission of the crime, and therefore, there was no error in instructing the jury on the lesser included offense of robbery. Further, the court held that the trial court did not commit error in refusing to allow the defendant's counsel to conduct direct examination of prospective jurors. The Supreme Court rule, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110A, para. 234, superseded a conflicting statute that had been found unconstitutional. The court also held that the evidence was sufficient to prove defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt; the testimony of the victim was sufficient to contradict the alibi of the defendant. Finally, the court held that the inadvertent disclosure by a testifying police officer concerning the defendant's prior record was harmless because the evidence already showed that defendant was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for robbery.

Woodward v. Burnham City Hospital


No. 14668


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


60 Ill. App. 3d 285; 377 N.E.2d 290; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2648; 18 Ill. Dec. 137



May 26, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. CREED D. TUCKER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the wife of the deceased patient, individually and as the administrator of the decedent's estate, challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Champaign County (Illinois) dismissing her medical malpractice action against defendants, the hospital and various doctors, and upholding the constitutionality of the Limitations Act § 21.1, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 83, para. 22.1 (1975). The wife argued that § 21.1 constituted special legislation.


OVERVIEW: The deceased patient entered the hospital in 1965 for a right thigh muscle biopsy, which resulted in an erroneous diagnosis of the decedent's condition. The complaint alleged that as a result of defendants' acts, the patient developed steroid myopathy and suffered the amputation of both legs, and had to undergo corrective surgery for the removal of cataracts. Defendants' alleged errors were first discovered in 1976. The complaint was later amended when the patient died in 1977 allegedly due to defendants' negligence. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss pursuant to the Limitations Act § 21.1, which provided that no action for damages for injury or death against any physician or hospital could be brought more than four years after the date on which occurred the act or omission or occurrence alleged to have been the cause of such injury or death. Reversing and remanding the matter, the court found that § 21.1, which granted immunity for hospitals and physicians while denying immunity for other members of the health care profession was clearly a special privilege in violation of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had dismissed plaintiffs' medical malpractice action, and also reversed insofar as it determined that the section of the Limitations Act at issue was unconstitutional. The matter was remanded to reinstate the complaint and for further proceedings.

 

1785 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Smith


No. 14752


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


60 Ill. App. 3d 403; 376 N.E.2d 787; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2664; 17 Ill. Dec. 641



May 26, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. ALBERT G. WEBBER, III, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which convicted her of the offense of cruelty to children and sentenced her to 2 years probation. She preserved for review her contention that the information failed to properly charge her with the offense with which she was convicted. On appeal this was her sole claim of error.


OVERVIEW: The statute that described the offense of cruelty to children stated that any person who wilfully and unnecessarily exposed to the inclemency of the weather, or in any other manner injured in health or limb, any child, apprentice, or other person under his legal control, was guilty of a Class 4 felony. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 2368 (1975). Defendant claimed that the State was required to allege that the injury to the child was inflicted "unnecessarily." Affirming, the court noted that the Criminal Code made the offense of cruelty to children by means of injury a viable and definitely stated offense even if the adverb "wilfully" did not modify the verb "injure." By the terms of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 4-3(b), when no mental state was set forth in a statute defining an offense, the mental state of either intent, or knowledge, or recklessness was applicable. In defendant's case, the State elected to charge willfulness, which, by the terms of § 4-5(b), was a proper way of alleging knowledge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Cabak v. St. Charles


No. 76-379


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


61 Ill. App. 3d 57; 377 N.E.2d 548; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2788; 18 Ill. Dec. 259



May 26, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 17, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. JOHN S. PAGE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which dismissed its class action for declaratory and injunctive relief against appellee city in a case concerning the rates charged for sewage service.


OVERVIEW: Appellants initiated a class action case against the city to declare their property owner contracts with the city concerning sewage service valid and enforceable. Appellants also sought to have St. Charles, Ill., Ordinance No. 1975-M-30 and 1975-M-45 declared unconstitutional and to permanently enjoin the city from charging sewer rates in violation of their property owner contracts. Appellants sought review of the trial court judgment that granted the city's motion to dismiss. The court held that the property owner contracts were enforceable against the city and did not interfere with the city's ability to pass ordinances dealing with sewage service charges. The property owner contracts stated that appellants' sewage service charge could only be increased by the enactment of city ordinances and that the surcharge to be paid as non-resident users could only be changed when the service charges for residents had been changed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment that dismissed appellants' complaint and remanded for further proceedings.

Rasky v. Anderson


No. 77-1932


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


62 Ill. App. 3d 633; 379 N.E.2d 1; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2995; 19 Ill. Dec. 486



May 26, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Opinion Filed on Denial of Rehearing July 28, 1978, Reported at 62 Ill. App. 3d 633 at 636.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff broker appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted a motion of defendants, Illinois Department of Registration and Education and its director, to dismiss the broker's action that sought declaratory and injunctive relief following the department's decision to revoke his real estate broker's license. He also filed a petition for rehearing after the court dismissed his appeal.


OVERVIEW: The department notified the broker that it was seeking to suspend his license after it had received complaints that the broker owned and operated several buildings in violation of the city's building code. He then filed an action for a declaration that the department's regulations were unconstitutional and for a stay of any proceeding to revoke his license. The broker did not appear at a scheduled revocation hearing and his license was revoked. The trial court dismissed the broker's action based on his failure to pursue his administrative remedies. The department notified the broker of its decision to revoke his license and the broker did not appeal to the director for a rehearing as he could have. On appeal, the court held that the subsequent revocation of the broker's license by the department had rendered his action moot because the court was no longer able to render any effective relief to the broker. The court determined that the broker could have sought judicial review of the department's administrative decision, however, he failed to do so, thus, the revocation became a final, nonappealable order.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the broker's appeal and denied his petition for rehearing.

1789 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Williams


No. 77-130


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


60 Ill. App. 3d 726; 377 N.E.2d 285; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2726; 18 Ill. Dec. 132



May 25, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. FRANK W. BARBARO, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of the unlawful use of weapons within five years of conviction for a felony under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1(a)(10) (1975).


OVERVIEW: When defendant saw a police squad car, he stopped and dropped a loaded pistol. The trial court convicted defendant, a recent probationer, of the unlawful use of weapons within 5 years of conviction for a felony. Defendant raised for the first time on appeal the constitutionality of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1(a)(10) (1975). The court found that defendant's failure to raise the constitutional issue at trial did not bar its presentation on appeal because the right not to be convicted under a statute whose constitutionality was questioned was a substantial right deserving of special notice by an appellate court. The court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1(a)(10) (1975) did not contravene the right-to-arms clause of Ill. Const. art. I, § 22 (1970), but merely regulated their use and sets out numerous exceptions that, taken together, could not have been construed as a total prohibition against such use. The court found that the restrictions imposed by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-1(a)(10) (1975) were a reasonable and necessary exercise of the State's police power as provided in Ill. Const. art. I, § 22 (1970).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1790 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Department of Revenue


No. 77-315


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


60 Ill. App. 3d 886; 377 N.E.2d 202; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2753; 18 Ill. Dec. 49



May 19, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. F. EMMETT MORRISSEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state department of revenue (department) sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which ordered a refund to appellee nonhighway fuel purchasers, in their class action declaratory judgment, of the Illinois use tax and the municipal retailers' occupation tax attributable to that portion of the Federal gasoline tax refunded where fuel was consumed for off-highway use.


OVERVIEW: The department refunded only the state fuel tax when the initial purchaser filed a claim for refund of state taxes paid on gasoline bought for nonhighway use. The purchaser filed a declaratory judgment action to obtain a refund of the use and occupation taxes attributable to the refundable Federal tax for himself and all other nonhighway use purchasers in Illinois. The trial court certified the class and ordered the refund. On appeal the court reversed, holding that: 1) the class of purchasers had not remitted the tax and had no statutory right to a refund of taxes remitted by retailers; 2) the purchasers had not engaged in the appropriate procedure to challenge nonpayment of refunds, and had no statutory right to a refund; 3) the Federal gasoline tax was not a part of the retailers' selling price for the purpose of determining occupation and use tax liability; 4) off-highway gasoline users were not discriminated against; and 5) the practice of including the refundable Federal gasoline tax in the retailers' selling price while excluding the refundable Illinois motor fuel tax from the selling price for purposes of determining occupation and use tax was not discriminatory.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which ordered a refund of use and occupation taxes, and remanded the cause for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

1791 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Remsen


No. 77-125


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


60 Ill. App. 3d 266; 376 N.E.2d 726; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2644; 17 Ill. Dec. 580



May 17, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. JOHN T. BEYNON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which found defendant guilty of two counts of disorderly conduct. The trial court sentenced defendant to 60 days in the county jail with credit given for the 60 days served prior to trial, and placed defendant on probation for a period of two years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his convictions for disorderly conduct. The court found that defendant's conviction under count I had to be reversed because the Illinois Supreme Court had declared unconstitutional the statute under which defendant was convicted, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 26-1(a)(2) (1975). The court so held even though the constitutionality of the statute was raised for the first time on appeal. The court upheld defendant's conviction for disorderly conduct under count II. Defendant was not denied a fair trial by the admission of evidence of other offenses. With regard to count II, the court held that defendant was not denied a fair trial by the State's introduction of prejudicial evidence of other offenses. The court concluded that the evidence of other contacts by defendant with the complainant and his family was not unduly prejudicial and was probative to circumstantiate defendant's intent and the unreasonableness and fractious nature of defendant's conduct. Even assuming that the admission of the evidence was erroneous, such error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction under count I for disorderly conduct and the cause was remanded with directions to vacate his conviction as to count I. Defendant's conviction for disorderly conduct under count II was affirmed.

 

1792 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Lampe v. Ascher


No. 14487


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


59 Ill. App. 3d 755; 376 N.E.2d 74; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2552; 17 Ill. Dec. 181



May 11, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. JAMES T. LONDRIGAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff detainees appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which denied their motion for a temporary restraining order to compel appellee police to accept their tendered bail, on the ground that acceptance of court-approved bail by the police pursuant to § 110-9 of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110-9 (1975), was discretionary.


OVERVIEW: Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110-9 (1975), provided that police "may" accept bail if tendered by the accused. The detainees were arrested and charged with soliciting prostitution, the trial court set bound, and the police refused to accept it when tendered by the detainees. In reversing the order and remanding for further proceedings, the court held that the case was justiciable under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 57.1 (1975), because it was capable of repetition yet evading review. The court next held that the word "may," as used in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110-9, meant "shall," and that the police had no discretion to refuse the bail tendered by the detainees. The court came to this conclusion by considering the context of the use of the word "may," and by noting that permitting the police to refuse bail. Or to accept it only on written order from a judge, would render the Illinois Supreme Court powerless to set bail for misdemeanants by rule.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that denied the detainees' motion for a temporary restraining order against the police, and remanded the cause.

People v. Young


No. 76-348


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


60 Ill. App. 3d 49; 376 N.E.2d 712; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2618; 17 Ill. Dec. 566



May 11, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. JOHN A. KRAUSE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Illinois sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to quash a search warrant and to suppress evidence seized in its execution. The court also granted defendant's motion for a directed verdict of not guilty at the close of the State's case as to both counts of the indictment. Defendant had been charged with possession of heroin and possession of cannabis.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of heroin and possession of cannabis. The trial court granted defendant's motion to quash a search warrant and to suppress evidence seized in its execution. The trial court found that the search warrant was invalid because the time of issuance noted on it was subsequent to its execution. The trial court also granted defendant's motion for a directed verdict of not guilty at the close of the State's case as to both counts of the indictment. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred in declining to consider evidence of an error in noting the time of its issuance on the search warrant. It was apparent from the record that the trial court was of the impression that it could not look beyond the four corners of the warrant in order to determine if it had been issued before the search. The court further found that the trial court erred in failing to terminate the trial and in refusing to permit the State to file its notice of appeal from the order quashing the warrant and suppressing the evidence. The order of acquittal entered immediately after denying the State leave to file its notice of appeal was void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order quashing the search warrant and suppressing the evidence. The court remanded the case with directions to vacate the order granting defendant's motion for a directed verdict of acquittal. Before a trial, a hearing would be conducted to determine whether the validity of the search warrant was affected by clerical error.

People v. Johnson


No. 60740


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


60 Ill. App. 3d 183; 376 N.E.2d 381; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2634; 17 Ill. Dec. 382



May 10, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. DAVID CERDA, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted her of prostitution, a violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-14 (1975). Defendant had initially appealed and an appellate court reversed the conviction, but that decision was reversed and the matter was remanded back to the trial court for a final determination.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with prostitution for agreeing to perform an act of deviate sexual conduct for money. The complaint against her was made out by a police officer and asserted that defendant had agreed to perform an act of oral copulation. Defendant first argued that the prostitution statute was unconstitutional. She asserted that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court disagreed and held that the statute was not void for being vague or overbroad. Defendant also contended that the statute took away her constitutional rights to freedom of speech and freedom of association. The court held that there was an important and substantial governmental interest in eliminating acts of prostitution. Defendant's words were spoken to lead immediately to an illegal act and were not constitutionally protected. Finally, defendant maintained that the statute violated her right to privacy. The court concluded that the statute was a rational attempt to protect valid State interests. Defendant next argued that she was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court held that the trial court could have inferred her guilt from the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1795 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Belleville v. Morgan


Nos. 76-268, 76-269, 76-242 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


60 Ill. App. 3d 434; 376 N.E.2d 704; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2671; 17 Ill. Dec. 558



May 9, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. D. W. COSTELLO, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the judgments of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which convicted them of violating City of Belleville, Ill., Ordinance No. 61-36, an obscenity ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of violating the ordinance in cases involving the sale or offering for sale of nine different magazines. They argued that the trial court abused its discretion by refusing to allow them to take discovery as to what parts of the magazines were asserted to be obscene, that the ordinance was unconstitutional, and that the magazines were protected by the First Amendment. The court observed that Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 210(h), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110A, para. 201(h) (1975) provided that in suits for violation of municipal ordinances where the penalty was a fine only no discovery method could be used except by leave of court. Defendants never made a record of what the possible penalties were, so the court had to presume that the authorized penalty was a fine only and that Rule 201(h) applied. The ordinance was not overbroad. It was plain from the ordinance's use of the wording of Miller that the City recognized the limitations on the kinds of representations or depictions of sexual activity which obscenity laws could prohibit. Eight of the magazines were not protected by the First Amendment because the constitutional requirement of lack of serious value was satisfied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgments with respect to the sale of one magazine and otherwise affirmed the trial court's judgments.

In Interest of Ephriam


No. 77-401


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


60 Ill. App. 3d 848; 377 N.E.2d 49; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2747; 17 Ill. Dec. 859



May 9, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 15, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. THOMAS M. WALSH, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that revoked his juvenile probation after he committed the offense of unlawful possession of firearms in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 24-3.1(a)(1) (1973).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, while a minor, was placed on juvenile probation after adjudicated as a ward of the court following the commission of an armed robbery. Defendant's probation was revoked after he committed the offense of unlawful possession of a firearm. Defendant appealed from the judgment of revocation, and the court affirmed. The court held that (1) the uncorroborated, credible testimony of the security officer who identified the specific type of gun possessed by defendant was sufficient to sustain the conviction, (2) it was proper for the trial court to take judicial notice of the fact that defendant was under the age of 18 because this fact was readily verifiable from sources of indisputable accuracy, (3) the unlawful possession of firearms statute was not unconstitutional, and (4) the trial court had jurisdiction to enter a dispositional order even though defendant was not specifically adjudicated as a "ward of the court" because other language describing the same status was used.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment revoking defendant's juvenile probation after he committed the offense of unlawful possession of firearms.

 

1797 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hobbs


Nos. 77-50, 77-64, 77-65, 77-111 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


59 Ill. App. 3d 793; 375 N.E.2d 1367; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2561; 17 Ill. Dec. 83



May 8, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 6, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. JOHN W. NIELSEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the judgments of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which convicted them following jury trials of obscenity in connection with the showing of films at two adult bookstores.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of obscenity following jury trials. They contended that the searches and seizures were impermissible, that the Illinois Obscenity Statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20 (1975) was unconstitutional, that a jury instruction given over objection was improper, and that the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing them. The court concluded that it was not necessary for the trial judge to view personally the films prior to his determination of probable cause and issuance of a warrant for the films. The court held that para. 11-20 was constitutional because it adopted explanatory examples of what constituted patently offensive descriptions or representations of ultimate sexual acts. Defendants waived the jury instruction issue. Even if they had preserved it, the trial court properly instructed the jury that the State was not required to produce expert testimony concerning whether the films were obscene. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in light of defendants' exemplary records in sentencing them to 90 days in jail and fining them because the imposition of probation would have deprecated the seriousness, nature, and extent of the crimes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments.

Coles v. Department of Registration & Education


No. 77-1797


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


59 Ill. App. 3d 1046; 376 N.E.2d 269; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2604; 17 Ill. Dec. 270



May 2, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff realtor appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed an order of defendant Department of Registration and Education of the State of Illinois suspending his real estate salesman license subsequent to his conviction for two counts of the offense of "Interference with Commerce by Threats or Violence."


OVERVIEW: By this appeal, the realtor sought to vacate an order of the Department of Registration and Education of the State of Illinois and its acting director, which suspended his real estate salesman license. The order, issued after a full administrative hearing, concluded that the realtor had violated the Real Estate Brokers and Salesmen License Act, Ill. Rev.
