On appeal, the court affirmed holding that while a license suspension could be a hardship, the Real Estate Brokers and Salesmen License Act was not a penal measure, to be strictly construed against the State, but a broad statutory system, interpretation of which had to regard the State's interest in protecting the public from the effects of improper conduct by real estate salesmen.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the suspension of a real estate sales license.

 

1799 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


S & F Corp. v. Daley


No. 77-651


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


59 Ill. App. 3d 1024; 376 N.E.2d 699; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2601; 17 Ill. Dec. 553



April 28, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 24, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mayor revoked a license held by appellee licensee due to assault by the licensee's employees, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-1(1975). The licensee filed in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) on a common law writ of certiorari a request that the trial court reverse the revocation. The trial court did reverse the revocation. The mayor sought review.


OVERVIEW: The licensee was licensed to dispense food and maintain a public place of amusement. At the commission's hearing, two patrons of the licensee's business testified that a waitress brought to their table unordered drinks and told the patrons that if they did not pay, two men seated at the bar "wouldn't like it" and the two men would have "bashed their heads in." But the patrons in their earlier statement to the police did not state they were threatened with physical injury. The court held that the trial court erred by ruling that the mayor's findings were contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence. It was for the hearing commissioner, as the fact finder, to determine witnesses' credibility and weigh the evidence. The patron's testimony was not inconsistent with his statements to the police. Any inconsistency was for the hearing commissioner to have evaluated. The evidence proved assault under para. 12-1. The threat was an immediate one. The bouncers had the present ability to inflict a battery. The fact that the patrons paid for the drinks should they have feared a battery.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's ruling, which reversed the determination of the mayor to revoke the licensee's license upon a finding of assault by the licensee's employees. The court reinstated the mayor's revocation order.

 

1800 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Scott v. Police Hall of Fame, Inc.


No. 77-65


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


60 Ill. App. 3d 331; 376 N.E.2d 665; 1978 Ill. App. LEXIS 2655; 17 Ill. Dec. 519



April 26, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 7, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. NATHAN COHEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant fundraisers appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which enjoined them from future solicitations in Illinois and ordered them to pay compensatory and punitive damages in plaintiff attorney general's fraud action. Defendant charities appealed the judgment dismissing their third-party complaint against the fundraisers.


OVERVIEW: The attorney general filed suit against the charities and the professional fundraisers they hired to recovery money he alleged was solicited fraudulently through the mails and to enjoin future solicitation in Illinois. The charities were accused of spending more than the statutorily allowed maximum of contributions in expenses thus leaving too little money for charitable purposes. The trial court dismissed the action against the charities, found that the fundraisers defrauded the public, enjoined them from soliciting in Illinois, and ordered them to pay compensatory and punitive damages. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The trial court erred by construing § 9(c) of the Illinois solicitation act as requiring the application of 75 percent of total receipts for charitable purposes as the statute allows the deduction of costs shown to have been legitimately and reasonably incurred. The trial court also erred by awarding the attorney general punitive damages because he did not seek that relief in his complaint.


OUTCOME: The judgment enjoining the fundraisers from soliciting funds in Illinois and ordering them to pay compensatory damages was affirmed, and the case was remanded to determine the amount of compensatory damages. The judgment requiring the fundraisers to pay punitive damages and the judgment against one fundraiser was reversed.
